Ruling on Eating and Drinking in Prayer
States the prohibition and its legal consequence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating/drinking in prayer, explain the 'chickpea' threshold, and apply the a fortiori analogy (qiyas jaliy).

Core Idea
Eating or drinking more than a chickpea in prayer invalidates it; less is only makruh.

This passage establishes a clear legal boundary for one of the most common nullifiers of prayer. Using the Prophet's prohibition of turning away, the Hanafi school draws an a fortiori analogy: if turning is prohibited, then eating is even more inconsistent with the state of prayer. The key distinction is quantity—a chickpea's worth separates makruh from fasid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The matn states 'He should not eat nor drink.' Identify the act (eating/drinking in prayer) and the default ruling (prohibition).
The prohibition is not absolute; it carries weight based on quantity.
2
Analyze the a fortiori analogy (qiyas jaliy)
The sharh explains: since turning away (which is less severe) is prohibited, eating/drinking is prohibited with greater reason. Understand the logical structure: turning is prohibited → eating is more contradictory to prayer → more prohibited.
This is a qiyas jaliy because the illa (incompatibility with prayer) is more evident in eating.
3
Distinguish the quantity threshold
The text specifies that eating more than a chickpea's worth makes prayer fasid (invalid). Less than that is makruh but does not invalidate. Identify the threshold and its legal consequence.
The threshold applies whether the food is a solid or liquid; drinking also follows the same rule.
4
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Consider a person who accidentally eats a date (approx. chickpea size or larger). State the ruling: if deliberate, prayer is fasid and must be repeated. If less than a chickpea (e.g., a sesame seed), it is makruh but valid.
Accidental eating does not invalidate; the ruling applies to deliberate acts.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Contrast with the Shafi'i view: they hold that any deliberate eating or drinking invalidates prayer regardless of amount. Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf: under Hanafi, small amounts are forgiven; under Shafi'i, they are not.
This difference affects daily practice, e.g., swallowing a grain of salt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[256] ( ) ولا يأكل ولا يشرب [267] (86) اور نہ کھائے اور نہ پیئے۔ جب نماز میں ادھر ادھر متوجہ ہونے سے منع فرمایا ہے تو کھانا پینا بدرجہ اولی مکروہ ہو گا۔ اور چنے کی مقدار سے زیادہ کھایا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
[256] ( ) And he should not eat nor drink. [267] (86) And he should not eat and not drink. When he has been prohibited from turning around in prayer, then eating and drink are, by even greater reason, makruh. And if he eats more than the amount of a chickpea, then his prayer becomes fasid.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that eating and drinking during prayer is prohibited. The Arabic matn is brief: 'He should not eat nor drink.' The Urdu sharh explains the reasoning: since the Prophet ﷺ prohibited turning one's face away from the qibla during prayer, eating and drinking are even more repugnant. This is an a fortiori analogy (qiyas jaliy). The legal consequence depends on quantity: if one eats more than a chickpea's worth, the prayer is invalidated (fasid); if less, it is makruh but does not break the prayer. This ruling is based on the principle that actions inconsistent with prayer (like eating) nullify it if done deliberately and substantially.

Key Terms
فاسد (fasid): Invalid; a prayer that requires repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what invalidates prayer in terms of eating?
A) Any amount of food
B) Eating more than a chickpea's worth
C) Eating only during obligatory prayers
D) Eating while standing

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, eating or drinking in prayer is not automatically invalidating; the threshold of a chickpea's amount determines whether it is a makruh act or a nullifier.

Building Prayer After Involuntary Hadath: Conditions and Proofs
Ruling with conditions and reconciliation of hadiths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building prayer after an involuntary hadath, list its four conditions, and explain the reconciliation of conflicting hadiths.

Core Idea
Building prayer after hadath is permissible but not preferred; it is a concession for frequently occurring impurities.

Imagine you are in the middle of Zuhr prayer and suddenly you pass wind. You are not leading the prayer. What should you do? This lesson addresses that very scenario. The Hanafi school offers a middle ground: you may leave, perform wudu, and resume from where you left off—but only under strict conditions. We will examine the proof texts that support this ruling and how the Hanafiyya reconcile them with a seemingly contrary command from the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is experiencing an involuntary hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer for a non-imam. According to the matn, he may 'build' (bana) upon his prayer. Determine the hukm level: is it obligatory, recommended, or merely permissible?
The text says 'fal yabni' (let him build), which is an imperative. However, it is interpreted as permissibility, not obligation, because of the reconciling with another hadith.
2
List the four conditions for building
The Urdu sharh explicitly lists four conditions. Memorize them: (1) no intentional repeat of hadath, (2) no speaking, (3) no other nullifying act, (4) no excessive delay. Any violation requires restarting the prayer.
If the person turns away from the qibla for going and coming, that is excused.
3
Examine the proof from the A'isha hadith
The hadith from A'isha (Ibn Majah, Darqutni) explicitly commands building after vomiting, nosebleed, etc. Identify the operative phrase 'fal yabni' and note that it is zanni al-thubut (a hadith) and zanni al-dalala, requiring interpretation.
The hadith also includes conditions: 'as long as he does not speak'.
4
Examine the opposing proof from Ali ibn Talq hadith
The hadith from Ali ibn Talq (Abu Dawud) commands: 'let him depart and repeat the prayer.' The Shafi'i school takes this as obligatory. How does the Hanafi school reconcile?
The Hanafi response: the command to repeat is interpreted as a recommendation (afdal), not an obligation, based on the principle of jama' (reconciliation).
5
Understand the rationale behind the concession
Building is contrary to qiyas (analogy) because normally a hadath invalidates the prayer. It is a concession (rukhsah) applicable only to frequently occurring hadath (e.g., wind, nosebleed). For rare hadath like nocturnal emission, building is not allowed.
This is an application of istihsan, preferring the stronger evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[257] (87) فان سبقه الحدث انصرف وتوضأ وبنى على صلوته ان لم يكن اماما. ا کسی کو خود بخود حدث ہو گیا ہو تو واپس جا کر وضو کرے گا اور واپس آکر پہلی نماز پر بنا کرے گا۔ اگر پہلے مثلا ظہر کی دو رکعت پڑھ چکا ہے تو وضو سے واپس آکر دو رکعت اور پڑھ کر چار رکعت پوری کرے گا۔ لیکن اس کے لئے چار شرطیں ہیں (۱) اس درمیان دوبارہ جان کر حدث نہ کیا ہو (۲) بات نہ کی ہو (۳) نماز ٹوٹنے کا اور کوئی کام نہ کیا ہو (۴) اور ضرورت سے زیادہ نہ ٹھہرا ہے۔ تو بنا کر سکتا ہے۔ اور اگر ان میں سے کوئی ایک کام کر لیا تو شروع سے نماز پڑھے گا۔ اور یہ جو آیا گیا، قبلہ سے سینہ پھر ا يہ معاف ہے۔ کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے اس لئے خلاف قیاس اس کو جائز قرار دیا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ جو حدث بار بار ہوسکتا ہے اس میں بنا کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن جو حدث بھی کھبار ہوتا ہے جیسے احتلام ہوتا تو اس میں بنا نہیں کرے گا بلکہ شروع سے نماز پڑھے گا۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله الله الله من اصابه قيء او رعاف او قلس او مذى فلينصرف فليتوضأ ثم ليبن على صلوته وهو في ذلك لا يتكلم (ب) (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ما جاء فی البناء علی الصلوۃ ص اسے انمبر ۱۲۲۱ ردار قطنی ، باب فی الوضوء من الخارج من البدن کالرعاف الخ ص ۶۰ نمبر ۵۵۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بنا کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن شروع سے نماز پڑھے تو بہتر ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ مسئلہ خلاف قیاس ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن على بن طلق قال قال رسول الله الله اذا فساء احدكم في الصلوة فلينصرف فليتوضأ وليعد الصلوة (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب اذا احدث فی الصلوۃ ص ۱۵۱ نمبر ۲۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز شروع سے پڑھنی چاہئے۔ خاندان امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ حدث ہونے کی صورت میں شروع سے نماز پڑھے اور ان کی دلیل یہی ابو داؤد شریف والی حدیث ہے۔ ہمارے نزدیک دونوں احادیث جمع کرنے کے بعد ابوداؤد کی حدیث افضل ہونے پر محمول ہے۔
[257] (87) If he is overtaken by hadath, he departs, performs wudu, and builds upon his prayer, provided he is not an imam. ... If someone has a hadath involuntarily, he will go back, perform wudu, and come back to build upon his previous prayer. For example, if he has already prayed two rak'ahs of Zuhr, he will return after wudu and pray two more to complete four. But there are four conditions: (1) He did not intentionally commit another hadath in between; (2) He did not speak; (3) He did not do any other act that breaks prayer; (4) He did not delay more than necessary. Then he may build. If he does any of these, he will restart the prayer. And the fact that he turned his chest away from the qibla while going and coming is excused. Because there is a hadith, so contrary to analogy it is permitted. This is why he may build in the case of a hadath that can occur frequently. But for a hadath that occurs rarely, like nocturnal emission, he will not build but restart. From A'isha: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever is afflicted with vomiting, nosebleed, regurgitation, or madhiy should depart, perform wudu, then build upon his prayer, as long as he does not speak during that. (Ibn Majah) So we know that building is permissible. But it is better to restart because this issue is contrary to analogy. Another hadith: From Ali ibn Talq: The Messenger of Allah said: If one of you passes wind during prayer, let him depart, perform wudu, and repeat the prayer. (Abu Dawud) From this we learn that the prayer should be read from the start. The Shafi'i school says to restart from the beginning, and their proof is the Abu Dawud hadith. According to us, after reconciling both hadiths, the Abu Dawud hadith is taken as indicating preference.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a worshipper (who is not an imam) who experiences an involuntary hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer. The Arabic matn states: if he is overtaken by hadath, he leaves, performs wudu, and builds upon his prayer—provided he is not the imam. The Urdu sharh expands: he may resume from where he left off, but four conditions must be met: he does not intentionally break wudu again, does not speak, does no other nullifying act, and does not delay excessively. If any condition is violated, he must restart. The text then cites two hadiths: the first from A'isha allows building, the second from Ali ibn Talq commands repetition. The Hanafi position harmonizes them: the second is interpreted as recommending restart (afdal), while building is permissible. The Shafi'i school holds that one must restart, using the second hadith. The Hanafi response is that both are authentic, and the command to repeat is taken as preference, not obligation. The reasoning is that building is contrary to qiyas (analogy), so it is a concession limited to frequently occurring hadath; for rare hadath like nocturnal emission, building is not allowed and one must restart.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that breaks wudu, such as passing wind, urine, etc.
بنا (bana): To build upon the previous prayer, continuing from where one left off.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for building upon prayer after hadath?
A) Not speaking
B) Not performing any other nullifying act
C) The hadath being intentional
D) Not delaying excessively

Key Takeaway
Building prayer after an involuntary hadath is a Hanafi concession limited to frequent impurities and strict conditions; otherwise, one must restart.

The Imam Overtaken by Hadath: Succession and Building
Hanafi ruling on imam's procedure when hadath occurs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for an imam who experiences hadath during prayer, explain the evidence from the Prophet's illness, and apply the condition that building is not allowed if the hadath was deliberate.

Core Idea
An imam overcome by hadath may appoint a successor and build upon his prayer; restarting is more virtuous.

When an imam loses wudu during congregational prayer, what should he do? The Hanafi school provides a specific procedure: appoint a successor, perform wudu, and continue from where he left off. This ruling is derived from the practice of the Prophet during his final illness when Abu Bakr was appointed. In this lesson, we examine the textual evidence and the school's reasoning, noting that if the hadath was deliberate, building is not allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam being overtaken by hadath. The ruling is: he appoints a successor (istakhlafa), performs wudu, and builds upon his prayer, as long as he does not speak. Restarting is better (afdal).
The ruling is ja'iz (permissible), not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Aisha about the Prophet's illness when Abu Bakr was appointed to lead the prayer. The hadith is from Muslim and Bukhari.
The hadith is sahih (qati al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows the Prophet appointing Abu Bakr as imam when he himself could not lead due to illness. This establishes the principle of istikhlaf (appointing a successor) in cases of necessity.
The dalala is zanni because the hadith describes a specific event, but the principle is derived by analogy.
4
Note the condition of speaking
The building is conditional upon not speaking. If the imam speaks after the hadath before appointing a successor or after returning, the building is nullified.
Also, if the hadath was deliberate, building is not allowed and the imam must restart entirely.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi preference
The text says restarting is better (al-istinaf afdal). This indicates that while building is permissible, restarting is more cautious and recommended to avoid any doubt.
This reflects a balance between necessity and precaution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[258] (88) فان كان اماما استخلف وتوضأ وبنى على صلوته مالم يتكلم والاستيناف افضل. امام ہے تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس کو اپنا خلیفہ بنانا پڑے گا تا کہ خلیفہ مقتدیوں کو نماز پڑھائے۔ اور اصلی امام وضو کر کے نماز پر بنا کرے گا۔ خلیفہ بنانے کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے دخلت على عائشة فقلت لها الا تحدثيني عن مرض رسول الله الله ... وكان ابو بكر يصلى وهو قائم يصلوة النبى الله والناس يصلون بصلوة ابى بكر (الف) ( مسلم شریف ، باب استخلاف الامام اذا عرض له عذرص ۷۷ انمبر ۴۱۸ / بخاری شریف، باب انما جعل الامام یورتم بہ ص ۹۵ نمبر ۷ ۶۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ضرورت کے موقع پر امام خلیفہ بنائے گا۔ کیونکہ ابو بکر کی جگہ پر حضور نے نماز پڑھائی۔ جب تک بات نہ کرنے کی شرط حدیث میں گزرگئی اور اسی سے معلوم ہوا کہ جان بوجھ کر کوئی حدث کیا ہو تو بنا نہیں کرے گا۔ شروع سے نماز پڑھے گا۔
[258] (88) If he is an imam, he appoints a successor, performs wudu, and builds upon his prayer, as long as he does not speak, and restarting is better. It is obvious that the imam has to appoint a successor so that the successor leads the followers. The original imam will perform wudu and build upon his prayer. For appointing a successor, there is this hadith: I entered upon A'isha and said to her: Won't you tell me about the illness of the Messenger of Allah ... And Abu Bakr was praying standing, leading the prayer of the Prophet, and the people were praying with the prayer of Abu Bakr. (Muslim, Bukhari) From this hadith we learn that in a time of necessity the imam will appoint a successor. Because the Prophet led the prayer in place of Abu Bakr. The condition of not speaking has already passed in the hadith, and from this it is understood that if one deliberately commits a hadath, he should not build but restart from the beginning.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage addresses the specific case where the imam experiences hadath during prayer. The Arabic matn says: if he is an imam, he appoints a successor (yastakhlif), performs wudu, and builds upon his prayer, as long as he does not speak, but restarting is better (al-istinaf afdal). The Urdu sharh explains the reasoning: the imam must appoint someone to lead the congregation while he goes to perform wudu. Upon return, he builds upon his own prayer. The evidence is from the incident during the Prophet's final illness when Abu Bakr was appointed as imam. This indicates the permissibility of substituting an imam in case of an excuse. The text also notes the condition of not speaking and that intentional hadath invalidates the possibility of building, requiring a fresh start.

Key Terms
استخلف (istakhlafa): To appoint a successor to lead the prayer in one's place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the first action an imam must take when he has hadath during prayer?
A) Perform wudu immediately.
B) Appoint a successor.
C) Repeat the takbir.
D) Leave the mosque.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits an imam to appoint a successor and build upon his prayer after hadath, as established by the Prophet's sunnah, though restarting is considered more virtuous.

Ruling on Sleep, Nocturnal Emission, Insanity, Fainting, and Laughter
List of events nullifying wudu and prayer requiring full restart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five events that invalidate both wudu and prayer according to the Hanafi school, and apply the rule that building is not allowed for rare nullifiers.

Core Idea
Five rare events nullify both wudu and prayer: sleep with emission, insanity, fainting, and loud laughter.

This lesson presents a concise ruling from al-Sharh al-Sameri listing specific events that invalidate both wudu and prayer. The Hanafi school holds that for these rare occurrences, the concession of building (bina') does not apply; one must restart both wudu and prayer from the beginning. Understanding the rationale based on the frequency of the cause is essential.

Guided Path
1
List the five events
Read the Arabic text: sleep with nocturnal emission (ihtilam), insanity (junun), fainting (ighma'), and loud laughter (qahqaha). Note that sleeping alone without emission also nullifies if deep, but the text focuses on the compounded case.
These are all considered major nullifiers that terminate the state of purity and the prayer.
2
Distinguish building vs. restart
Building (bina') is a concession for frequently occurring hadath, such as nosebleeds. The commentary explicitly states these events are rare, so building is not permitted.
This is based on hadith that building is only for recurring events.
3
Apply the ruling
If any of these events occur during prayer, one must break the prayer, perform wudu (and ghusl for ihtilam), and start the prayer anew.
For sleep without emission, the ruling depends on depth of sleep; deep sleep nullifies wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[259] (89) وان نام فاحتلم او جن او اغمى عليه او قهقه استأنف الوضوء والصلوة. یہ سب امور کبھی کبھار پیش آتے ہیں اس لئے حدیث کی بنا پر اس میں بنا نہیں کرے گا۔ کیونکہ حدیث میں ان چیزوں میں بنا کرنے کا جواز ہے جو بار بار پیش آتے ہوں لغت اٹمی : بے ہوشی طاری ہوتا۔ وت سویا اور احتلام ہوا کی قید اس لئے لگائی کہ تھوڑا سویا اور احتلام ہوا تو شروع سے کرے گا اور اگر بہت سویا تو خود سونا بھی ناقض وضو ہے۔
[259] (89) And if he slept and had a nocturnal emission, or became insane, or fainted, or laughed loudly (qahqaha), he restarts the wudu and the prayer. These matters occur rarely, therefore based on hadith, one should not build in these cases. Because the hadith permits building only in cases that occur frequently. Lexically: 'أغمي عليه' means he loses consciousness. The condition of 'sleep and nocturnal emission' is specified because if he sleeps little and has emission, he will restart; but if he sleeps a lot, then sleep itself breaks wudu.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage lists events that invalidate both wudu and the current prayer, requiring full restart (isti'naf). The Arabic matn states: if one sleeps and has a nocturnal emission (ihtilam), or becomes insane (junna), or faints (ughmiya 'alayhi), or laughs loudly (qahqaha), then one must restart both wudu and prayer. The Urdu sharh explains that these are rare occurrences, and the concession of building (bina) is only for recurring hadath, not for these. The mention of sleep with emission is qualified: if he slept lightly and had emission, he must restart because the hadath is compounded. If he slept deeply, then sleep alone nullifies wudu. The rule is based on the principle that building is a concession contrary to analogy, so it is limited to cases explicitly allowed.

Key Terms
قهقه (qahqaha): Laughing loudly enough that others hear; it invalidates wudu and prayer.
احتلام (ihtilam): Nocturnal emission; requires ghusl and invalidates prayer in progress.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the events listed in the text that require full restart of wudu and prayer?
A) Sleep with nocturnal emission
B) Laughing loudly
C) Fainting
D) Sneezing

Key Takeaway
Five rare events — sleep with emission, insanity, fainting, and loud laughter — require full restart of wudu and prayer, as building is a concession only for frequent hadath.

Ruling on Speaking During Prayer
Speech invalidates prayer; evidence from Quran and Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on speaking during prayer, identify the primary evidences (Quran and Hadith), and explain why both intentional and forgetful speech invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Speaking during prayer invalidates it — whether deliberate or forgetful.

This lesson examines the ruling on speech during prayer. According to the Hanafi school, any form of human speech not part of the prayer itself makes the prayer invalid, regardless of intention. We will explore the primary evidence from the Quran and Sunnah that establishes this rule, and clarify why forgetful speech also nullifies the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Speaking during Salah. What is the hukm? The prayer becomes invalid (batil).
The text explicitly says 'batalat salatuhu'.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Quran 2:238 'wa qumoo li'llahi qanitin' and the Hadith of Zaid ibn Arqam from Muslim.
The Quranic command implies silence; the Hadith shows the prohibition of speech.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The command 'qumoo qanitin' is understood to require attentive silence. The Hadith explicitly states that speaking was allowed then forbidden, and the verse abrogated the practice.
The imperative 'wa qumoo' in Hanafi usul indicates obligation, here commanding silence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools make exceptions for forgetful speech, but the Hanafi school holds no such exception.
The mufta bihi is the strict position: any speech invalidates.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The Hanafi position that all speaking invalidates is based on the apparent meaning of the texts and is the operative ruling for fatwa.
No distinction between amdan and sahwan.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage delivers the ruling that speaking during prayer invalidates it, whether the speech is deliberate (amdan) or forgetful (sahwan). The Arabic matn is categorical. The Urdu sharh then provides the hadith of Zaid ibn Arqam: before the revelation of the verse 'Qumoo li'llahi qanitin', the Companions used to converse during prayer; after that verse, it became forbidden, and the prayer was invalidated by speech. This establishes that speaking is a major nullifier. The ruling is based on the clear command in the Quran (surah al-Baqarah, verse 238) and the Sunnah. There is no distinction between intentional and unintentional speech in terms of invalidation; both break the prayer.

Key Terms
ساهيا (sahyan): Forgetfully; unintentional speech due to negligence.

Imam's Succession When Hadath Occurs
Ruling on imam appointing successor when hadath occurs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for an imam who experiences hadath during prayer, apply the conditions for building upon the prayer, and distinguish the Hanafi view from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
An imam who breaks wudu may appoint a successor, make wudu, and continue his prayer—but starting over is more virtuous.

In congregational prayer, an imam may unexpectedly lose wudu. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling from the tradition of the Prophet (ﷺ) and clarifies the conditions and preferability of restarting. We also compare the Shafi'i school's position to understand the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the act
The ruling applies when an imam experiences hadath (ritual impurity that nullifies wudu) during salah. Determine what actions are required and what is optional.
2
State the three required actions and the condition
The imam must: (1) appoint a successor to lead the congregation, (2) perform wudu, and (3) build upon the existing prayer—but only if he has not spoken. If he speaks, he must restart.
Building upon the prayer means continuing from the point where he stopped, not starting over.
3
Note the superior option (istinaf)
Although building is permissible, restarting the prayer from the beginning is afdal (better/more virtuous). This is the preferred Hanafi practice.
The hadith used by Shafi'is is interpreted as recommending restart, not obligating it.
4
Recognize the cross-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school holds that after hadath, the imam must restart the prayer; they do not allow building upon the previous prayer. Understand the proof they cite and the Hanafi reconciliation.
The difference affects how an imam should act in the moment.
5
Examine the Hanafi proof
The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ), while ill, appointed Abu Bakr (رضي الله عنه) to lead the prayer. This shows the permissibility of appointing a successor. The Shafi'i hadith is interpreted as indicating preference, not obligation.
The Hanafi tarjih (preference) method reconciles the two hadiths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

خاندان امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ حدث ہونے کی صورت میں شروع سے نماز پڑھے اور ان کی دلیل یہی ابو داؤد شریف والی حدیث ہے۔ ہمارے نزدیک دونوں احادیث جمع کرنے کے بعد ابوداؤد کی حدیث افضل ہونے پر محمول ہے۔ [۲۵۸] (۸۸) اور اگر امام ہے تو خلیفہ بنائے گا اور وضو کرے گا اور بنا کرے گا اپنی نماز پر جب تک بات نہ کی ہو اور شروع سے نماز پڑھنا بہتر

If he is an imam, he appoints a successor, performs wudu, and builds upon his prayer as long as he did not speak, and restarting is better. The school of Imam Shafi'i says that when hadath occurs, one should pray from the beginning, and their proof is this hadith from Abu Dawud. According to us, after reconciling the two hadiths, the hadith of Abu Dawud is interpreted as indicating preference. [258] (88) And if he is an imam, he will appoint a successor, perform wudu, and build upon his prayer as long as he did not speak, and starting anew is better. It is obvious that an imam must appoint a successor so that the successor leads the followers. And the original imam will build upon his prayer after wudu. The hadith for appointing a successor is: 'I entered upon Aisha and said to her: Will you not tell me about the illness of the Messenger of Allah... And Abu Bakr was praying while standing, following the prayer of the Prophet, and the people were following the prayer of Abu Bakr.' (Muslim, Bab Istiqlal al-Imam idha 'arada lahu 'udhr, p.77 no.418 / Bukhari, Bab Innama ju'ila al-Imam li yu'tamma bihi, p.95 no.768) From this hadith it is understood that an imam will appoint a successor when necessary. Because the Prophet led the prayer in the place of Abu Bakr. The condition of not speaking has passed in the hadith, and from this it is understood that if someone intentionally causes hadath, he will not build upon [the prayer]. He will pray from the beginning.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on what an imam should do if he experiences hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer. The ruling has two aspects: first, the imam should appoint a successor to lead the congregation; second, after performing wudu, he may build upon his existing prayer (i.e., continue from where he left off) as long as he has not spoken. However, it is considered better (afdal) to restart the prayer from the beginning. The proof comes from the hadith where the Prophet, while ill, appointed Abu Bakr to lead the prayer. This indicates the permissibility of appointing a successor. The text then addresses a potential objection from the Shafi'i school, which holds that one must start the prayer anew in case of hadath. The Hanafi response reconciles the apparent conflict between hadiths by interpreting the one that commands starting anew as indicating preference, not obligation. Importantly, the permission to build upon the prayer is conditional upon not having spoken; if the imam speaks, he must restart. Also, if the hadath was intentional (as opposed to involuntary), building upon the prayer is not allowed, and he must pray from the beginning.

Key Terms
استخلف (istakhla): To appoint a successor to lead the prayer in place of the imam.
بنى (bana): To build upon; meaning to continue the prayer from where one left off after performing wudu, without restarting from the beginning.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies wudu, such as passing wind, urination, etc.
الاستيناف (al-istinaf): Starting the prayer again from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Perform wudu and then make salam without building.

Key Takeaway
An imam who breaks wudu during prayer may appoint a successor, perform wudu, and continue his prayer, but restarting from the beginning is more virtuous.

Invalidators Requiring Restart: Sleep with Wet Dream, Insanity, Fainting, and Loud Laughter
Ruling on sleep, janabah, insanity, fainting, and loud laughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five events that invalidate wudu and prayer requiring restart, and explain the condition regarding sleep and the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Uncommon events invalidate entirely; building is only for frequent occurrences.

This lesson covers several events that completely invalidate both wudu and prayer, forcing the worshiper to restart from the beginning. The underlying principle is that building upon a prayer is only permitted for events that occur frequently; the events listed here are considered rare. The passage also clarifies an important nuance about sleep: if a person sleeps lightly and has a wet dream, they must restart; but deep sleep itself nullifies wudu, as per other rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five invalidating events
List the events mentioned: sleeping with a wet dream (ihtilam), insanity (junun), fainting (ighma), and laughing loudly (qahqaha). Note that the text mentions 'sleeping and having a wet dream' as a combined event.
The fifth event is loud laughter.
2
Determine the ruling for each event
For each event, the ruling is that the person must restart both wudu and the prayer from the beginning. They cannot build upon the previous prayer (i.e., continue from where they left off).
The ruling is wajib (obligatory) based on the evidence.
3
Understand the principle of building (bina) vs. restarting
Building (bina) is only allowed for events that occur frequently (like passing wind). Since these events are uncommon, building is not permitted. The hadith indicates that one may build only for frequent occurrences.
This principle is derived from a general hadith, though not explicitly quoted in the passage.
4
Analyze the nuance regarding sleep
The text specifies 'if he sleeps and has a wet dream' – this implies light sleep where the wet dream occurs. For deep sleep without a wet dream, sleep itself nullifies wudu (as per other rulings), but the text does not address building in that scenario.
The distinction is between light sleep (with wet dream) and deep sleep; the latter is already a wudu nullifier.
5
Identify the proof (dalil)
The passage references hadith as the basis: the ruling relies on the principle that building is only for frequent events. The dalil is considered Sunnah ahad (single transmission), which is zanni al-thubut but accepted in fiqh.
No specific hadith is cited; the general understanding is used.

Speech in Prayer: Hanafi Ruling and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Hanafi ruling with inter-madhhab dispute response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on speech in prayer, identify the opposing Shafi'i and Maliki views, and explain the Hanafi response based on naskh (abrogation).

Core Idea
All speech in prayer invalidates it, even forgetful speech—because prayer requires total remembrance.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that any speech during prayer invalidates the prayer, whether intentional or forgetful. The passage presents the key proofs from hadith and then addresses the disagreement with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. Understanding the role of abrogation (naskh) is central to the Hanafi argument.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: intentional and forgetful speech both invalidate prayer. Note the key phrase: 'ساهيا او عامدا بطلت صلوته'.
The Hanafi position is absolute: no speech is permitted.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their views
Imam Shafi'i holds that forgetful speech does not invalidate. Imam Malik holds that speech for correcting the prayer does not invalidate.
Both exceptions are based on the hadith of Dhul-Yadain.
3
Examine the opponent's proof
The hadith of Dhul-Yadain, where the Prophet spoke during prayer to correct a mistake, implying permission for such speech.
This hadith is cited as evidence for a specific exception.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the permission in the hadith of Dhul-Yadain was abrogated (naskh) by later revelation—the verse 'Qumoo lillahi qaniteen' and subsequent hadiths that forbid all speech.
The abrogation is confirmed by chapters in Muslim and Tirmidhi titled 'Abrogation of Speech in Prayer'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi: any speech invalidates; Shafi'i: forgetful speech valid; Maliki: corrective speech valid. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.
This affects daily practice: a Hanafi must repeat prayer if any words are uttered, even accidentally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۶۰] (۹۰) وان تكلم في صلوته ساهيا او عامدا بطلت صلوته.
اگر نماز میں بھول کر بات کی یا جان کر بات کی تو نماز باطل ہو جائے گی۔
حدیث میں ہے عن زيد بن ارقم قال كنا نتكلم في الصلوة ، يكلم الرجل صاحبه وهو الي جنبه في الصلوة حتى نزلت وقوموا لله قانتين فامرنا بالسكوت ونهينا عن الكلام (ب) ( مسلم شریف ، باب تحريم الكلام في الصلوة و نسخ ما كان من
حاشیہ : (الف) میں حضرت عائشہ کے پاس آیا اور کہا حضور کے مرض الوفات کے سلسلے میں آپ بیان کریں گے؟ ابوبکر کھڑے ہو کر حضور کی اقتدا میں نماز پڑھ رہے تھے۔ اور لوگ ابوبکر کی اقتدا میں نماز پڑھ رہے تھے (ب) زید بن ارقم فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نماز میں بات کرتے تھے۔ آدمی نماز میں اپنے بغل والے ساتھی سے بات کرتا تھا یہاں تک کہ قو مو اللہ قاشتین آیت نازل ہوئی تو ہم کو چپ رہنے کا حکم دیا اور بات کرنے سے روک دیا گیا۔
اباحته ص ۲۰۴ نمبر ۵۳۹ را بود اؤ د شریف، باب انہی عن الكلام فی الصلوۃ ص ۱۴۴ نمبر ۹۴۹ / ترمذی شریف، باب في نسخ الکلام فی الصلوۃ ص۹۲ نمبر ۴۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں کلام کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور چونکہ نماز کی حالت نماز کو یاد کرنے کی حالت ہے اس لئے اس میں بھول کر کلام کرنا بھی نماز کو فاسد کرے گا۔ چنانچہ دوسری حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ موجود ہے عن معاوية بن حكم السلمي قال بينا انا اصلى مع رسول الله الله ... ثم قال ان هذه الصلوة لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس انما هو التسبيح والتكبير وقراءة القرآن (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم الکلام فی الصلوة ونسخ ما كان من اباحتی ص ۲۰۳ نمبر ۵۳۷ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز لوگوں کے کلام کی کچھ بھی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بھول کر بولنا بھی نماز کو فاسد کرے گا۔ فائده امام شافعی کے نزدیک بھول کر کلام کرنے سے اور امام مالک کے نزدیک اصلاح نماز کے لئے کلام کرنے سے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ ان کی دلیل ذوالیدین والی مشہور حدیث ہے۔ جو مسئلہ نمبر ۸۴ میں گزرگئی۔ اور اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اب کلام کرنا منسوخ ہو گیا جیسا کہ مسلم نے اور امام ترمذی نے خود اپنی کتاب میں شیخ الکلام اور تحریم الکلام باب باندھ کر بتایا کہ بعد میں ہر قسم کا کلام منسوخ ہو گیا۔ اس لئے اب بھول کر بھی کلام کرے گا تو چونکہ نماز یاد دلانے والی حالت ہے اس لئے وہ فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
And if he speaks in his prayer, forgetfully or intentionally, his prayer is invalid. If he speaks forgetfully or intentionally in prayer, the prayer becomes invalid. There is a hadith from Zaid ibn Arqam: 'We used to speak in prayer, a man would talk to his companion beside him in prayer until the verse "And stand before Allah devoutly" was revealed, so we were commanded to be silent and forbidden from speaking.' (Muslim, Bab Tahrim al-Kalam fi al-Salah wa Naskh ma kana min ibaha, no. 539; Abu Dawud, Bab al-Nahy 'an al-Kalam fi al-Salah, no. 949; Tirmidhi, Bab fi Naskh al-Kalam fi al-Salah, no. 405) This hadith shows that speaking in prayer is not permissible. And because the state of prayer is a state of remembering prayer, forgetful speech also invalidates prayer. Another hadith indicates this: from Mu'awiya ibn Hakam al-Sulami: 'While I was praying with the Messenger of Allah... then he said: This prayer is not suitable for any speech of people; it is only tasbih, takbir, and recitation of the Quran.' (Muslim, Bab Tahrim al-Kalam fi al-Salah wa Naskh ma kana min ibaha, no. 537) This hadith shows that prayer has no tolerance for people's speech. From this it is understood that forgetful speech also invalidates prayer. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i, forgetful speech does not invalidate prayer, and according to Imam Malik, speech for the correction of prayer does not invalidate it. Their proof is the well-known hadith of Dhul-Yadain, which passed in issue number 84. The answer to that is that speech has been abrogated. As Muslim and Imam Tirmidhi themselves have written chapters on 'Abrogation of Speech' and 'Prohibition of Speech', it shows that all types of speech were abrogated later. Therefore, now if one speaks forgetfully, since the state of prayer is a state of reminding of prayer, it becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that any speech during prayer, whether intentional or forgetful, invalidates the prayer. The primary proof is the hadith of Zaid ibn Arqam, which reports that the Companions used to speak in prayer until the verse 'Qumoo lillahi qaniteen' was revealed, commanding silence. The Hanafi argument is that the state of prayer requires total devotion and remembering Allah, so any speech is incompatible. A second hadith from Mu'awiya ibn Hakam reinforces that prayer is not a place for human speech. The passage then addresses the disagreement with Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik: Shafi'is hold that forgetful speech does not invalidate (since one is not intentionally violating), and Malikis allow speech for correcting the prayer. Their proof is the hadith of Dhul-Yadain, where the Prophet spoke during prayer to correct a mistake. The Hanafi response is that the permissibility was abrogated (naskh) by later revelation, as confirmed by the chapters in Sahih Muslim and Sunan al-Tirmidhi titled 'Abrogation of Speech in Prayer'. Thus, the Hanafi position is that all speech invalidates.

Key Terms
تكلم (takallama): To speak; utter any words intentionally or forgetfully.
ساهيا (sahiyan): Forgetfully; without remembrance of being in prayer.
عامدا ('amidan): Intentionally; with full awareness of being in prayer.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation; the later prohibition overriding the earlier permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, what is the effect of speaking forgetfully during prayer?
A) The prayer is still valid because it was unintentional.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) The prayer is valid but requires prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw).
D) The prayer is valid only if the speech was to correct the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that any speech, forgetful or intentional, invalidates prayer, based on the general prohibition and the principle of naskh abrogating earlier permissions.

Hadath After Final Sitting: Building Upon the Prayer
Explains the Hanafi ruling on building after hadath in the final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when hadath occurs after sitting for tashahhud and explain why the prayer is not invalidated.

Core Idea
If hadath occurs after the fard sitting, the prayer is valid; only wudu and salam remain.

What happens when a sudden hadath (ritual impurity) strikes after you have completed the final sitting of prayer? The Hanafi school provides a clear and practical ruling that preserves the prayer's validity. In this lesson, we unpack the ruling from the matn and its rationale, focusing on the distinction between fard (integral) and wajib (obligatory) elements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Determine the exact condition: hadath occurs after sitting for the duration of tashahhud, not before.
The key is timing relative to the final sitting.
2
State the Ruling
The person must perform wudu and then make salam. The prayer is not invalidated; it is built upon.
This is the Hanafi position (wajib: performance of wudu and salam).
3
Understand the Rationale
The final sitting (qadah) is a fard (integral). Since it was completed before hadath, the prayer's essential structure is intact. The salam is a wajib (obligatory but not integral), so it can be performed after wudu.
This hinges on the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib.
4
Apply the Rule
In practice: get up, perform wudu, return to the same prayer position (no need to repeat rak'ahs), and say salam.
No repetition of tashahhud is needed.

This passage deals with a scenario where a person experiences an involuntary hadath (ritual impurity) after having sat for the duration of tashahhud (the final sitting). The Hanafi ruling is that the prayer is not invalidated because the last fard (the sitting of tashahhud) has been completed. However, the salam (salutation) is still wajib (obligatory but not a fard). Therefore, the person should perform wudu again and then build upon the prayer by making salam. The reasoning is that the essential part of the prayer is done, so building is allowed for the remaining wajib act. The proof for this ruling is found in a hadith quoted in the next section (lesson 92).

Intentional Hadath After Tashahhud: Prayer Complete with Deficiency
Ruling with proof for intentional hadath after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person intentionally invalidates the prayer after tashahhud, and explain why the prayer is considered complete despite the omission of salam.

Core Idea
After tashahhud, intentional hadath completes the fard but leaves a wajib deficiency — the prayer is valid but sinful.

You have learned that involuntary hadath after tashahhud allows building upon the prayer. This lesson examines the intentional case. The Hanafi school holds that the prayer is not invalidated; instead it is considered complete (tammat salatuhu) because the essential fard act — sitting for tashahhud — has been performed. However, the person commits a sin by deliberately omitting the wajib salam, and building (bina) is not permitted. Let's walk through the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is intentional hadath, speech, or any action contrary to prayer after the final sitting (tashahhud). The ruling is that the prayer is 'complete' (tammat).
The Arabic term 'تمت صلوته' is key: it means the fard obligation is fulfilled, not that the prayer is perfect.
2
Distinguish the case from involuntary hadath
Involuntary hadath after tashahhud allows building (bina) on the prayer. Intentional hadath does not allow building because the person deliberately introduced a nullifier.
The previous lesson covered involuntary hadath; this lesson contrasts intentional.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar where the Prophet says that if the imam completes the prayer and sits, then has hadath before speaking, his prayer is complete.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and Darqutni; it is ahad but considered strong in transmission.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'قضى الامام الصلوة' (the imam completes the prayer) indicates that the fard is done. The sitting (قعد) marks the completion. Hadath before speaking (i.e., salam) does not revoke the completion.
The Hanafi usul principle: the command to complete the prayer is fulfilled by the fard acts; salam is only wajib.
5
Note the cross-madhhab disagreement
Other schools may consider the prayer invalid if salam is omitted intentionally. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith to hold that the prayer is valid but deficient.
This difference stems from whether salam is considered a rukn or a wajib in Hanafi usul.

اور اگر جان بوجھ کر حدث کیا اس حالت میں یا بات کی یا ایسا عمل کیا جو نماز کے منافی ہے تو اس کی نماز پوری ہوگئی۔ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد جان بوجھ کر حدث کرنے سے اس کے ذمہ کوئی فرض باقی نہیں رہا تھا صرف سلام کرنا واجب باقی رہا تھا۔ اس لئے نماز ایک حیثیت سے پوری ہوگئی تھی لیکن سلام چھوڑا اس لئے اچھا نہیں کیا تھا اور بنا اس لئے نہیں کر سکتا کہ جان بوجھ کر قاطع اور مانع لے آیا اس لئے نماز پر بنا بھی نہیں کر سکتا۔ اس لئے یہی کہا جائے گا کہ نماز پوری ہو گئی لیکن واجب کی کمی کے ساتھ (۲) نماز پوری ہونے کی دلیل حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله الله الله قال اذا قضى الامام الصلوة وقعد فاحدث قبل ان يتكلم فقد تمت صلوته ومن كان خلفه ممن اتم الصلوة (ب) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب الامام يحدث بعد یا برفع رأسه ص ۹۸ نمبر ۶۱۷ ردار قطنی ، باب من احدث قبل التسلیم فی آخر صلوتہ اواحدث قبل تسلیم الامام فقد تمت صلوته ص ۳۶۸ نمبر ۱۴۰۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تشہد کی حاشیہ : (الف) ہم حضور کے ساتھ نماز پڑھ رہے تھے پھر آپ نے فرمایا یہ نماز صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی ہے اس میں لوگوں کے کلام کی ۔ وہ صرف تسبیح ہمیر اور قرآت قرآن ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا اگر امام نماز پوری کر دے اور بیٹھ جائے پھر حدث کرے بات کرنے سے پہلے (یعنی سلام کرنے سے پہلے ) تو اس کی نماز پوری ہو گئی ۔ اور جولوگ ان کے پیچھے ہیں ان میں سے ہوں گے جنہوں نے نماز پوری کر لی ۔ یعنی ان کی بھی نماز پوری ہوگئی۔
And if he intentionally causes hadath in this state, or speaks, or performs an action contrary to prayer, his prayer is complete. And if he intentionally causes hadath in this state, or speaks, or performs an action that contradicts prayer, his prayer is complete. After sitting for the amount of tashahhud, intentionally causing hadath means no fard remains on his responsibility; only salam, which is wajib, remained. So the prayer is considered complete in one sense, but he left salam, so it is not good. He cannot build because he intentionally brought a breaker and obstacle. So it will be said that the prayer is complete but with deficiency in the wajib. The proof for the prayer being complete is the hadith: from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'When the imam completes the prayer and sits, then he has hadath before speaking, his prayer is complete, and whoever is behind him, among those who completed the prayer.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Imam yuhdithu ba'da ma yarfa'u ra'sahu, no. 617; Darqutni, Bab man ahdatha qabl al-taslim fi akhir salatihi aw ahdatha qabl taslim al-imam faqad tammat salatuhu, no. 1407) From this hadith it is understood that after tashahhud... (footnote: (a) 'We were praying with the Prophet... then he said: This prayer does not tolerate people's speech; it is only tasbih, takbir, and Quran recitation.' (b) The Prophet said: 'If the imam completes the prayer and sits, then he has hadath before speaking, his prayer is complete, and those behind him who completed the prayer [their prayer is complete].')
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a person intentionally causes hadath, speaks, or performs an action that contradicts the prayer after having sat for the tashahhud (final sitting). According to the Hanafi school, the prayer is considered complete (tammat salatuhu) because the essential fard act—the sitting of tashahhud—has been performed. However, the salam, which is wajib, has been omitted intentionally. Therefore, the person has committed a sin by leaving a wajib, but the prayer is not void; it is valid but deficient. Building upon the prayer is not permitted because the person intentionally brought a nullifier. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet says that if the imam sits for tashahhud and then has hadath before speaking (i.e., before salam), his prayer is complete. The footnote indicates that the same principle applies to the congregation. Thus, the ruling distinguishes between involuntary hadath (previous lesson) and intentional acts: involuntary allows building, intentional does not, but both result in the prayer being complete in the sense that the fard is done.

Key Terms
تعمد (ta'ammada): Intentionally; with deliberate intent.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity.
عمل عملا ينافي الصلوة ('amila 'amalan yunafi al-salah): Performed an action that contradicts the nature of prayer (e.g., eating, walking away).
تمت صلوته (tammat salatuhu): His prayer is complete; used here to mean the prayer is considered valid and the obligation of fard is fulfilled.

Hadath After Tashahhud: Valid Prayer Requires Wudu and Salam
States the ruling for unintentional hadath after sitting for tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when hadath occurs after sitting for the measure of tashahhud and explain why the prayer remains valid, applying the distinction between fard and wajib.

Core Idea
Hadath after tashahhud does not invalidate prayer; the last fard is complete.

A common concern is whether an impurity (hadath) during prayer nullifies the entire act. In this passage, the Hanafi school clarifies that if hadath occurs unintentionally after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, the prayer is valid because the last fard—sitting for tashahhud—is complete. However, since salam is wajib and not yet performed, the person must renew wudu and then say salam. This ruling highlights the crucial Hanafi distinction between fard (invalidating if omitted) and wajib (requiring compensation but not invalidating).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm level
Recognize that the passage concerns the prayer (salah) after performing tashahhud. The overall hukm is that the prayer remains valid (sahih), but the person must perform wudu and then say salam.
The prayer is not invalid; the hadath only interrupts the state of purity, not the prayer itself.
2
Locate the key terms and their definitions
Understand the terms: hadath (ritual impurity), tashahhud (the final sitting and recitation), and the phrase 'qadr al-tashahhud' (the time sufficient to recite the tashahhud).
The measure of tashahhud is a fixed duration; once that time has passed, the fard of sitting is fulfilled.
3
Distinguish fard from wajib in this context
The Hanafi school holds that sitting for the measure of tashahhud is a fard (pillar), while saying salam is a wajib (obligatory but not a pillar). Hadath after completing the fard does not invalidate the prayer; only the remaining wajib (salam) must be performed after renewing wudu.
If hadath occurred before completing the fard, the prayer would be invalid because a pillar was missed.
4
Apply the ruling to the given scenario
Given the scenario: after sitting for tashahhud, hadath occurs. The person must perform wudu (to remove the impurity) and then say salam. They do not need to repeat the entire prayer.
The person builds upon the existing prayer; they do not start over.
5
Consider the cross-madhhab difference
Note that the Shafi'i school considers salam as a fard. Therefore, in their view, hadath before salam invalidates the prayer. The Hanafi position relies on the weaker obligation (wajib) of salam.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different classifications of salam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۶۱] (۹۱) وان سبقه الحدث بعد ما قعد قدر التشهد توضأ وسلم
[۲۶۱] (۹۱) اور اگر حدث لاحق ہو گیا تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد تو وضو کرے گا اور سلام کرے گا۔ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد خود بخود حدث ہو گیا تو تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنا آخری فرض تھا جو پورا ہو گیا لیکن ابھی سلام کرنا جو واجب ہے وہ باقی ہے اس لئے اس کو دوبارہ وضو کر کے نماز پر بنا کرنا چاہئے اور سلام کرنا چاہئے۔
(91) And if hadath overtakes him after he has sat for the measure of tashahhud, he performs wudu and says salam. (91) And if hadath occurs after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, then he will perform wudu and say salam. After sitting for the measure of tashahhud, if hadath occurs unintentionally, then sitting for the measure of tashahhud was the last fard which was completed, but saying salam which is wajib still remains. Therefore, he should perform wudu again and build upon his prayer and say salam.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This is a ruling statement. The matn states that if a person experiences hadath (impurity) after sitting for the duration of tashahhud, he should perform wudu and then say salam. The commentary explains that when hadath occurs unintentionally after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, the last fard (obligatory act) of the prayer—sitting for tashahhud—has been completed. However, saying salam is wajib (obligatory) and still remains. Therefore, the person should renew his wudu and then continue his prayer from where he left off, i.e., he should say salam. He does not need to repeat the entire prayer because the fard acts are complete. This is the Hanafi position as per the text.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Minor ritual impurity that nullifies wudu (e.g., passing wind, urine, stool).
تشهد (tashahhud): The sitting and recitation of the testimony of faith in the last rak'ah of prayer.
فرض (fard): An obligatory act established by decisive evidence; omission invalidates the prayer.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act proven by speculative evidence; omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation (e.g., sajdah al-sahw).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Continue without wudu and say salam.
C) Perform wudu and then say salam.
D) Say salam and then perform wudu.

Key Takeaway
Hadath after completing the last fard (sitting for tashahhud) does not invalidate the prayer; one must perform wudu and then say salam.

Intentional Hadath or Speech After Tashahhud: Validity and Proof
Ruling for intentional hadath after tashahhud with hadith proof and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intentional hadath after tashahhud and explain the hadith proof and the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
After tashahhud, fard is complete; intentional hadath does not invalidate but missing salam is a wajib deficiency.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: what happens if a person intentionally performs an act contrary to prayer (like speaking or causing hadath) after sitting for the final tashahhud but before saying salam? The Hanafi school has a clear ruling that the prayer is valid, though deficient because the obligatory salam was missed. We will explore the textual proof from the Sunnah and the reasoning behind distinguishing fard from wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The matn states that if a person intentionally performs hadath, speaks, or does an act contrary to prayer after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, his prayer is completed (tammat salatuhu). Identify the act (intentional hadath/speech after tashahhud) and the ruling (prayer is valid but with deficiency).
The ruling applies to both imam and follower.
2
Understand the Fard vs. Wajib Distinction
After sitting for tashahhud, all fard acts (arkan) are complete. Only the wajib salam remains. Intentional hadath/speech does not invalidate because no fard is left; however, it prevents building upon the prayer (bina) and the person is sinful for missing the wajib.
This distinction is central to the Hanafi position.
3
Analyze the Hadith Proof
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar: 'When the imam has completed the prayer and sat, then he has hadath before speaking, his prayer is completed...' Note the operative phrases 'qada al-salat' and 'qa'ada' to understand that sitting for tashahhud is considered part of completion. The hadith establishes that hadath after sitting does not nullify.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and Sunan al-Darqutni; it is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
4
Evaluate the Shafi'i Objection and Hanafi Response
Imam al-Shafi'i holds salam as fard based on the hadith 'Miftah al-salat... wa tahliluha al-taslim'. The Hanafi response: that hadith indicates the key elements but does not alone establish the fardiyyah of salam; other proofs establish takbir and purification as fard. Thus, salam remains wajib in the Hanafi school.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the practical consequence is that in the Shafi'i school, hadath before salam invalidates the prayer.

Source Text

[۲۶۲) (۹۲) وان تعمد الحدث في هذه الحالة او تكلم او عمل عملا ينافي الصلوة تمت صلوته
[۲۶۲) (۹۲) اور اگر جان بوجھ کر حدث کیا اس حالت میں یا بات کی یا ایسا عمل کیا جو نماز کے منافی ہے تو اس کی نماز پوری ہوگئی۔ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد جان بوجھ کر حدث کرنے سے اس کے ذمہ کوئی فرض باقی نہیں رہا تھا صرف سلام کرنا واجب باقی رہا تھا۔ اس لئے نماز ایک حیثیت سے پوری ہوگئی تھی لیکن سلام چھوڑا اس لئے اچھا نہیں کیا تھا اور بنا اس لئے نہیں کر سکتا کہ جان بوجھ کر قاطع اور مانع لے آیا اس لئے نماز پر بنا بھی نہیں کر سکتا۔ اس لئے یہی کہا جائے گا کہ نماز پوری ہو گئی لیکن واجب کی کمی کے ساتھ (۲) نماز پوری ہونے کی دلیل حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله الله الله قال اذا قضى الامام الصلوة وقعد فاحدث قبل ان يتكلم فقد تمت صلوته ومن كان خلفه ممن اتم الصلوة (ب) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب الامام يحدث بعد يا برفع رأسه ص ۹۸ نمبر ۶۱۷ ردار قطنی ، باب من احدث قبل التسلیم فی آخر صلوتہ اواحدث قبل تسلیم الامام فقد تمت صلوته ص ۳۶۸ نمبر ۱۴۰۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد حدث کر دیا تو نماز پوری ہوگئی۔ بلکہ کوئی آدمی امام کے پیچھے ہو اور امام کے سلام کرنے سے پہلے اس نے جان بوجھ کر حدث کر دیا تو اس آدمی کی نماز پوری ہو جائے گی۔ اور چہ اس پر سلام کا واجب باقی رہا۔ حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله الله قال اذا جلس الامام في آخر ركعة ثم احدث رجل من خلفه قبل ان يسلم الامام فقد تمت صلوته (الف) (دار قطنی ، باب من احدث قبل التسلیم ص ۳۶۸ نمبر ۱۴۰۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مقتدی بھی مقدار تشہد بیٹھنے کے بعد حدث کر دے تو اس کی نماز پوری ہو جائے گی۔
فائده امام شافعی کے نزدیک سلام فرض ہے اس لئے تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد حدث کر دیا تو چونکہ فرض باقی رہ گیا اس لئے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن علی عن النبي عل الله قال مفتاح الصلوة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم (ب) ( ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء مفتاح الصلوة التطهو رص ۵ نمبر ۳ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب الامام يحدث بعد ما يرفع رأسه من آخر ركعته ص ۹۸ نمبر (۶۱۸) اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جس طرح طہارت اور تکبیر تحریمہ فرض ہیں اسی طرح ان کے یہاں سلام بھی فرض ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ طہارت اور تکبیر تحریمہ فرض ہونے کی وجہ دوسری آیتیں ہیں صرف یہ حدیث نہیں ہے
(92) And if he intentionally performs hadath in this state, or speaks, or performs an action contrary to prayer, his prayer is completed. (92) And if he intentionally performs hadath in this state, or speaks, or performs an action that contradicts prayer, then his prayer is completed. After sitting for the measure of tashahhud, if he intentionally performs hadath, no fard remains upon him; only the wajib of salam remains. Therefore, in one sense the prayer was completed, but he abandoned the salam, so he did not do well. He cannot build upon it because he intentionally brought something that cuts and prevents, so he cannot build upon the prayer. Therefore, it will be said that the prayer is completed but with a deficiency of wajib. (2) The proof that the prayer is completed is in the Hadith: from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When the imam has completed the prayer and sat, then he has hadath before speaking, his prayer is completed, and those behind him who have completed the prayer.' From this Hadith it is understood that after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, if hadath occurs, the prayer is completed. Moreover, if a man is behind the imam and intentionally commits hadath before the imam says salam, his prayer is completed, even though the wajib of salam remains. There is a Hadith: from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When the imam sits in the last rak'ah, then a man behind him commits hadath before the imam says salam, his prayer is completed.' From this Hadith it is understood that the follower also, after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, if he commits hadath, his prayer is completed. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i, salam is fard, so if hadath occurs after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, since a fard remains, the prayer becomes invalid. Their proof is the Hadith: from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The key to prayer is purification, its tahrīm is takbir, and its tahlīl is salam.' Because of this Hadith, just as purification and takbir are fard, so too salam is fard in their view. We say that purification and takbir are fard due to other verses, not solely this Hadith.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The matn states that if a person intentionally commits hadath, speaks, or does an act contrary to prayer after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, his prayer is completed. The commentary explains that after sitting for tashahhud, all fard acts are done, only the wajib of salam remains. If he intentionally causes hadath, he introduces a 'qati'' (cutting element) and a 'mani'' (preventer), so he cannot build upon the prayer (bina). Therefore, the prayer is considered valid but with deficiency of having missed the wajib salam. The proof is the hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar that if the imam completes the prayer and sits, then has hadath before speaking, his prayer is complete. This indicates that hadath after sitting does not invalidate the prayer, even if salam is not said. Another hadith confirms this for the follower. The commentary then addresses an inter-madhhab dispute: Imam Shafi'i considers salam as fard based on the hadith 'the key to prayer is purification...'. The Hanafi response is that purification and takbir are proven fard by other conclusive evidence, not solely this hadith, and the hadith is about the key elements, not that each is fard to the same degree. Thus, the Hanafi position that salam is wajib, not fard, is maintained.

Key Terms
قاطع (qati'): An act that cuts or disrupts the continuity of prayer, making it invalid if done intentionally.
مانع (mani'): A preventer that prevents building upon the prayer (bina) after an interruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person intentionally speaks after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, what is the status of his prayer?
A) Invalid and must be repeated.
B) Valid but deficient due to missing wajib salam.
C) Valid and complete with no deficiency.
D) Invalid unless he performs sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
Intentional hadath after tashahhud does not invalidate the salah because the fard is complete; the omission of salam is a wajib deficiency, not a fatal flaw.

Salah — Prayer

Mutayammim Seeing Water After Tashahhud: Hanafi vs Shafi'i and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling and disputes on mutayammim seeing water after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mutayammim sees water after tashahhud, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding taslim as fard.

Core Idea
After tashahhud, faraid are complete; the dispute hinges on whether remaining wajibat override tayammum.

This passage addresses a key practical scenario: a person performing tayammum sees water after sitting for the final tashahhud but before saying salam. Does his prayer become invalid, or is it complete? The answer reveals important principles about the completion of prayer, the status of taslim (salam), and the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib. We will explore two layers of dispute: the Hanafi-Shafi'i difference on whether taslim is fard, and the internal Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the Hanafi position (mufta bihi)
Understand the exact situation: a mutayammim sees water after sitting for the measure of tashahhud. According to the relied-upon view (Sahibayn), the prayer is complete and no repetition is needed.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn view, supported by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that taslim is fard (pillar) of prayer, so if water becomes available after tashahhud, the prayer is incomplete because a fard remains. They cite the hadith of 'Ali: 'The key to prayer is purification, its tahrīm is the takbīr, and its tahlīl is the taslīm.'
For Shafi'is, taslim is analogous to takbir in being a definitive pillar.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that the fardiyyah of purification and takbir are established by other Quranic verses, not solely by this hadith. The hadith does not prove taslim is fard; it only indicates its importance. The prayer's faraid are complete at tashahhud, as per the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud states: 'When you have said this (tashahhud), your prayer is complete.'
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that after tashahhud, three things remain: salawat, dua, and taslim. Since the prayer is still ongoing, seeing water invalidates the tayammum and thus the prayer. The Sahibayn argue that only wajibat or sunan remain, not faraid, so the prayer is complete.
Abu Hanifa's principle: if during prayer one becomes able to use the original (water) instead of the substitute (tayammum), the prayer is invalid. Sahibayn: after tashahhud, the faraid are done, so the prayer stands.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn: the prayer is complete. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the principle that the faraid are satisfied, leaving only wajibat which do not invalidate the act if omitted knowingly.
The tarjih authority here is the text itself, which implies the Sahibayn view is stronger.

فذكر مثل دعاء حديث الاعمش اذا قلت هذا هو قضيت هذا فقد قضيت صلوتک ان شئت ان تقوم فقم وان شئت ان تقعد فاقعد (الف) (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب التشہد ص ۱۴۶) اس حدیث نمبر ۹۷ میں فرمایا گیا کہ تشہد کی مقدار And if he sees water after sitting for the measure of tashahhud and then does hadath, the prayer is complete. Rather, if a person is behind an imam and before the imam's salam he intentionally does hadath, that person's prayer is complete, even though the obligation of salam remains. There is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When the imam sits in the last rak'ah, then a man behind him does hadath before the imam says salam, his prayer is complete.' (al-Daraqutni, chapter on hadath before taslim, p. 368, no. 1407) From this hadith, it is understood that if a follower does hadath after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, his prayer is complete. Benefit: According to Imam al-Shafi'i, taslim is fard; therefore, if one does hadath after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, since the fard remains, the prayer becomes corrupt. Their proof is the hadith from Ali from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The key to prayer is purification, its tahrīm is the takbīr, and its tahlīl is the taslīm.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on the key to prayer, etc.) Due to this hadith, just as purification and the opening takbīr are fard, similarly with them (Shafi'is) taslim is also fard. We say that purification and the opening takbīr are fard due to other verses, not only this hadith. (264) (94) And if water is seen after sitting for the measure of tashahhud (then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the prayer becomes invalid, and according to the two companions the prayer is complete). (1) Imam Abu Hanifa says: after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, when ability to use water occurs, although the faraid are complete, three things remain: the Salawat (blessings upon the Prophet), supplication, and taslim. So the prayer is still ongoing; therefore, during the prayer, the substitute is replaced by the original, and the original cannot be based on a weak foundation, so the prayer is invalid and must be prayed from the beginning. The two companions say: all faraid are complete; only wājib or sunnah remain. And it has passed in issue no. 92 that if one does hadath after tashahhud, the prayer is complete. So here, it is as if hadath was done after tashahhud, so the prayer is complete. (2) Besides the hadith in issue no. 92, they also deduce from this hadith: Abdullah ibn Mas'ud's hadith: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) took Abdullah's hand and taught him the tashahhud in prayer, and then mentioned similar to the supplication hadith of A'mash: 'When you have said this, or completed this, then your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, stand; if you wish to sit, sit.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on tashahhud, p. 146) In this hadith no. 97, it is said that after sitting or reciting the measure of tashahhud, the prayer is complete. Now whether one sits and recites supplications and salam, or stands up. Therefore, when water is seen after tashahhud, the prayer was already complete before that. Hence, when the mutayammim sees water after tashahhud, his prayer is complete. Rather, the principle and basis of the difference are in these eleven issues. The principle of Imam Abu Hanifa: if before salam one becomes able to use the original instead of the substitute during prayer, the prayer becomes corrupt because the prayer is still ongoing. The principle of the two companions: after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, if one becomes able to use the original instead of the substitute, since all faraid are complete, the prayer is complete with deficiency.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling when a mutayammim sees water after sitting for tashahhud. It begins with a hadith about a follower doing hadath after the imam sits, indicating that the prayer is complete after tashahhud. Then a 'benefit' contrasts the Shafi'i position that taslim is fard, so prayer would be invalid due to remaining fard. The Hanafi response counters that the proof for taslim being fard is not strong enough. The main text then presents the intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that since salawat, supplication, and taslim remain, the prayer is ongoing, thus seeing water invalidates it. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the faraid are complete, so the prayer is complete. They support this with the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud indicating that after tashahhud the prayer is complete. The passage ends with a summary of the two principles: Abu Hanifa's rule that any substitution during ongoing prayer invalidates it, and the Sahibayn's rule that after tashahhud the faraid are done.

Key Terms
تشہد (tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith while sitting in the last part of prayer.
سلام (taslim): The concluding salutation of prayer, saying 'Assalamu alaikum'.
فرض (fard): An obligatory element whose omission invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best explains why the Sahibayn hold that a mutayammim's prayer is complete after tashahhud?
A) Taslim is not fard; only wajib.
B) All faraid of prayer are fulfilled.
C) The hadith of Ali is fabricated.
D) Water must be used only before prayer begins.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that a mutayammim's prayer is valid and complete once the faraid are performed at tashahhud, even if water appears before salam.

Regaining Ability After Tashahhud: Four Scenarios
Expansion of tashahhud ruling to four analogous cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four scenarios where original ability is regained after tashahhud and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the validity of the prayer.

Core Idea
Regaining ability after tashahhud splits Hanafi scholars: Abu Hanifa invalid, Sahibayn complete.

We have already learned that if a person's wudu breaks after sitting for tashahhud, there is a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Now the author expands this principle to four additional scenarios: expiry of the wiping period over khuffs, removal of khuffs with a small action, an illiterate person learning to recite, and a naked person finding clothes. In each case, the same question arises: does the prayer remain valid or become invalid? This lesson examines each scenario and the underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common element
In all four scenarios, the person regains the ability to perform a fard obligation (complete wudu, recite, cover) after having already performed the tashahhud. This is analogous to the earlier case of wudu breaking after tashahhud.
2
Recall the earlier ruling
From the previous lesson: if wudu breaks after tashahhud, Imam Abu Hanifa says the prayer is invalid because the prayer is still ongoing until salam; the Sahibayn say it is complete because the essential parts (faraid) are finished.
3
Apply to each scenario
Expiry of mas'h period effectively breaks wudu; removal of khuffs (with a small action) also breaks wudu; learning a surah gives ability to recite; finding clothes gives ability to cover. In all, the condition changes after tashahhud.
The condition 'small action' for khuff removal ensures that the action itself does not invalidate the prayer, isolating the effect of wudu breaking.
4
State the dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds all four cases invalid; the Sahibayn hold them valid. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the Sahibayn.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if you follow Abu Hanifa, you must repeat the prayer; if you follow the Sahibayn, you do not. In fatwa, the Sahibayn's view is preferred.

Source Text

ما قعد قدر التشهد [۲۶۵ (۹۵) او كان ماسحا فانقضت مدة مسحه او خلع خفيه بعمل قليل او كان اميا فتعلم سورة او عريانا فوجد ثوبا.
موزے پر مسح کرنے والا تھا اور تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد مسح کی مدت ختم ہوگئی اور گویا کہ وضو ٹوٹ گیا یا دونوں موزے عمل قلیل سے کھل گئے ۔ کیونکہ عمل کثیر سے کھلے تو خود عمل کثیر سے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ موزہ کھلنے کی بات تو بعد کی ہے۔ اس لئے عمل قلیل سے کھلنے کی قید لگائی تا کہ یہ مسئلہ بن سکے کہ موزہ کھلنے کی وجہ سے اس کا وضو تشہد کے بعد ٹوٹ گیا۔ یا ایک آیت بھی یاد نہیں تھی کہ قرآت کی وجہ سے نماز ہو سکے۔ تشہد کے بعد اس نے تین آیتیں سیکھ لی اور اصل پر قدرت ہو گئی۔ یا ننگا تھا اور تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد اتنا کپڑا مل گیا جس سے نماز جائز ہو سکتی تھی۔ اس میں بھی اصل پر قدرت ہوگئی تو امام اعظم کے نزدیک پچھلے دلائل کی وجہ سے نماز باطل ہوگی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ان تمام صورتوں میں نماز پوری ہو جائے گی۔
Whoever sits for the measure of tashahhud, [if he was] one who wipes over khuffs and the duration of his wiping expires, or he removes his khuffs with a small action, or he was an 'ami (unable to recite) and learns a surah, or he was naked and finds a garment. The one who was wiping over khuffs: after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, the duration of wiping expired, effectively his wudu broke, or both khuffs came off with a small action. Because if they came off with a large action, the large action itself would invalidate the prayer. The removal of the khuffs is a later matter; therefore the condition of a small action is placed so that this issue arises: that the removal of the khuff caused his wudu to break after tashahhud. Or he did not even know one verse, so that prayer could be performed with recitation; after tashahhud he learned three verses and gained ability over the original (recitation). Or he was naked and after sitting for the measure of tashahhud he found enough clothing to make the prayer valid. In these cases also, ability over the original occurred. According to the Great Imam (Abu Hanifa), due to previous evidence, the prayer becomes invalid; according to the two companions, in all these cases the prayer is complete.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to four additional scenarios: (1) a person wiping over khuffs whose wiping period expires after tashahhud, (2) khuffs removed with a small action (large action would invalidate prayer regardless), (3) an 'ami (one who cannot recite) who learns three verses after tashahhud, and (4) a naked person who finds clothing after tashahhud. In each case, the original (water for wudu, ability to recite, clothing) becomes available after tashahhud. The same dispute applies: Imam Abu Hanifa says the prayer becomes invalid because the prayer is ongoing (remaining acts like salam), while the Sahibayn say the prayer is complete because the faraid are already fulfilled. The author notes that a 'small action' is specified for khuff removal to isolate the effect of removal from the effect of a large action that would independently invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms
مسح (mas'h): Wiping over leather socks (khuffs) as a substitute for washing feet in wudu.
امی (ummi): A person who cannot recite Quran or any verses of it.
عمل قلیل ('amal qalil): A small action that does not invalidate prayer by itself.

Key Takeaway
After tashahhud, regaining ability does not invalidate the prayer according to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn); Abu Hanifa's view of invalidity is not followed in fatwa.

Salah — Prayer
