Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Gaining Ability After Tashahhud
Intra-Hanafi dispute with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Imam Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) on the validity of a substitute prayer when ability to perform the original is gained after tashahhud, and apply the hadith evidence to determine the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
After tashahhud, the Sahibayn deem the prayer complete; regaining original ability does not invalidate it.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi disagreement: what happens when a person performing prayer with a valid substitute (e.g., tayammum, wiping over khuffs) suddenly becomes able to perform the original obligation after sitting for tashahhud? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differ on this point. The principle hinges on whether the prayer is considered complete after tashahhud or only after salam. This ruling has practical implications for many scenarios, including finding water, khuff expiration, learning a surah, or finding clothes.

Guided Path
1
State the common scenario
Identify the set of cases where a person uses a valid substitute (badal) for an obligation (asl) and then regains ability to perform the original after sitting for tashahhud. Examples: one in tayammum finds water, one wiping over khuffs whose duration expires, an illiterate person learns a surah, a naked person finds clothes.
All these share the same rule: gaining ability after tashahhud.
2
Identify the two opinions
State the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa (prayer becomes invalid) and the Sahibayn (prayer is complete and valid). Note that the Sahibayn consider the prayer 'sahih ma'a naqs' (valid with deficiency).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both opinions are within the school.
3
Examine the evidence for Sahibayn
Analyze the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet taught that after saying tashahhud, the prayer is complete. This is the primary dalil for the Sahibayn's position.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and considered zanni al-thubut, but it is explicit in meaning (dalala).
4
Examine the evidence for Abu Hanifa
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the prayer is not complete until salam, which is a rukn. Gaining the original before salam means the substitute is no longer valid, so the prayer becomes fasid.
Abu Hanifa relies on the principle that the prayer continues until salam.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify which view is adopted for fatwa: the Sahibayn's view, because of the clear hadith and the fact that after tashahhud all fara'id are complete. The author of the commentary supports this tarjih.
The mufta bihi is that the prayer is valid and complete without repetition.

Source Text

The Explanation of al-Thamiri, Part One, 184. The Book of Prayer. Whoever sits for the amount of tashahhud (95) or was one who wipes and the duration of his wiping expired, or his khuffs came off with a small action, or was illiterate and learned a surah, or was naked and found clothes. It cannot be, therefore the prayer becomes invalid and must be prayed from the beginning. The Sahibayn say that all obligations have been completed; only wajib or sunan remain. And it has passed in mas'alah no. 92 that if one has an event after tashahhud, the prayer is complete. So here, as if he had an event after tashahhud, therefore the prayer is complete. (2) Besides the hadith of mas'alah 92, they also use this hadith as evidence: The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Messenger of Allah took the hand of Abdullah and taught him the tashahhud in prayer. He mentioned the supplication like the hadith of al-A'mash: 'When you say this, you have completed your prayer; if you wish to stand, stand, and if you wish to sit, sit.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Tashahhud, p. 146). In this hadith (no. 97) it is said that after sitting for the amount of tashahhud, the prayer is complete. Now if he wishes, he may sit and pray, or he may stand. Therefore, if after tashahhud he gains ability to use water, the prayer of the one who performed tayammum is complete. The rule and principle and difference in the next eleven mas'alah. The rule and principle of Imam Abu Hanifa: If before the salam, in prayer, the original is gained instead of the substitute, the prayer becomes invalid because the prayer still remains. The principle of the Sahibayn: After sitting for the amount of tashahhud, if the original is gained instead of the substitute, since all obligations are complete, the prayer is complete, albeit with deficiency. [265] (95) Or he was one who wipes and the duration of his wiping expired, or both khuffs came off with a small action, or he was illiterate and learned a surah, or he was naked and found clothes. He was one who wipes and after sitting for the amount of tashahhud the duration of wiping expired, and as if his ablution broke. Or both khuffs came off with a small action. Because if they came off with a large action, the large action itself would invalidate the prayer. The matter of the khuff coming off is later. So the condition of small action is set so that this mas'alah can occur: that due to the khuff coming off, his ablution broke after tashahhud. Or he did not even know one verse such that prayer could be performed with recitation. After tashahhud he learned three verses and gained ability over the original. Or he was naked and after sitting for the amount of tashahhud he found enough clothes to make prayer valid. In these, he gained ability over the original, so according to Imam A'zam (Abu Hanifa) due to the previous evidences the prayer is invalid, and according to the Sahibayn in all these cases the prayer is complete.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the ruling when a person performing prayer with a valid excuse (e.g., tayammum, wiping over khuffs, being illiterate, or naked) gains the ability to fulfill the original obligation (e.g., finds water, khuff period expires, learns a surah, finds clothes) after having sat for the duration of tashahhud. The author explains that the fundamental difference lies in the status of the prayer after tashahhud. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer is still ongoing until the salam, so gaining the original invalidates the substitute prayer because the original obligation now can be performed. The Sahibayn consider the prayer as effectively complete after tashahhud because all obligations (fara'id) are fulfilled; remaining acts are wajib or sunan. Therefore, gaining the original after tashahhud does not invalidate the prayer; rather, it is valid with deficiency. The author supports the Sahibayn's view by citing the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet taught that after saying the tashahhud, the prayer is complete. The commentary then elaborates the specific scenarios: one wiping over khuffs whose period expires, one whose khuffs come off with a small action, an illiterate person who learns a surah, a naked person who finds clothes. In all cases, the ruling follows the same principle.

Key Terms
تشہد (tashahhud): The sitting position in which the testimony of faith is recited in the last rak'ah.
خلیفہ (khalifah): Substitute; in this context, the act performed as a valid alternative (e.g., tayammum for wudu) due to inability to perform the original.
اصل (asl): The original obligation (e.g., wudu with water, recitation, covering 'awrah) that one was unable to perform.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is complete and valid.
C) The prayer becomes invalid but does not need repetition.
D) The prayer is valid only if he does not use the water.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, after tashahhud the prayer is considered complete for the purpose of substitute-to-original transitions, making the prayer valid even if ability to perform the original is regained.

Validity of Prayer After Regaining Ability or Remembering Missed Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions regarding the validity of a prayer when a gesturing person gains ability or remembers a missed prayer after tashahhud, and explain which position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
After tashahhud, the prayer is effectively complete; later events do not invalidate it.

This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of a prayer when a person who was gesturing (mummiya) either gains the ability to bow and prostrate or remembers a missed prayer after sitting for tashahhud. Imam Abu Hanifa considered the prayer invalid because the new event breaks continuity, while the Sahibayn ruled it valid, analogizing to the case of hadath after tashahhud. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principle that after tashahhud, the essential obligations are fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the event and its timing
The event (gaining ability to bow/prostrate or remembering a missed prayer) occurs after tashahhud. The person is a mummiya (one who gestures due to inability).
The missed prayer must be less than five and the person must be sāhib al-tartīb with time scope.
2
State the two positions
Imam Abu Hanifa: the current prayer becomes invalid (bātil). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the prayer is complete and valid (sahīh).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's rationale
Abu Hanifa views the prayer as not yet fully complete; the new obligation (regaining ability or remembering a missed prayer) interrupts the flow, analogous to an external factor breaking continuity.
He considers the prayer like an ongoing act that can be disrupted.
4
Analyze Sahibayn's rationale
The Sahibayn analogize to the case of hadath (ritual impurity) after tashahhud: once the essential obligations (rukns) are done, the prayer is considered complete; any later event does not invalidate what is already complete.
After tashahhud, only the salām remains, which is a sunnah, not a rukn.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the Sahibayn's view: the prayer is valid. This is because the prayer is effectively complete after tashahhud.
Tarjih authority: Later Hanafi scholars uphold the Sahibayn's view as stronger.

Source Text

[۲۶] (۹۶) او موميا فقدر على الركوع والسجود او تذكر ان عليه صلوة قبل هذه

[۲۶۶] (۹۶) یا اشارہ کرنے والا تھا اور رکوع سجدہ پر قدرت ہوگئی یا یاد آ گئی کہ اس پر اس سے پہلے کی نماز قضا تھی۔ آدمی صاحب ترتیب تھا اور اس پر پانچ نمازوں سے کم قضا تھی اور وقت میں گنجائش بھی تھی اور تشہد کے بعد اس کو یاد آگیا کہ اس پر اس سے پہلے کی نماز قضا ہے تو گویا کہ اس کا وضوٹوٹ گیا۔ اس لئے امام اعظم کے نزدیک نماز باطل ہو جائے گی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نماز پوری ہو جائے گی۔
ان مومنیا : جو اشارہ کر کے رکوع سجدہ کرتا ہو۔
(96) Or one who gestures and is able to bow and prostrate, or remembers that he has a prayer before this one. [266] (96) Or he was one who gestures and gained ability to bow and prostrate, or he remembered that he had a missed prayer before this. The man was a person of order and had less than five missed prayers, and there was scope in the time, and after tashahhud he remembered that he had a missed prayer before this, then as if his ablution broke. Therefore, according to Imam A'zam (Abu Hanifa), the prayer becomes invalid, and according to the Sahibayn, the prayer is complete. 'Mummiya' means one who gestures in bowing and prostrating.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This is another intra-Hanafi dispute. The case is of a person who was unable to bow and prostrate normally due to illness and was gesturing (mummiya). After sitting for tashahhud, either he gains the ability to actually bow and prostrate, or he remembers a missed prayer that he must make up (if he is a person of order and has less than five missed prayers with time scope). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this remembrance or ability invalidates the current prayer because it breaks the continuity (like a hadath). According to the Sahibayn, since the prayer is effectively complete after tashahhud, the prayer remains valid. The commentary adds a definition of 'mummiya' as one who gestures in bowing and prostrating.

Key Terms
مومنیا (mummiyā): A person who gestures (e.g., with head) for bowing and prostrating due to inability to move.
صاحب ترتیب (sāhib al-tartīb): A person who maintains the order of prayers (i.e., makes up missed prayers in order). This concept applies when less than five prayers are missed.

Checkpoint

A) His prayer becomes invalid.
B) His prayer is complete and valid.

Key Takeaway
After tashahhud, the prayer is considered complete; thus, a later event like regaining ability or remembering a missed prayer does not invalidate it according to the mufta bihi (Sahibayn).

Ruling on Appointing an Illiterate Deputy After Tashahhud
Ruling on a reciting imam who appoints an illiterate deputy after becoming impure after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the later Hanafi view permits an ummi deputy after tashahhud and distinguish it from the earlier view.

Core Idea
After tashahhud, recitation is no longer required, so an ummi deputy's inability does not invalidate the prayer.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a prayer when a reciting imam becomes impure after tashahhud and appoints an illiterate (ummi) deputy. The early view held the prayer invalid because the deputy cannot recite, but later scholars led by Fakhr al-Islam argued that recitation is no longer obligatory after tashahhud, making the deputyship valid. We will unpack the reasoning and identify the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The imam knows enough Quran to lead, but after sitting for tashahhud (the minimum amount), he becomes impure and appoints an ummi as deputy.
The key detail is that the hadath occurs after tashahhud, not before.
2
State the Early Hanafi View
The initial reasoning considered the prayer invalid because the ummi cannot perform the required recitation, making the deputyship ineffective.
This view treats recitation as an ongoing requirement even after tashahhud.
3
Identify the Later View (Fakhr al-Islam)
Fakhr al-Islam states that after tashahhud, there is no need for recitation, so the ummi's inability is irrelevant; the prayer remains valid.
This view shifts the focus to the structure of salah: the obligation of qira'ah ends with tashahhud.
4
Understand the Talil (Reasoning)
The later view bases its ruling on the principle that the remaining actions (tashahhud, salawat, salam) do not require Quranic recitation. The deputy only needs to complete these actions.
The imam had already fulfilled the recitation wajib; the deputy's role is merely to continue the remaining sunan and concluding acts.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The majority of scholars, including later authorities, adopt the view that the prayer is valid. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The earlier view is not abandoned but is considered less sound for this specific scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۶٧] (۹۷) یا قاری امام نے حدث کیا اور امی کو خلیفہ بنایا۔
امام کو اتنی آیتیں یاد تھیں جس سے نماز جائز ہو سکے تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد اس کو حدث ہوا اور امی کوخلیفہ بنایا تو چونکہ امی قراکت پر قادر نہیں ہے تو گویا کہ عاجز کو خلیفہ بنایا ہے اس لئے نماز فاسد ہوگی۔
فخر الاسلام نے فرمایا کہ تشہد کے وقت قرآت کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے اس لئے امی کو خلیفہ بنانے سے کوئی فرق نہیں پڑتا۔ اس لئے اکثر کی رائے یہ ہے کہ اس وقت امی کو خلیفہ بنانے سے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔
(97) Or a reciting imam had an event and appointed an ummi as deputy. The imam knew enough verses to make prayer valid, and after sitting for the amount of tashahhud he had an event and appointed an ummi as deputy. Since the ummi is not able to recite, it is as if he appointed an incapable person as deputy, so the prayer would be invalid. Fakhr al-Islam said that at the time of tashahhud there is no need for recitation, so appointing an ummi makes no difference. Therefore, the majority opinion is that appointing an ummi as deputy at that time does not invalidate the prayer.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on an imam who knows enough Quran to lead prayer but becomes impure after sitting for tashahhud. He then appoints an ummi (someone who cannot recite Quran) as his deputy to lead the rest of the prayer. The initial reasoning suggests that since the ummi cannot recite, the prayer is invalid because the deputy is incapable of performing the required recitation. However, Fakhr al-Islam (a later Hanafi authority) argues that after tashahhud, recitation is no longer required (since the obligation of recitation ends with the tashahhud), so the ummi's inability to recite is irrelevant. Thus, the majority opinion (most scholars) is that the prayer remains valid. This shows a refinement of the earlier rule: the key point is the time of the event (after tashahhud) and the fact that recitation is no longer obligatory.

Key Terms
امی (ummī): An illiterate person who cannot recite Quran or does not know any verses.
خلیفہ (khalīfah): Deputy; here, a person who takes over as imam when the original imam becomes unable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because recitation is not required after tashahhud.
C) Because the imam's event does not invalidate the prayer.
D) Because the deputy must complete the prayer quickly.

Key Takeaway
After tashahhud, the obligation of recitation ends, so an illiterate deputy can validly lead the remainder of the prayer.

Sunrise During Fajr After Tashahhud
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sunrise during Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on sunrise during Fajr prayer after tashahhud and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
If the sun rises during Fajr prayer after tashahhud, Abu Hanifa rules the prayer invalid; the Sahibayn disagree.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a person is praying Fajr and sunrise occurs after they have sat for tashahhud. The text presents Imam Abu Hanifa’s opinion that the prayer becomes invalid, citing hadith that prohibit prayer at sunrise. However, there is an intra-Hanafi difference with the Sahibayn. Understanding this ruling requires analyzing the nature of the prohibition and its effect on an ongoing prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The text describes a person who has sat for the amount of tashahhud (the final sitting) in Fajr prayer, and then the sun rises.
The condition 'after tashahhud' is critical—it means the prayer's essential recitation is complete.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling
Imam Abu Hanifa rules the prayer invalid (fasid) because the time of sunrise is prohibited for prayer. He relies on the hadith forbidding prayer after Fajr until sunrise.
The hadith is general, but Abu Hanifa applies it to invalidate an ongoing prayer if the prohibited time begins during it.
3
Consider the Sahibayn's likely position
Although not explicitly stated in the text, based on their general principles, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) would likely rule the prayer valid. They consider the prayer complete after tashahhud, so subsequent sunrise does not invalidate it.
The Sahibayn's view prioritizes the completion of the prayer over the prohibition at that time.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the sun rises after tashahhud, Abu Hanifa requires the prayer to be repeated (qada), while the Sahibayn say it is valid and no repetition is needed.
This affects a worshiper who experiences sunrise during Fajr.
5
Note the source authority
The text presents Abu Hanifa's view as the ruling, but does not specify which is mufta bihi. Later Hanafi works may prefer the Sahibayn's view for ease, but the author seems to lean toward Abu Hanifa here.
Students should be aware of differing weights in the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۶۸) (۹۸) یا فجر کی نماز میں سورج طلوع ہو گیا۔
تفرق تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد سورج طلوع ہوا تو امام اعظم کے نزدیک نماز فاسد ہوگی۔
حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة قال نھی رسول الله الا اللهم عن صلوتين بعد الفجر حتى تطلع الشمس وبعد العصر
حتى تغرب الشمس (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب لا تخرى الصلوة قبل غروب الشمس ص ۸۳ نمبر ۵۸۸ مسلم شریف، باب الاوقات التی نھی عن الصلوة فيها ص ۲۷۵ نمبر ۸۲۵) (۲) ابو سعيد الخدري يقول سمعت رسول الله الا الله يقول لا صلوة بعد الصبح حتى ترتفع الشمس ولا صلوة بعد العصر حتى تغيب الشمس (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب لا تخرى الصلوة قبل الغروب ص ۸۲ نمبر ۵۸۶ر مسلم شریف ، باب الاوقات التي نهى عن الصلوة فيها ص ۲۷۵ نمبر ۸۲۷ ) ان دونوں احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طلوع آفتاب کے
وقت نماز نہیں پڑھنی چاہئے اس لئے اگر تشہد کے بعد آفتاب نکل گیا تو امام اعظم کی رائے ہے کہ نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
(98) Or the sun rose during the Fajr prayer. Difference: After sitting for the amount of tashahhud, the sun rose, so according to Imam A'zam (Abu Hanifa) the prayer becomes invalid. There is a hadith: Abu Huraira said, 'The Messenger of Allah forbade two prayers: after Fajr until the sun rises, and after Asr until the sun sets.' (Bukhari, Muslim). Also Abu Sa'id al-Khudri said he heard the Messenger of Allah say, 'No prayer after Fajr until the sun rises high, and no prayer after Asr until the sun sets.' (Bukhari, Muslim). From these two hadiths it is known that at the time of sunrise prayer should not be performed. Therefore, if after tashahhud the sun has risen, Imam A'zam's opinion is that the prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage deals with sunrise occurring during the Fajr prayer after the worshipper has sat for tashahhud. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the prayer becomes invalid because the time of sunrise is prohibited for prayer (makruh tahrimi) based on the hadith forbidding prayer at that time. The commentary cites two hadiths: one from Abu Huraira and one from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, both stating prohibition of prayer after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset. Note that the text says 'tashahhud ke baad' (after tashahhud), but the hadith is general. The text also mentions the Sahibayn's view? Actually the text only states Imam A'zam's opinion, implying a difference. From the earlier principle, the Sahibayn would presumably consider the prayer complete after tashahhud and thus not invalidated by sunrise. However, the text only explicitly gives Abu Hanifa's ruling. The phrase 'تفرق' might be a typo for 'اگر' (if). The passage concludes that Abu Hanifa says invalid.

Key Terms
طلوع آفتاب (tulū‘ āftāb): Sunrise; the moment when the sun begins to appear above the horizon, which is a time when prayer is prohibited.
تفرق تشہد (tafarruq tashahhud): Possibly a misprint for 'اگر تشہد' (if tashahhud); refers to the final sitting in prayer.

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that sunrise during Fajr prayer, even after tashahhud, invalidates the prayer, but the Sahibayn differ, illustrating how a single dalil can yield multiple valid interpretations within the Hanafi school.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Events After Tashahhud Invalidating Prayer
Explains six cases where Abu Hanifa rules prayer invalid, Sahibayn rule valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six cases where Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ, explain each position's legal reasoning, and identify which view is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
After tashahhud, only sunnah/wajib remain; Abu Hanifa invalidates, Sahibayn uphold the prayer as complete.

What happens if, after sitting for tashahhud in prayer, you remember a missed prayer, or the imam becomes unable to continue, or the sun rises during Fajr? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa rules the prayer invalid in such cases, while his illustrious students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), uphold the prayer as complete. This lesson unpacks six concrete scenarios where this dispute arises, traces the proofs from hadith and qiyas, and explains why the later Hanafi fatwa favors the Sahibayn's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common factor
All six cases share one critical feature: the event occurs after the tashahhud (final sitting), when the obligatory acts (fara'id) of the prayer have been completed. Only the sunnah acts of sending blessings and supplication, and the wajib salaam remain.
This temporal context is key to understanding why the Sahibayn consider the prayer complete.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his grounds
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer is still ongoing because the salaam has not yet been given. Any event that fundamentally changes the basis of the prayer—such as gaining ability after incapacity, or sunrise in Fajr—invalidates it. He relies on a cautious approach (ihtiyat) and hadith prohibiting prayer at sunrise.
His reasoning is that building the weaker (sunnah) upon the stronger (fard) or vice versa is not permissible.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their grounds
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that since the pillars of prayer are complete, the prayer is essentially done. Any event thereafter does not affect validity. They rely on hadith evidence that after tashahhud, no fard remains; the prayer is considered concluded.
They emphasize that the prohibition of prayer at sunrise applies only to new prayers, not to completing an existing one.
4
Analyze the hadith evidence
The passage cites authentic hadith from Bukhari and Muslim: the Prophet forbade prayer after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset. Abu Hanifa interprets this as applying to the ongoing Fajr prayer if sunrise occurs; the Sahibayn restrict the prohibition to initiating prayer at those times.
This difference in interpretation is a classic example of how textual umum (generality) is narrowed by context.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities, including Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and the majority of scholars, adopt the Sahibayn's view as the operative position (mufta bihi). The commentator notes that for cases explicitly mentioned in hadith, the prayer is complete; for rare unspecified events, caution may still require repetition.
Thus, in most of the six cases, the prayer is valid and need not be repeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلوة
[۲۶] (۹۶) او موميا فقدر على الركوع والسجود او تذكر ان عليه صلوة قبل هذه ۹۷۲۶۷) او احدث الامام القارئ فاستخلف اميا [۲۶۸] (۹۸) او طلعت الشمس في صلوة الفجر [ ۲۶۹ (۹۹) او دخل وقت العصر في الجمعة.

ان مومنیا : جو اشارہ کر کے رکوع سجدہ کرتا ہو۔
[۲۶۷] (۹۷) یا قاری امام نے حدث کیا اور امی کو خلیفہ بنایا۔
امام کو اتنی آیتیں یاد تھیں جس سے نماز جائز ہو سکے تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد اس کو حدث ہوا اور امی کوخلیفہ بنایا تو چونکہ امی قراکت پر قادر نہیں ہے تو گویا کہ عاجز کو خلیفہ بنایا ہے اس لئے نماز فاسد ہوگی۔

كتاب الصلوة
۲۰ (۱۰۰) او كان ماسحا على الجبيرة فسقطت عن برء [۲۷] (۱۰۱) او كانت مستحاضة فبرأت بطلت صلوتهم في قول ابي حنيفة وقال ابو یوسف و محمد تمت صلوتهم في هذا المسائل كلها.
وجه
جمعہ پڑھا رہا تھا۔ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھا تھا کہ عصر کا وقت داخل ہو گیا۔
چونکہ عصر کا وقت داخل ہونے کی وجہ سے قضا ہو گی۔ اس لئے قضا کی بنا ادا پر ہوئی۔ اس لئے امام اعظم کے نزدیک نماز فاسد ہوگی۔ [۲۷۰] (۱۰۰) یا چیچی پر مسح کرنے والا تھا وہ ٹھیک ہو کر گر گئی۔
ایک آدمی نے زخم پر پٹی باندھی تھی اور وہ اس پر مسح کر کے نماز پڑھ رہا تھا۔ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد زخم مکمل ٹھیک ہو کر پٹی گرگئی۔ چونکہ زخم ٹھیک ہو کر پٹی گری ہے اس لئے وضو ٹوٹ گیا۔ کیونکہ وہ مسح جو نقل ہے اس کے بجائے اصل پر قادر ہو گیا۔ اس لئے امام اعظم کے نزدیک نماز باطل ہوگئی۔ الجيرة : زخم پر بندھی ہوئی پٹی کھچی، بره : زخم اچھا ہونا۔ (۲۷۱) (۱۰۱) یا مستخلصہ تھی اور اچھی ہو گئی تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول میں نماز باطل ہو جائے گی۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ان تمام مسائل میں ان کی نماز پوری ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل گزرگئی ہے کہ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد کوئی فرض باقی نہیں رہا صرف درود اور دعا سنت ہیں اور سلام واجب ہے جو باقی رہیں۔ اور احادیث سے ثابت کیا جا چکا ہے کہ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد کوئی حدث پیش آئے تو اس کی نماز پوری ہو جائے گی۔ اس لئے ان بارہ مسئلوں میں سب کی نماز پوری ہو جائے گی۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر چہ سنن اور واجب ہی باقی ہیں لیکن نماز بھی بحال ہے۔ اور نماز کے دوران اصل کے بجائے خلیفہ یا خلیفہ کے بجائے اصل پیش آیا جس کی وجہ سے ماقبل پر بنا نہیں کر سکتے ۔ اس لئے نماز فاسد ہوگی۔ امام ابو حنیفہ ان مسائل میں احتیاط کی طرف گئے ہیں۔ کیونکہ ان مسائل میں اضعف کی بنا اقومی پر یا اقوی کی بنا اضعف پر ہے (۲) امام شافعی کے نزد یک سلام فرض ہے اس لئے ان کی بھی رعایت کی گئی ہے (۳) نماز کے اتمام کا حکم خلاف قیاس حدیث کی بنا پر کیا گیا ہے۔ اس لئے جو حدث بار بار پیش آتے ہیں اور حدیث میں بھی ان کی تصریح ہے تو ان کے بارے میں حکم ہوگا کہ اس پر بنا کر لیا جائے یا نماز پوری ہوگئی۔ لیکن جو مسائل بار بار پیش نہیں آتے اور حدیث میں بھی ان کی تصریح نہیں ہے ان میں احتیاط کا تقاضا ہے کہ نماز فاسد کر دی جائے اور شروع سے دوبارہ نماز پڑھے۔ اور صاحبین اس بات کی طرف گئے ہیں کہ حدیث کی بنا پر جب نماز پوری ہوگئی تو دوبارہ پڑھنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
Book of Prayer. 266 (96) Or a person who gestures (mummiya) then gains ability to bow and prostrate, or he remembers that he owes a previous prayer. 267 (97) Or the reciting imam had an event (hadath) and appointed an illiterate (ummi) as substitute. 268 (98) Or the sun rose during Fajr prayer. 269 (99) Or the time of Asr entered during Jumu'ah. Explanation: (96) He was gesturing and then gained ability for bowing and prostrating, or he remembered that he owed a previous prayer. He was a person maintaining order (sahib tartib) and owed less than five prayers, and there was ample time. After tashahhud, he remembered that he owed a previous prayer, so it was as if his ablution was invalidated. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the prayer is invalid; according to the Sahibayn, the prayer is complete. (97) Or the reciting imam had an event and appointed an illiterate as substitute. The imam knew enough verses for prayer to be valid. After sitting for the duration of tashahhud, he had an event and appointed an illiterate as substitute. Since the illiterate cannot recite, it is like appointing an incapable person, so the prayer is invalid. Fakhr al-Islam said that at the time of tashahhud, there is no need for recitation, so appointing an illiterate makes no difference. Therefore, the majority opinion is that the prayer is not invalidated by appointing an illiterate at that time. (98) Or the sun rose during Fajr prayer. After sitting for tashahhud, the sun rose. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the prayer is invalid. The hadith: Abu Huraira reported that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade two prayers: after Fajr until sunrise, and after Asr until sunset. (Bukhari, Muslim). Another hadith: Abu Sa'id al-Khudri said he heard the Messenger of Allah say: No prayer after dawn until the sun rises, and no prayer after Asr until the sun sets. From these hadiths, it is known that prayer at the time of sunrise is not allowed. Therefore, if the sun rises after tashahhud, Imam Abu Hanifa rules the prayer invalid. (99) Or the time of Asr entered during Jumu'ah. A person was leading Jumu'ah. He sat for tashahhud and then the time of Asr entered. Since the time of Asr entering would invalidate (qada), therefore qada is built upon ada, so according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the prayer is invalid. (100) Or a person was wiping over a bandage and it fell off after healing. A man had tied a bandage over a wound and was praying by wiping over it. After sitting for tashahhud, the wound completely healed and the bandage fell off. Since the wound healed and the bandage fell, the ablution is invalidated because he transferred from the substitute to the original. Therefore, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the prayer is invalid. (101) Or a woman with chronic bleeding (mustahada) recovered. Then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the prayer is invalid. The Sahibayn said that in all these cases, their prayer is complete. The evidence has passed: after sitting for tashahhud, no obligatory act remains; only the sunnah of sending blessings and supplication remain, and the salaam is obligatory which remains. And it has been established from hadith that if any event occurs after sitting for tashahhud, his prayer is complete. Therefore, in all these twelve issues, everyone's prayer is complete. Imam Abu Hanifa says: even though only sunnan and wajib remain, the prayer is still ongoing. And during prayer, instead of the original, a substitute or instead of the substitute, the original occurred, so one cannot build upon what preceded. Therefore, the prayer is invalid. Imam Abu Hanifa went towards caution in these issues because in these issues, the weaker is built upon the stronger or the stronger upon the weaker. (2) According to Imam al-Shafi'i, salaam is obligatory, so that is also taken into consideration. (3) The ruling of completing the prayer is contrary to qiyas and is based on hadith. Therefore, for events that occur frequently and are mentioned in hadith, the ruling is that one should build upon it or the prayer is complete. But for issues that do not occur frequently and are not explicitly mentioned in hadith, caution requires that the prayer be invalidated and repeated from the beginning. The Sahibayn incline that when the prayer is complete based on hadith, there is no need to repeat it.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage from al-Sharh al-Samari presents a series of six cases (numbered 96-101) where there is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) concerning whether a prayer becomes invalid due to certain events occurring after the tashahhud (the final sitting). The common pattern is that after the obligatory acts (fara'id) of prayer are completed, only the sunnah (recommended) acts and the wajib (obligatory) salaam remain. For Abu Hanifa, any event that fundamentally changes the basis of worship (like gaining ability after being excused, the imam's ability changing, or a change in time or physical condition) invalidates the prayer, requiring restart. The Sahibayn, however, hold that since the prayer's pillars are complete, it is valid and need not be repeated. The commentator provides evidence from hadith (e.g., the prohibition of prayer at sunrise) and explains the reasoning: after tashahhud, only sunan and wajib remain, so the prayer is essentially complete. Nevertheless, Abu Hanifa takes a cautious approach, fearing that building a weaker act (like sunnah) upon a stronger original (like fard) or vice versa would invalidate the prayer. The commentator notes that for frequently occurring events explicitly mentioned in hadith, the prayer is considered complete; for rare events not specified, caution dictates invalidation. This passage is an excellent example of the Hanafi methodology of balancing textual evidence (hadith) with qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference).

Key Terms
مومئ (mummiya): A person who prays by gestures (ishaarah) due to inability to bow/prostrate, but later gains ability.
أمي (ummi): A person who cannot recite the Quran at all, not even one verse.
الجيرة (al-jabirah): A bandage or splint tied over a wound, over which wiping (mash) is allowed in wudu.
مستحاضة (mustahada): A woman with chronic uterine bleeding (istihadah) that is not menstruation or lochia.
تشهد (tashahhud): The sitting and recitation of the testimony (at-tahiyyat) in the last rak'ah of prayer.
احتياط (ihtiyat): Legal caution; preferring to repeat an act to ensure validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person praying Fajr experiences sunrise after tashahhud?
A) The prayer is invalid because the sun rose.
B) The prayer is valid because the fara'id were completed before sunrise.
C) The prayer is valid only if sujud al-sahw is performed.
D) The prayer is invalid unless the person was praying as a mummiya.

Key Takeaway
After tashahhud, the prayer's pillars are complete; the mufta bihi Hanafi view is that events do not invalidate it, following the Sahibayn's position.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Prayer Invalidation After Tashahhud: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer validity after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state both Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on prayer invalidation after tashahhud, identify their proofs, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
After tashahhud, the prayer is not over—sunan and wajib remain, hence a new hadath can invalidate it.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: What happens if, after sitting for tashahhud, a person's bandage falls off due to healing or a mustahadah becomes clean? Does the prayer remain valid? Abu Hanifa says it becomes invalid, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it is complete. The disagreement hinges on whether the prayer is still considered 'in progress' after the core obligations are fulfilled and how to weigh caution (ihtiyat) against the general permission from hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify the ruling Abu Hanifa gives for both scenarios: the prayer becomes invalid. Understand his reasoning: the occurrence of hadath (breaking wudu) and the change from substitute (wiping) to original (washing) disrupt the prayer's continuity.
2
Identify the opposing position (Sahibayn)
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the prayer is complete and valid. Their proof: a hadith indicates that after sitting for tashahhud, no fard remains, so events after that do not invalidate.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Sahibayn's dalil: they rely on a hadith that the prayer is complete after tashahhud. They argue that only sunan and the wajib salām remain, and these do not require a new state of purity.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa responds that even though fard is done, the prayer is still ongoing because sunan and wajib are yet to be performed. The occurrence of hadath nullifies purity, and the shift from substitute to original (or vice versa) makes it impossible to build upon the earlier part of the prayer. He prioritizes caution (ihtiyat).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Abu Hanifa, the person must repeat the entire prayer. According to the Sahibayn, the prayer is accepted and no repetition is required. This affects whether the worshipper has an additional obligation.
The mufta bihi in the school is often the Sahibayn's view due to the hadith evidence and ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Or if he was wiping over a bandage and it fell off due to healing [27] (101) or if she was a mustahadah and she became clean, then their prayer becomes invalid according to the statement of Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: their prayer is complete in all these cases. Explanation: He was leading Friday prayer. He sat for the duration of tashahhud when the time of Asr entered. Since the time of Asr entered, it becomes qada' (missed). Therefore, the qada' was built upon the performance, so according to Imam Azam, the prayer becomes invalid. (100) Or one who was wiping over a bandage, it healed and fell off. A man had tied a bandage over a wound and was praying while wiping over it. After sitting for the duration of tashahhud, the wound completely healed and the bandage fell. Since the wound healed and the bandage fell, the wudu broke. Because the wiping was a substitute, and he became capable of the original. So according to Imam Azam, the prayer became invalid. Al-jabirah: a bandage tied over a wound; bur'u: healing of the wound. (271) (101) Or she was a mustahadah and became well. According to Abu Hanifa's statement, the prayer becomes invalid. And the Sahibayn said: in all these cases, their prayer is complete. And it has been proven from hadith that if an event occurs after sitting for the duration of tashahhud, his prayer will be complete. Therefore, in all these twelve cases, the prayer of everyone will be complete. And Imam Abu Hanifa says: even though the sunan and wajib remain, but the prayer is still valid. And during the prayer, the substitute came instead of the original, or the original came instead of the substitute, so one cannot build upon what preceded. Therefore, the prayer is invalid. Imam Abu Hanifa went towards caution in these cases. Because in these cases, the building of the weaker upon the stronger or the stronger upon the weaker (occurs). So for events that occur repeatedly and are explicitly mentioned in hadith, the ruling is that this is built upon or the prayer is complete. But for cases that do not occur repeatedly and are not explicitly mentioned in hadith, caution requires that the prayer be invalidated and performed again from the beginning. And the Sahibayn went towards the view that since the prayer is completed based on hadith, there is no need to repeat it.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of prayer when a specific event occurs after the tashahhud. The two cases are: (1) a person who was wiping over a bandage (jabirah) and the wound heals causing the bandage to fall off, and (2) a mustahadah (woman with chronic uterine bleeding) who becomes clean. The core question: Does the prayer remain valid if these events happen after sitting for the tashahhud (the sitting for the final testimony)? According to Abu Hanifa, in both cases the prayer becomes invalid. His reasoning: After the tashahhud, although no fard (obligatory act) remains, there are still sunan (recommended acts) and the wajib (obligatory) salutation (salam). The occurrence of a fresh impurity (hadath) after tashahhud breaks wudu, and since he was doing the prayer using a substitute (wiping over bandage) and then became capable of the original (washing), or the substitute ceased, the continuity of the prayer is disrupted. He emphasizes caution, preferring to invalidate the prayer to avoid any defect. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the prayer is complete and valid. They argue that once a person has sat for the tashahhud, the main obligation of prayer is fulfilled; only sunan and the wajib salam remain. They cite a hadith that if an event occurs after tashahhud, the prayer is still valid. They extend this principle to all similar cases, even those not explicitly mentioned in hadith, because the rationale (that the prayer's core is complete) applies generally. The text further explains that the ruling of completion is contrary to qiyas but upheld due to hadith. For recurring events mentioned in hadith, the ruling is based on that. For rare events not mentioned, Abu Hanifa prefers caution (ihtiyat) by invalidating the prayer, while the Sahibayn maintain the general principle. This dispute shows the tension between strict analogy (qiyas) and exceptional permission (rukhsah) based on hadith, and how each Hanafi authority balances these.

Key Terms
الجبيرة (al-jabirah): A bandage or splint tied over a wound, allowing wiping (mash) instead of washing in wudu.
مستحاضة (mustahadah): A woman who experiences chronic uterine bleeding (istihadah) outside the menstrual and postnatal bleeding periods.
تشهد (tashahhud): The sitting position in prayer during which the testimony of faith (al-tahiyyat) is recited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a mustahadah becomes clean after sitting for tashahhud, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because her wudu changed.
B) The prayer is complete and valid because tashahhud marks the end of fard.
C) The prayer is invalid only if she had not performed wudu before.
D) The prayer is valid only if she had intended to remain a mustahadah.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, after sitting for tashahhud, the prayer is considered complete by the Sahibayn, so events like a bandage falling or a mustahadah recovering do not invalidate it, though Abu Hanifa held a more cautious view.

The Obligation to Make Up Missed Prayers
Opening of the chapter on qada' with ruling and evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up missed obligatory prayers and identify the primary evidence from the hadith and Quran.

Core Idea
A missed obligatory prayer must be prayed when remembered; no other expiation suffices.

This lesson introduces the foundational ruling that any missed obligatory prayer (fard) must be made up (qada'). The passage from Sharh al-Sameri defines key terms, establishes the obligation firmly, and provides the primary textual evidence from the hadith of Anas ibn Malik and the verse of Surah Ta-Ha. Understanding this obligation is essential for every Muslim, as it is a unanimous ruling across all schools and a direct application of the Prophet's command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text discusses 'qada' al-fawa'it' – making up missed prayers. The ruling is clearly stated: it is fard (obligatory) to perform a missed obligatory prayer.
The word 'fard' appears explicitly in the Arabic text.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites two proofs: a hadith from Anas ibn Malik (Marfu') and a Quranic verse (20:14). The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sunan Abi Dawud.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) but its meaning is definitive.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof indicates the ruling)
In the hadith, the imperative 'فليصل' (let him pray) indicates obligation (wujub) per Hanafi usul. The phrase 'لا كفارة لها إلا ذلك' emphasizes that the only remedy is the prayer itself, reinforcing obligation.
The Quranic verse 'أقم الصلاة لذكري' is used as further proof, linking remembrance to prayer.
4
Note any ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
There is no significant difference among the Hanafi school or the broader Sunni consensus on the obligation of qada'. The ruling is unanimous.
The consensus strengthens the authority of the ruling.

Chapter on Making Up Missed Prayers
Necessary Note: The missed prayers (al-fawa'it) are called fawa'it, and performing them is called qada'. Making up a prayer is an obligation (fard). Because performing the prayer on time was an obligation; when one could not perform it on time, now performing it as qada' becomes obligatory. Its proof is this hadith: 'From Anas ibn Malik from the Prophet (peace be upon him): He said: Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray it when he remembers; there is no expiation for it except that.' And recite the prayer for My remembrance [Quran 20:14]. (Bukhari, Chapter on Whoever Forgets a Prayer, Let Him Pray When He Remembers, p.84 no.597; Abu Dawud, Chapter on Whoever Sleeps Through a Prayer or Forgets It, p.70 no.435). From this hadith and verse, it is understood that performing a missed prayer is obligatory.
Footnote (a): The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Whoever forgets a prayer, then he must pray when he remembers; there is no expiation for it except this. Then the narrator recited as evidence the verse 'and establish prayer for My remembrance.'
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on making up missed prayers (qada' al-fawa'it). It first defines key terms: 'fawa'it' (singular fa'itah) refers to prayers that have been missed or left out, and 'qada'' is the act of performing them after their prescribed time. The ruling is unequivocal: making up a missed obligatory prayer is fard (obligatory). The reason given is that the original obligation was to perform the prayer within its time; if that is not done, the obligation remains and must be fulfilled later. The evidence cited is the well-known hadith narrated by Anas ibn Malik: the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded that whoever forgets a prayer should pray it when he remembers, and that no expiation (kafarah) can substitute for that; the only remedy is to pray it. The narrator of the hadith (presumably Anas or another) then recited the Quranic verse 'and establish prayer for My remembrance' (Surah Ta-Ha, 20:14) as further proof. The hadith is reported in both Sahih al-Bukhari and Sunan Abi Dawud. This establishes the obligation of qada' for any missed obligatory prayer, whether due to forgetfulness or sleep (as indicated in Abu Dawud's chapter heading), and by extension, for any deliberate miss (though the sin of deliberate omission is greater). The footnote explains the hadith more clearly.

Key Terms
قضاء الفوائت (qada' al-fawa'it): Performing a missed obligatory prayer after its prescribed time has elapsed.
فوائت (fawa'it): Plural of fa'itah: prayers that have been missed or omitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is recommended but not obligatory.
B) It is obligatory (fard) to make up a missed prayer.
C) It is only required if one forgets, not if one sleeps.
D) One must give charity instead of making up the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to make up a missed fard prayer is established by the Prophet's command and the Quranic verse; it applies regardless of the reason for missing.

Immediate Qada' and the Makruh Time Exception
Expansion of the ruling on immediate qada' with the exception of makruh times.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on qada' of missed prayers and identify the condition of avoiding makruh times.

Core Idea
A missed fard prayer must be performed immediately upon remembrance, but never during a disliked time.

This passage expands on the foundational rule that a missed fard prayer must be made up. While the obligation is urgent, the Hanafi school also considers the prohibition of performing any prayer during certain disliked times. Here, the commentator clarifies that qada' is obligatory immediately upon remembrance, but with the important condition that it cannot be performed during a makruh time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
What does the author say must be done when a prayer is missed? Read the first sentence.
The ruling is: qada' is fard.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
Which hadith is cited to support immediate performance? Find the citation.
The hadith from Bukhari: 'فليصل اذا ذكر'.
3
Analyze the implication of the hadith
How does the hadith indicate immediacy? Consider the imperative and the second part.
The imperative 'فليصل' and 'لا كفارة لها الا ذلك' show that prayer must be done immediately with no other expiation.
4
Identify the exception
What condition is added to the ruling? Look for the phrase 'بشرطیکہ'.
The condition: not during a makruh time.
5
Note the future reference
Where will the details of makruh times be discussed?
The commentary says 'اس کی تفصیل آگے آئے گی' – detail will come later.

[272] (1) Whoever misses a prayer should make it up when he remembers. The prayer was an obligation (fard); he left it, so making it up becomes obligatory. Commentary
This section expands on the first ruling of the chapter, number 272. It restates the obligation: whoever misses a prayer must make it up when they remember. The commentary emphasizes that the obligation is urgent (fard); one should not delay unnecessarily. The immediate performance is derived from the same hadith cited earlier from Bukhari: 'let him pray when he remembers,' which implies promptness. However, there is an important exception: if the time at which one remembers is a 'makruh time' (disliked time for prayer, such as at sunrise, noon when the sun is at its zenith, or at sunset), then performing the qada' prayer at that time is not permissible. The commentary notes that the detailed list of such times will be explained later in the book. So the ruling is clear: qada' is obligatory and should be done immediately upon remembering, but not at any time—it must be avoided during the three disliked times.

Key Terms
قضا (qada'): Performing a prayer after its prescribed time has passed due to having been missed.
وقت مکروہ (waqt makruh): A time during which it is disliked (makruh) to perform prayer, including qada' prayers.

Precedence of Missed Prayer over Current Prayer
Ruling on whether a missed prayer takes precedence over the current time's prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which tartib (order) between missed and current prayer becomes wajib in the Hanafi school, and apply the exception when the current prayer would be missed.

Core Idea
Missed prayer comes first unless it would cause the current prayer also to be missed.

This lesson addresses an important practical issue: when you have a missed prayer to make up (qada) and the time for the current obligatory prayer has entered, which should you pray first? The Hanafi school generally requires that the missed prayer be performed first (tartib), but only under three specific conditions. If those conditions are not met, you may pray the current prayer first. Understanding these conditions ensures you do not inadvertently cause a current prayer to become missed while making up past ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
The general rule is that a missed prayer should be prayed before the current prayer.
This is based on the principle that the missed prayer becomes immediately due upon remembrance.
2
Identify the exception
If performing the missed prayer would cause the current prayer to be missed, then the current prayer takes precedence.
This is to avoid missing two prayers.
3
List the three conditions for tartib
Tartib is wajib only when: (a) enough time, (b) awareness of the missed prayer, (c) missed prayers are five or fewer (i.e., less than six).
The condition of six is specific to the Hanafi school; some earlier views said three.
4
Understand the evidence
The hadith 'pray when you remember' and the specific hadith from Ibn Umar indicate the order of priority.
The evidence is ahad, so the ruling is wajib, not fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۷۳] (۲) اور فائنہ نماز کو مقدم کرے وقت یہ نماز پر، مگر یہ کہ وقتیہ نماز فوت ہونے کا خوف ہو تو مقدم کی جائے گی وقتیہ نماز کو فائتہ نماز پر پھر فائنہ نماز کی قضا کی جائے گی۔ تشر تین شرطیں پائی جائیں تو فائنہ نماز وقتیہ سے پہلے پڑھی جائے گی (۱) وقت میں اتنی گنجائش ہو کہ فائتہ اور وقتیہ دونوں پڑھ سلکیں کیونکہ دونوں نمازیں پڑھنے کی گنجائش نہ ہو اور فاستہ پڑھنے لگ جائے گا تو وقتیہ بھی فوت ہو جائے گی تو فائدہ کیا ہوا (۲) یاد ہو کہ مجھے پر فائتہ نماز ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر فاستہ نماز یاد نہ ہو اور وقتیہ پڑھ لی تو ترتیب ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ یاد نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ مجبور ہے (۳) چھ نمازوں سے زیادہ قضا نہ ہوں۔ کیونکہ چھ نمازوں سے زیادہ قضا ہو تو ان چھ نمازوں کو قضا کرتے کرتے ہی وقت یہ نماز فوت ہو جائے گی۔ اور وقتیه پڑھنے کا وقت نکل جائے گا۔ اس لئے یہ تین شرطیں ہوں تو فائتہ اور وقتیہ کے درمیان ترتیب واجب ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ (۱) اوپر کی حدیث بخاری کے الفاظ ' فليصل اذا ذکر سے معلوم ہوا کہ فائتہ کا وقت یاد آتے ہی قضا واجب ہوا ۔ اور وقتیہ کا وقت اس کے بعد ہو گا۔ اس لئے پہلے فائتہ ادا کی جائے گی بعد میں وقتیہ ۔ حدیث کی اس تاکید سے ترتیب واجب ہوتی ہے (۲) عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله الله قال من نسى صلوة فلم يذكرها الا وهو مع الامام فليصل مع الامام فاذا فرغ من صلوته فليعد الصلوة التي نسى ثم ليعد الصلوة التي صلى مع الامام (ب) (سن سليم للبیھقی ، باب من ذکر صلوۃ وھوفى اخرى ج ثانی
حاشیہ : (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جو نماز بھول جائے۔ پس یاد آئے اس حال میں کہ وہ امام کے ساتھ ہے تو وہ نماز پوری کرنا چاہئے پھر قضا کرے وہ (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
[273] (2) And he should give precedence to the missed prayer (fai'tah) over the time-based prayer (waqt), except if there is fear that the time-based prayer will be missed, then the time-based prayer should be given precedence over the missed prayer, and then the missed prayer will be made up. Three conditions must be present for the missed prayer to be prayed before the time-based prayer: (1) There should be enough time in the period to perform both the missed and the time-based prayers, because if there is not enough time to pray both, and he begins the missed one, the time-based prayer will also be missed, so what benefit is there? (2) He must remember that he has a missed prayer upon him. Because if he does not remember the missed prayer and prays the time-based one, the order (tartib) is waived, due to his being compelled (unaware). (3) There should not be more than six prayers as qada'. Because if there are more than six qada' prayers, then while performing those six, the time-based prayer would be missed and its time would elapse. Therefore, when these three conditions are present, the order between the missed and the time-based prayer is obligatory; otherwise not. (1) From the wording of the hadith in Bukhari 'falyusalli idha dhakara' it is understood that the time for the missed prayer becomes obligatory as soon as he remembers, and the time for the time-based prayer is after that. So the missed prayer should be performed first, then the time-based one. The emphasis of the hadith makes the order obligatory. (2) From Abdullah ibn Umar: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Whoever forgets a prayer and does not remember except while he is with an imam, then let him pray with the imam, and when he completes his prayer, let him repeat the prayer he forgot, and then let him repeat the prayer he prayed with the imam. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Whoever Remembers a Prayer While in Another Prayer, vol.2 Footnote (b): The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Whoever forgets a prayer, then remembers while he is with an imam, he should complete the prayer, then make it up... (remaining on next page)
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage discusses the order of precedence between a missed prayer (fai'tah) and the current obligatory prayer (waqt). The basic rule is that the missed prayer should be performed first. However, there is an exception: if performing the missed prayer would cause the current time prayer to be missed (i.e., there isn't enough time left for both), then the current time prayer takes precedence. The commentary specifies three conditions that must be met for the order (tartib) to be obligatory: (1) There must be enough time in the time window to perform both prayers comfortably. Otherwise, if you start the missed prayer and the time runs out, the current prayer is also missed, which is counterproductive. (2) The person must be aware that they have a missed prayer. If they forgot about the missed prayer and pray the current one first, the order is not required because they were unaware. (3) The number of missed prayers should not exceed six. If more than six prayers are overdue, then the order is not required because making up all six would inevitably cause the current prayer to be missed. Under these three conditions, performing the missed prayer before the current one is obligatory (wajib); otherwise, it is not. The evidence for the order comes from two sources: first, the same hadith 'pray when you remember' implies that upon remembering, the missed prayer becomes due immediately, so it must be done before the current one. Second, a hadith from Ibn Umar narrated by Bayhaqi states that if someone remembers a missed prayer while praying with an imam, they should complete the current prayer and then repeat the missed prayer and also repeat the prayer they performed with the imam (this indicates the importance of order). The footnote indicates the hadith continues on the next page.

Key Terms
فائتہ (fai'tah): A missed obligatory prayer that requires qada'.
وقتیہ (waqtiyyah): The current obligatory prayer that is due in its time.
ترتیب (tartib): Order of precedence between prayers, specifically that the missed prayer should be offered before the current one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone remembers a missed prayer and has enough time to pray both the missed and the current prayer, what is the ruling?
A) Pray the current prayer first, then the missed one.
B) Pray the missed prayer first, then the current one.
C) Only pray the missed prayer; the current one is waived.
D) Only pray the current prayer; the missed one is waived.

Key Takeaway
The order (tartib) between missed and current prayer is wajib only when there is enough time, you remember the missed prayer, and you have five or fewer missed prayers.

Making Up Missed Prayers: Obligation and Proof
States obligation and proof for qada of missed prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of making up a missed fard prayer (qada) and explain the proof from hadith and Quran, including the condition of immediacy and the exception for makruh times.

Core Idea
A missed obligatory prayer must be made up as soon as it is remembered—the obligation is not waived by time passing.

In this passage, the author establishes a fundamental ruling: whoever misses a fard prayer must make it up when they remember. The proof is drawn from a well-known hadith and a Quranic verse, showing that qada is fard. The passage also clarifies that the makeup must be done immediately upon remembering, but not during prohibited times. Let us walk through the reasoning and the textual evidence step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is missing an obligatory prayer. The ruling is that it must be made up (qada) when remembered. The hukm level is fard_ayn.
The ruling applies equally to all five daily prayers.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites the hadith of Anas ibn Malik (marfu‘): 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers; no expiation except that.' The Quranic verse 'Establish prayer for My remembrance' (20:14) is also referenced.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Abu Dawud; the verse is from Surah Ta-Ha.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The imperative 'falyusalli' indicates obligation per Hanafi usul: 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub' (a command indicates obligation). The phrase 'no expiation' reinforces that only performing the prayer suffices.
Both the hadith and verse are zanni in transmission (ahad) but strong in meaning.
4
Note the Condition of Immediacy
The hadith says 'when he remembers', implying immediate performance. The commentary emphasizes that it must be done as soon as remembered.
Delaying without a valid excuse is sinful.
5
Identify the Exception
The passage adds that qada should not be performed during makruh times (disliked times for prayer). The obligation is immediate except when the time is prohibited.
Details of makruh times are given later in the text.

Book of Prayer. Chapter on Making up Missed Prayers. [272] Whoever misses a prayer, he makes it up when he remembers it. [273] (2) And he gives precedence to it over the time prayer except... Chapter on Making up Missed Prayers: Necessary Note on Making up Missed Prayers: The prayer that is missed and left out is called fawa'it. Performing it is called qada'. Making up a prayer is obligatory because praying on time was obligatory; when one could not pray on time, now making it up becomes obligatory. Its proof is this hadith: from Anas ibn Malik from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers; there is no expiation for it except that. And establish prayer for My remembrance (Surah Ta-Ha, verse 14). (Bukhari, chapter on whoever forgets a prayer... p.84 no.597; Abu Dawud, chapter on whoever sleeps over a prayer or forgets it p.70 no.435) From this hadith and verse it is known that performing a missed prayer is obligatory. [272] (1) Whoever misses a prayer, he will make it up when he remembers. The prayer was obligatory; he has left it, so making it up becomes obligatory. In fact, as soon as he remembers, he should perform it immediately because in the above hadith of Bukhari it says: let him pray when he remembers; there is no expiation for it except that. Therefore, he makes up the prayer as soon as he remembers, provided it is not a disliked time. Because making up prayer in a disliked time is not permissible. Its detail will come later.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the obligation of making up missed prayers. The author states the matn: Whoever misses a prayer makes it up when he remembers. The commentary explains that qada is obligatory because the original prayer was obligatory (fard). The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers; there is no expiation for it except that.' This hadith from Bukhari and Abu Dawud, along with the verse 'Establish prayer for My remembrance,' establishes immediate obligation. The commentary further clarifies that making up should be done immediately upon remembering, but not during prohibited times (makruh awqat). This is the Hanafi position that missed prayers must be performed as soon as they are remembered without delay unless a valid excuse.

Key Terms
فوائت (fawa'it): Missed obligatory prayers that were not performed in their prescribed time.
قضاء (qada'): Performing an obligatory act of worship after its designated time has passed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on making up a missed obligatory prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is recommended but not obligatory.
B) It is obligatory and must be done immediately upon remembering.
C) It is obligatory but can be delayed to a convenient time.
D) It is not required if one has a valid excuse.

Key Takeaway
A missed fard prayer must be performed as soon as it is remembered, unless it is a prohibited time (makruh).

Order Among Missed Prayers: Wajib Up to Five
Ruling with proof on order of missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of missed prayers, identify the limit of five, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Order among missed prayers is wajib up to five; beyond that, the obligation is lifted due to hardship.

When a person has missed several prayers, does he have to make them up in the order they were originally due? The Hanafi school answers with a clear ruling: maintaining the sequence (tartib) is wajib, but only up to five missed prayers. Beyond that, the requirement is dropped. This lesson examines the textual evidence from the hadith of the Battle of the Trench (Khandaq) and addresses the Shafi'i view that order is merely sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The matn states: 'Whoever misses several prayers, he arranges them in qada as they were obligated originally, unless the missed prayers exceed five.' So the hukm is wajib with a limit.
The limit of five is specific to the obligation of order.
2
Examine the primary dalil
The hadith of Jabir (Bukhari, Tirmidhi) reports that on the day of Khandaq, the Prophet prayed the missed Asr before the on-time Maghrib.
This action demonstrates the necessity of order between missed and time prayers.
3
Understand the Hanafi istidlal
The Prophet's delaying of Maghrib to first make up Asr shows that order is obligatory, not merely recommended.
If order were sunnah, the Prophet would not have delayed the time prayer.
4
Consider the Shafi'i objection
Shafi'is cite the hadith of Ali (Bayhaqi) where the Prophet prayed Asr after Maghrib, suggesting order is not wajib.
The Hanafi response interprets this as an exceptional circumstance.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and the limit of five
The Hanafi school holds that the hadith of Ali is an exception; the overwhelming practice from the Khandaq hadith establishes wujub. The limit of five is a concession to remove hardship when the backlog becomes large.
The limit is based on the principle of ease (taysir) in the Shariah.

Source Text

[۲۷۴] (۳) ومن فاتته صلوات رتبها في القضاء كما وجبت في الاصل الا ان تزيد الفوائت على خمس ص ۱۳۱۳، نمبر ۳۱۹۳)

فائده امام شافعی اور دیگر ائمہ کے نزدیک فائتہ اور وقتیہ کے درمیان اسی طرح بہت سی فائتہ کے درمیان ترتیب سنت ہے۔ وہ بھی اوپر کی احادیث سے استدلال کرتے ہیں۔ اور ایک حدیث یہ بھی ہے جو سنت پر دلالت کرتی ہے عن علـى بـن طـالب انه قال شغل رسول الله له يوم الاحزاب عن صلوة العصر حتى صلى ما بين المغرب والعشاء فقال شغلونا عن الصلوة الوسطى
صلى الله

[274] (3) Whoever misses several prayers, he arranges them in qada as they were obligated originally, unless the missed prayers exceed five. (p.1313, no.3193) In this hadith, it is mentioned that even if he prayed the time prayer with the imam, he should make up the missed prayer; to maintain order, he repeats the time prayer. This shows that order between missed and time prayer is wajib. (3) The hadith in Bukhari for maintaining order between missed and time prayer: from Jabir who said: Umar was cursing the disbelievers on the day of Khandaq and said: O Messenger of Allah, I almost did not pray Asr until the sun set. He said: We descended at Bathan, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed Asr after sunset, then prayed Maghrib. (Bukhari, chapter on making up prayers in order, p.84 no.598; Tirmidhi, chapter on the man who misses prayers, with which to start, p.43 no.179/180) In this hadith, the missed Asr was prayed first, then Maghrib on time. This shows that order between missed and time prayer is necessary; otherwise they would not have delayed Maghrib. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i and other imams, the order between missed and time prayer, and similarly among many missed prayers, is sunnah. They also argue from the above hadith, and there is a hadith that indicates sunnah: from Ali ibn Talib that he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was occupied on the day of Ahzab from Asr prayer until he prayed between Maghrib and Isha, and he said: They distracted us from the middle prayer, the Asr prayer; may Allah fill their graves and homes with fire. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on those who say to abandon order in making them up, and it is the saying of Tawus and Hasan, vol.2 p.1312 no.3189) In this hadith, he prayed Asr after Maghrib, showing that order is not wajib but sunnah. [274] (3) Whoever misses many prayers, he will make them up in order as they were obligated originally, unless the missed prayers exceed five, then order falls away.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This final ruling addresses the sequence when multiple prayers are missed. The matn states that missed prayers must be made up in the order they were originally obligatory, with a limit: if they exceed five, order is no longer required. The commentary supports this with the hadith of Umar on the day of Khandaq, where Asr was made up before Maghrib. A benefit (fa'idah) introduces the Shafi'i position that order is sunnah, not wajib, citing the hadith of Ali who prayed Asr after Maghrib. The Hanafi position is that order is wajib up to a limit of five missed prayers; beyond that, the obligation of maintaining order is lifted due to hardship.

Key Terms
فوائت (fawa'it): Multiple missed prayers.
ترتیب (tartib): Sequential order of making up missed prayers according to their original times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Up to three
B) Up to five
C) Up to six
D) Always, no limit

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, maintaining order among missed prayers is wajib only when the total missed does not exceed five; beyond that, order is not required.

Order (Tarteeb) in Making Up Missed Prayers
Explains the ruling of order between missed and current prayers and among missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tarteeb between missed and current prayers, identify the proofs, and apply the exception when missed prayers exceed five.

Core Idea
Order between missed and current prayers is wajib; it drops only when missed prayers exceed five.

When a Muslim has missed prayers (qada), the Hanafi school requires him to make them up in the same order they were originally obligatory. This ruling, known as tarteeb, is derived from actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and is considered wajib. The Shafi'i school, however, classifies it as sunnah. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the exception for a large backlog, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that the act is making up missed prayers and that the Hanafi ruling is wajib for maintaining order.
The act is qada of fawaat.
2
Locate the proofs
Find the hadith cited: the hadith of Jabir (Bukhari) and the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i).
These are ahad hadith, so their thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the Prophet's action of praying 'Asr before Maghrib indicates obligation.
In Hanafi usul, the action of the Prophet in a context of teaching indicates wujub.
4
Analyze the dispute
Understand the Shafi'i position using the hadith of 'Ali, and note the Hanafi response that it was a special circumstance.
The thamarah al-khilaf is that in Hanafi, violating order is makruh tahrimi; in Shafi'i, it is merely leaving a sunnah.
5
Evaluate the exception
When missed prayers exceed five, order drops to avoid missing current prayers.
The wisdom is to prevent perpetual delay of the current prayer.

فائده امام شافعی اور دیگر ائمہ کے نزدیک فائتہ اور وقتیہ کے درمیان اسی طرح بہت سی فائتہ کے درمیان ترتیب سنت ہے۔ وہ بھی اوپر کی احادیث سے استدلال کرتے ہیں۔ اور ایک حدیث یہ بھی ہے جو سنت پر دلالت کرتی ہے عن علـى بـن طـالب انه قال شغل رسول الله له يوم الاحزاب عن صلوة العصر حتى صلى ما بين المغرب والعشاء فقال شغلونا عن الصلوة الوسطى صلوة العصر ملأ الله قبورهم وبيوتهم نار (ب) ( سنن سیھتی ، باب من قال بترك الترتيب في قضائهن وهو قول طاؤس والحسن ج ثانی ص ۱۳۱۲، نمبر ۳۱۸۹) اس حدیث میں آپ نے عصر کی نماز مغرب کے بعد پڑھی ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فائتہ اور وقتیہ کے درمیان ترتیب واجب نہیں سنت ہے۔ (۲۷۴) (۳) جس کی بہت سی نمازیں فوت ہو گئیں ان کو ترتیب وار قضا کرے گا۔ جس طرح اصل میں واجب ہوئی تھیں ۔ مگر یہ کہ فوائت پانچ نمازوں سے زیادہ ہو جا ئیں تو ان میں ترتیب ساقط ہو جائے گی۔

حاشیہ : ( پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) نماز جو بھولا ہے۔ پھر لوٹائے وہ نماز جو امام کے ساتھ پڑھی ہے (الف) حضرت عمرؓ جنگ خندق کے دن ان کے کفار کو برا بھلا کہنے لگے۔ پھر کہا کہ میں نے اب تک عصر کی نماز نہیں پڑھی۔ یہاں تک کہ سورج غروب ہو گیا۔ فرمایا ہم مقام بطحان میں اترے۔ پس ان لوگوں نے اور حضور نے سورج کے غروب ہونے کے بعد عصر کی نماز پڑھی۔ پھر مغرب کی نماز پڑھی (ب) حضرت علی فرماتے ہیں کہ حضور جنگ احزاب کے دن عصر کی نماز سے مشغول کر دیئے گئے ۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کو مغرب اور عشا کے درمیان پڑھی۔ پھر آپ نے فرمایا مجھے صلوۃ الوسطی صلوۃ عصر سے روک دیا گیا۔ اللہ ان کی قبروں اور گھروں کو آگ سے بھر دے۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاوّل)
