كتاب الصلوة
صلوات فيسقط الترتيب فيها.
ثم أقام فصلى الظهر ثم أقام فصلى العصر ثم اقام فصلى المغرب ثم اقام فصلى العشاء (الف)(ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الرجل تفوته الصلوات با تحصن سبد ص ۴۳، نمبر ۷۹ ارنسائی شریف، باب کیف یقضی الفوائت من الصلوۃ ص ۸۵، نمبر ۶۲۳ ) اس حدیث میں ترتیب کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی گئی ہے۔ پہلے ظہر پھر عصر پھر مغرب پھر عشا پڑھی ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ترتیب ضروری ہے لیکن اگر چھ نمازیں قضا ہو جا ئیں تو چونکہ اب ان کو قضا کرتے کرتے وقت یہ بھی فوت ہو جائے گی۔ اس لئے اب ترتیب ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ تاہم وقت ملے تو ترتیب برقرار کھے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) عبداللہ بن مسعود فرماتے ہیں کہ مشرکین نے حضور کو جنگ خندق کے دن چار نمازوں سے مشغول کر دیا۔ یہاں تک کہ جتنا اللہ چاہے رات چلی گئی۔ پس حضرت بلال کو حکم دیا ، پس اذان دی، پھر اقامت کہی۔ پس ظہر کی نماز پڑھی۔ پھر اقامت کہی پس عصر کی نماز پڑھی۔ پھر اقامت کہی پس مغرب کی نماز پڑھی۔ پھر اقامت کہی گئی پس عشا کی نماز پڑھی۔
If one fears that the time for the current prayer will pass, he gives precedence to the current prayer over the missed one, then makes up the missed prayer. (27)(3) Whoever has missed prayers should make them up in order as they were originally obligatory, unless the missed prayers exceed five. (p. 1313, no. 3193) This hadith states that even if he prayed the current prayer with the imam, he should make up the missed one, and for maintaining order, he should repeat the current prayer. From this it is understood that order between the missed and current prayer is obligatory. (3) The hadith for maintaining order between missed and current prayer is in Bukhari: from Jabir who said: 'Umar on the day of the trench was cursing the disbelievers and said: O Messenger of Allah! I could hardly pray 'Asr until the sun set. He said: We descended to Bathan, and the Messenger of Allah prayed 'Asr after the sun had set, then prayed Maghrib.' (Bukhari, chapter on making up prayers one after another, p. 84 no. 598; Tirmidhi, chapter on one who misses prayers, p. 43 no. 180/179) In this hadith, the missed 'Asr was prayed first, then the current Maghrib. From this it is understood that order between missed and current is necessary; otherwise they would not have delayed Maghrib. Benefit: According to Imam al-Shafi'i and other imams, order between a missed and current prayer, and similarly among many missed prayers, is sunnah. They also deduce from the above hadith, and there is another hadith that indicates sunnah: from 'Ali ibn Talib that he said: The Messenger of Allah was occupied on the day of the Confederates from the 'Asr prayer until he prayed between Maghrib and 'Isha, and he said: They occupied us from the middle prayer, the 'Asr prayer; may Allah fill their graves and houses with fire. (Sunan al-Kubra, chapter on those who say to leave order in qada, which is the view of Ta'us and al-Hasan, vol. 2, p. 1312, no. 3189) In this hadith, he prayed 'Asr after Maghrib. From this it is understood that order between missed and current is not obligatory but sunnah. (274)(3) Whoever has many prayers missed should make them up in order as they were originally obligatory, unless the missed prayers exceed five, then order drops. Just as order between a missed and current prayer is necessary, similarly if many are missed, order among them is necessary. For example, first Zuhr, then 'Asr, then Maghrib, then 'Isha, in the order they became obligatory. The proof is this hadith: 'Abdullah said: The polytheists occupied the Messenger of Allah from four prayers on the day of the trench until part of the night passed as Allah willed. He commanded Bilal, who gave the adhan, then the iqama, and he prayed Zuhr, then iqama for 'Asr, then iqama for Maghrib, then iqama for 'Isha.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on one who misses prayers, p. 43 no. 79; Nasa'i, chapter on how to make up missed prayers, p. 85 no. 623) In this hadith, prayers were prayed in order: first Zuhr, then 'Asr, then Maghrib, then 'Isha. From this it is understood that order is necessary. But if six prayers are missed, because while making them up the time would also be missed, therefore order drops. Nevertheless, if time permits, order should be maintained.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the obligation of order (tarteeb) in making up missed prayers. The author begins by stating a conditional ruling: if one fears missing the current prayer, he prays the current prayer first, then makes up the missed one. This implies that order between a missed prayer (faa'itah) and a current prayer (waqtiyyah) is required. The text then clarifies that this order is wajib (obligatory), not optional. The proof is the hadith of Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) from Sahih al-Bukhari: during the Battle of the Trench, 'Umar had not prayed 'Asr, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed 'Asr after sunset, then prayed Maghrib. This shows that the missed 'Asr was given precedence over the current Maghrib, indicating that order is necessary. The author then addresses the view of Imam al-Shafi'i and others who consider this order to be sunnah (commendable) rather than wajib. They cite a hadith from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) where the Prophet prayed 'Asr between Maghrib and 'Isha, i.e., after the current Maghrib, suggesting that order is not obligatory. The Hanafi response, implicit in the text, is that the hadith of 'Ali can be interpreted as an emergency situation (shopping/deflection), and the general practice is to maintain order. The text then moves to the case of multiple missed prayers. Ruling: If a person has missed several prayers, he must make them up in the order they were originally obligatory (e.g., Zuhr first, then 'Asr, then Maghrib, then 'Isha). This is proven by the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud from Tirmidhi and Nasa'i: the Prophet made up four prayers in order. However, if the number of missed prayers exceeds five, the obligation of order drops. The reason is practical: if one keeps order with too many prayers, he may miss the current prayer again. Nonetheless, if time permits, maintaining order is still better.

Key Terms
ترتیب (tarteeb): The obligated sequence in making up missed prayers according to their original order.
فائتہ / فوائت (faa'itah / fawaat): A prayer that was missed due to being occupied or forgetfulness; plural: fawaat.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its time has expired.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on order (tarteeb) when a person has missed more than five prayers?
A) Order remains wajib regardless of the number.
B) Order becomes sunnah.
C) Order drops and is no longer required.
D) Order becomes haram.

Key Takeaway
Order (tarteeb) in making up missed prayers is wajib in the Hanafi school, but this obligation drops if the missed prayers exceed five.

The Obligation of Order in Qada and When It Drops
Ruling with proof on the obligation of order in qada and its exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of missed prayers and identify when the obligation of order is dropped.

Core Idea
Order for qada is wajib for up to five prayers; for six or more, obligation drops.

This passage addresses a key practical question: how to make up multiple missed prayers. The Hanafi school derives from the Prophet's action that order is normally required, but an important exception exists to avoid further loss of prayers. We will examine the proof and the reasoning behind the exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the order (tarteeb) when performing multiple missed prayers (qada). The Hanafi ruling: order is wajib (obligatory).
Wajib means the omission requires compensation (sajdah sahw or repetition) but does not invalidate the entire qada.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) made up four missed prayers in sequence (Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha).
The hadith is found in Tirmidhi and Nasa'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of praying in order indicates the obligation of order. The Hanafi principle: the act of the Prophet in a context of clarification (bayan) is evidence of obligation.
The command for order is derived from the action, not verbal command.
4
Note the exception
If six or more prayers are missed, the obligation of order drops. Reason: insisting on order would cause further prayers to be missed, leading to greater hardship.
The number six is derived from the principle that if the number exceeds five, order drops.
5
Identify the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that order is obligatory in all cases of missed prayers, with no exception. The difference stems from how each school interprets the same hadith and the principle of necessity.
The Hanafi school uses the principle of darura (necessity) to limit the obligation.

Prayers, so order drops in them. Then he said the iqama and prayed Zuhr, then said the iqama and prayed Asr, then said the iqama and prayed Maghrib, then said the iqama and prayed Isha. (Tirmidhi, chapter on the one who misses prayers, p. 43, no. 79; Nasa'i, chapter on how to make up missed prayers, p. 85, no. 623). In this hadith, prayers were offered in order: first Zuhr, then Asr, then Maghrib, then Isha. From this it is understood that order is necessary. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the order (tarteeb) when making up missed prayers (qada). It presents a hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) made up four missed prayers from the Battle of the Trench in sequence: Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha. From this, the Hanafi school derives that order is normally obligatory (wajib) when making up multiple missed prayers. However, if the number of missed prayers reaches six or more, the obligation of order is dropped because insisting on order would cause further prayers to be missed. The commentator notes that if there is sufficient time, order should still be observed as a recommended practice. The footnote provides the full context of the hadith. The Hanafi ruling is based on the principle of necessity (darura) and avoiding undue hardship.

Key Terms
صلاة (salah): Prayer, the act of worship consisting of specific recitations and physical postures.
قضا (qada): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its time has ended.
ترتيب (tarteeb): Observing the correct sequence when performing multiple missed prayers.

The Three Times When Prayer is Disliked
Stating and explaining the three times when prayer is prohibited

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three times when prayer is makruh tahrimi, explain the Hanafi evidence, and distinguish the ruling for nafl vs fard prayers after Asr and Fajr.

Core Idea
Prayer at sunrise, midday, and sunset is makruh tahrimi; after Asr and Fajr, only nafl is makruh tanzihi.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on prohibited times for prayer. The matn states the general prohibition, and the commentary classifies the severity of dislike (karahah) into tahrimi and tanzihi. Understanding this distinction is essential for knowing when a prayer is valid but sinful versus merely discouraged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three times and the ruling
Look at the matn: sunrise, sunset, midday. The ruling is that prayer is not permissible (la yajuz). The commentary clarifies it is makruh tahrimi. Note the exception for Asr of that day at sunset.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of Uqba ibn Amir lists the same three times. Identify that the Prophet forbade prayer and burying dead in these hours. This is the primary evidence.
Hadith from Muslim and Nasa'i.
3
Distinguish severe vs. mild dislike
The commentary says the three times are severe (makruh tahrimi) for all prayers. After Asr and Fajr, only nafl is makruh tanzihi, and fard/wajib are allowed. Fajr sunnah before Fajr is allowed, but other nafl after Fajr time begins is disliked.
4
Understand the wisdom
The hadith of Umar ibn Abasa explains that non-Muslims worship the sun at these times, and Satan is present. This wisdom supports the prohibition but does not make it haram.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a scenario, identify whether prayer is makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi, or permissible. For example, praying Asr at sunset on the same day is allowed because of the exception.

Chapter on the times when prayer is disliked. [275] (1) It is not permissible to pray at sunrise, nor at sunset, except the Asr of that day, nor at midday. Necessary note: This is an explanation of the times when prayer is disliked. Its proof is this hadith: I heard Uqba ibn Amir al-Juhani say: There are three hours when the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) used to forbid us from praying or burying our dead: when the sun rises until it has risen high, when the sun is at its zenith until it declines, and when the sun inclines to set until it sets. (Muslim, no. 1831; Nasa'i, no. 561). From this hadith it is understood that prayer in these three times is disliked. Now there are three categories of disliked times: (1) At sunrise, sunset, and midday the dislike is severe. It is makruh tahrimi to pray any fard or nafl prayer in these times. (2) After Asr fard and Fajr fard, the dislike is lesser. It is disliked to pray nafl, but one may pray fard and wajib. (3) After Fajr time begins, apart from the two sunnah of Fajr, it is disliked to pray any nafl. This is also a lesser dislike. [275] (1) It is not permissible to pray at sunrise, nor at sunset, except the Asr of that day, nor at midday. (1) In these three times, non-Muslims worship the sun, so prayer is prohibited. He said, Umar ibn Abasa al-Sulami... He said: O Messenger of Allah, inform me about prayer. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Pray Fajr, then refrain from prayer until the sun rises high, for it rises between the horns of Satan, and at that time the disbelievers prostrate to it. Then pray, for the prayer is witnessed and attended until the shadow is the length of a spear. Then refrain from prayer, for at that time Hell is kindled. When the shadow moves, pray, for the prayer is witnessed and attended until you pray Asr. Then refrain from prayer until the sun sets, for it sets between the horns of Satan, and at that time the disbelievers prostrate to it. (Muslim, no. 832; Nasa'i, chapter on prohibition of prayer after Asr). Footnote (a): Uqba ibn Amir says: The Prophet used to forbid us from praying and burying our dead in three times: when the sun rises brightly until it rises high, when the sun is exactly at midday until it declines, and when the sun inclines to set until it sets. Footnote (b): He said: Pray Fajr, then refrain from prayer until the sun rises or becomes high, for it rises between the horns of Satan, and the disbelievers prostrate to it. Then pray, for the prayer is witnessed and attended until the shadow is a spear's length. Then refrain from prayer, for at that time Hell is kindled. When the shadow moves, pray, for the prayer is witnessed and attended until you pray Asr. Then refrain from prayer until the sun sets, for it sets between the horns of Satan, and the disbelievers prostrate to it. (Remainder on next page).
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the disliked times for prayer. It opens with a matn (base text) stating the prohibition of prayer at sunrise, sunset, and midday, with an exception for the Asr of that day. The commentator then provides a necessary note, citing the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir that lists three times: sunrise, zenith, and sunset. The commentary explains that there are three categories of disliked times: (1) At sunrise, sunset, and midday, the dislikedness is severe (makruh tahrimi) and includes all prayers. (2) After the fard of Asr and Fajr, the dislike is lesser (makruh tanzihi), and only nafl prayers are disliked; fard and wajib prayers may be offered. (3) After Fajr time begins, it is disliked to pray any nafl except the two sunnah of Fajr. The commentator then provides the reason: these times are associated with sun worship by non-Muslims, as indicated in the hadith of Umar ibn Abasa, which also links the times to Satan. The Hanafi school distinguishes between severe and mild dislike based on the strength of evidence and the extent of prohibition.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): A disliked act that is close to forbidden; committing it is sinful but does not invalidate faith.
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): A disliked act that is better to avoid but not sinful.
وقت نهي (waqt nahy): A time in which prayer is prohibited or disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Prohibited Times for Salah and the Exception for Asr
Ruling on prohibited times for salah with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited times for salah, distinguish between makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi, and explain the Hanafi exception for Asr salah at sunset.

Core Idea
Salah is severely prohibited at sunrise, sunset, and zenith; only Asr caught before sunset is valid.

The Hanafi school identifies three times when performing salah is severely disliked (makruh tahrimi) due to explicit prophetic prohibitions. However, there is an important exception: if you catch a rak'ah of Asr before sunset, the prayer is valid despite the sunset time. This lesson unpacks the rulings, their proof from hadith, and the differences between Hanafi and other madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited times
From the matn and hadith, list the three times: sunrise, sunset, and zenith (when the sun is directly overhead).
These are times of makruh tahrimi for any salah.
2
Understand the degrees of dislike
Note that the dislike is severe (makruh tahrimi) at the three times, but after Fajr and after Asr the dislike is lighter (makruh tanzihi) and only for voluntary prayers.
Obligatory prayers can still be performed after Fajr and Asr.
3
Analyze the exception for Asr
The hadith of Abu Hurayrah states that catching a rak'ah of Asr before sunset counts as performing it. The Hanafi school applies this only to Asr, not Fajr.
If you catch a rak'ah of Fajr at sunrise, the prayer is invalid because the whole time is not complete.
4
Examine the Shafi'i disagreement
Imam al-Shafi'i allows salah in Makkah at any time due to a hadith about the Kaaba. The Hanafi school maintains the general prohibition applies everywhere.
The Hanafi response is that the Makkah exception does not override the clear prohibitions.

Source Text

باب الاوقات التي تكره فيها الصلوة
[۲۷۵] (۱) لا يجوز الصلوة عند طلوع الشمس ولا عند غروبها الا عصر يومه ولا عند قيامها في الظهيرة
ضروری نوٹ جن اوقات میں نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے اس کا بیان ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے سمعت عقبة بن عامر الجهني يقول ثلاث ساعات كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ينهانا ان نصلى فيهن او ان نقبر فيهن موتانا حين تطلع الشمس بازغة حتى ترتفع وحين يقوم قائم الظهيرة حتى تميل الشمس و حين تضيف الشمس للغروب حتى تغرب (الف)(مسلم شریف، باب الاوقات التی تنھی عن الصلوة فيها ص ۲۷۶ نمبر ۱۸۳۱ نسائی شریف، باب الساعات التی نہی عن الصلوۃ فیھا ص ۶۵ نمبر ۵۶۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان تین اوقات میں نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔
نون تین قسم کے مکروہات ہیں (۱) طلوع آفتاب، غروب آفتاب اور دوپہر کے وقت میں کراہیت شدید ہے۔ اس میں کوئی فرض یا نفل نماز پڑھنا مکروہ تحریمی ہے (۲) اور عصر کے فرض اور فجر کے فرض کے بعد کراہیت اس میں کم ہے۔ اس میں نوافل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے البتہ فرائض اور واجبات پڑھ سکتا ہے (۳) فجر طلوع ہونے کے بعد نجر کی دوسنتوں کے علاوہ کسی بھی نوافل کا پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ اس میں بھی کراہیت کم ہے۔ [۲۷۵] (۱) نہیں جائز ہے نماز سورج طلوع ہوتے وقت اور نہ اس کے غروب ہوتے وقت مگر اس دن کی عصر اور نہ ٹھیک دوپہر کے وقت ۔ (۱) ان تین اوقات میں غیر مسلم سورج کی عبادت کرتے ہیں اس لئے ان تین اوقات میں نماز پڑھنے سے روکا۔ قال عمر بن عنسة السلمي ... اخبرني عن الصلوة؟ قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى صلوة الصبح ثم اقصر عن الصلوة حتى تطلع الشمس حتى ترتفع فانها تطلع حين تطلع بين قرنى شيطان و حينئذ يسجد لها الكفار ثم صل فان الصلوة مشهودة محضورة حتى يستقل الظل بالرمح ثم اقصر عن الصلوة فان حينئذ تسجر جهنم فاذا اقبل الفيئ فصل فإن الصلوة مشهودة محضورة حتى تصلى العصر ثم اقصر عن الصلوة حتى تغرب الشمس فانها تغرب بين قرنی شیطان و حینئذ يسجد لها الكفار (ب) (مسلم شریف ، باب الاوقات التي نہی عن الصلوة فيها ص ۲۷۶ نمبر ۸۳۲ نسائی شریف ، باب النهي عن الصلوة بعد العصرص ۶۶ نمبر ۵۷۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان تین اوقات میں نماز عصر پڑھنا مکروہ ہے (۲) اوپر کی ضروری نوٹ میں بھی مسلم کی حدیث گزری (۳) عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لا تتحروا بصلوتكم طلوع الشمس ولا غروبها (فانها تطلع بين قرني الشيطان) (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلوة بعد الفجرحتى ترتفع الشمس ص ۸۲ نمبر ۸۲ ۵ر مسلم شریف، باب الاوقات التی نہی عن الصلوة فيها ص ۲۷۵ نمبر ۸۲۸ رنسائی شریف، باب نھی عن الصلوۃ بعد العصر ص ۶۶ نمبر ۵۷۱) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان تین اوقات میں نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے (۴) عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله اذا بدا حاجب الشمس فأخروا الصلوة حتى تبرزواذا غاب حاجب الشمس فأخروا الصلوه حتى تغيب (ب) ( مسلم شریف ، باب الاوقات التی نہی عن الصلوة فيها ص ۲۷۵ نمبر ۸۲۹) امام شافعی کے نزدیک بیت اللہ کے ارد گر د اوقات مکروہ میں بھی نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن جبیر بن مطعم ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال يا بني عبد مناف لا تمنعوا احدا طاف بهذا البيت وصلى اية ساعة شاء من ليل أو نها (ج) ( نسائى شریف ، باب اباحۃ الصلوة في الساعات کلھا بمکۃ ص ۶۸ نمبر ۵۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مکہ میں اوقات مکروہ میں بھی نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔
اس دن کی عصر غروب آفتاب کے وقت پڑھنے کی وجہ یہ ہے (۱) عن ابي هرير ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من ادرك من الصبح ركعة قبل ان تطلع الشمس فقد ادرك الصبح ومن ادرك ركعة من العصر قبل ان تغرب الشمس فقد ادرک العصر (1) ( بخاری شریف، باب من ادر ک من الفجر ركعته ص ۸۲ نمبر ۸۵۷۹ مسلم شریف ، باب من ادرک رکعتة من الصلوة فقدا درک تلک الصلوۃ ص ۲۲۱ نمبر ۲۰۸ / ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فیمن ادرك ركعة من العصر قبل ان تغرب الشمس ص ۴۵ نمبر ۶ ۱۸ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورج کے غروب ہونے سے پہلے عصر کی نماز مل گئی تو گویا کہ وہ نماز مل گئی۔ چونکہ عصر کا آخری وقت مکروہ ہے اور وہی وقت اس کی نماز کے لئے سبب بنا اس لئے سورج کے غروب ہونے کی کراہیت درمیان نماز میں آگئی پھر بھی نماز ہو جائے گی۔ اس حدیث کو حنفیہ کے نزدیک صرف عصر کی نماز پر محمول کرتے ہیں۔ اور فجر کا پورا وقت کامل ہے اس لئے اس کے درمیان میں سورج نکل گیا تو نماز فاسد ہوگی۔ گویا کہ اوقات مکروہ میں نماز پڑھنے کی ممانعت والی حدیث کو فجر کے وقت پر محمول کرتے ہیں۔
دوسرے ائمہ کے نزدیک ان اوقات میں نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے لیکن پڑھ لیا تو فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔ الظهيرة : ٹھیک دوپہر ۔
Chapter of the times in which salah is disliked. [275] (1) It is not permissible to perform salah at sunrise, nor at sunset except the Asr of that day, nor when it [the sun] is at its zenith. Essential note: An explanation of the times when praying is disliked. Its proof is this hadith: I heard 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir al-Juhani say: There are three hours in which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to forbid us to pray or to bury our dead in them: when the sun rises until it rises fully, when the sun is at its zenith until it declines, and when the sun inclines towards setting until it sets. (Muslim, Sunan al-Nasa'i). It is learned from this hadith that praying in these three times is disliked. There are three types of disliked acts: (1) At sunrise, sunset, and midday, the dislike is severe. In these, praying any obligatory or voluntary prayer is tahrimi makruh. (2) After Asr and after Fajr, the dislike is less. In these, performing voluntary prayers is disliked, but obligatory and wajib prayers can be performed. (3) After sunrise, besides the two sunnah of Fajr, any voluntary prayer is disliked. The dislike here is less. [275] (1) It is not permissible to pray at the time of sunrise, nor at sunset except the Asr of that day, nor at midday. (1) In these three times, non-Muslims worship the sun, therefore one is prohibited from praying in these three times. 'Umar ibn 'Anasah al-Sulami said: ... He asked about prayer. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Pray the morning prayer, then refrain from prayer until the sun rises and becomes high, for it rises between the two horns of Satan, and at that time the disbelievers prostrate to it. Then pray, for the prayer is witnessed and attended until the shadow becomes equal to a spear. Then refrain from prayer, for at that time Hell is kindled. When the shadow returns, pray, for the prayer is witnessed and attended until you pray Asr. Then refrain from prayer until the sun sets, for it sets between the two horns of Satan, and at that time the disbelievers prostrate to it. (Muslim, Sunan al-Nasa'i). It is learned from this hadith that praying in these three times is disliked. (2) The hadith of Muslim has also passed in the essential note above. (3) From Ibn 'Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Do not seek to pray at sunrise or sunset, for they rise between the horns of Satan. (Bukhari, Muslim, Nasa'i). From these hadiths it is learned that praying in these three times is disliked. (4) From Ibn 'Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: When the edge of the sun appears, delay the prayer until it fully rises, and when the edge of the sun disappears, delay the prayer until it fully sets. (Muslim). According to Imam al-Shafi'i, around the Kaaba, praying in these disliked times is permissible. His proof is the hadith from Jubayr ibn Mut'im that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: O Banu 'Abd Manaf, do not prevent anyone from circumambulating this House and praying at any hour of the night or day. (Nasa'i). It is learned from this hadith that in Makkah, praying in the disliked times is permissible. The reason for reciting the Asr of that day at sunset is (1) From Abu Hurayrah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr. (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi). It is learned from this hadith that if one catches the Asr prayer before sunset, it is as if he caught the prayer. Since the end time of Asr is disliked and that time is the cause for its prayer, the dislike of sunset enters the prayer, yet the prayer is valid. According to the Hanafis, this hadith is applied only to Asr prayer. For Fajr, its entire time is complete, so if the sun rises during it, the prayer becomes invalid. Thus, the hadith prohibiting prayer in disliked times is applied to the time of Fajr. According to other imams, praying in these times is disliked, but if one does pray, it is not invalid. Al-Zahirah: exactly midday.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the times when salah is prohibited or disliked. The matn states that salah is not permissible at three times: sunrise, sunset (except Asr of that day), and when the sun is at its zenith. The commentary explains that the dislike is of different degrees. At the three times of sunrise, sunset, and zenith, the dislike is severe (makruh tahrimi), meaning it is forbidden but not to the level of haram. After Fajr and after Asr, the dislike is less severe (makruh tanzihi), only for voluntary prayers; obligatory prayers can still be performed. After sunrise until shortly after, only the two sunnah of Fajr can be prayed; other voluntary prayers are disliked. The text provides several hadith proofs. The first hadith from 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir lists the three times. The second from 'Umar ibn 'Anasah explains the reason: at these times, the sun rises and sets between the horns of Satan, and disbelievers prostrate to it, so we avoid resemblance. The third from Ibn 'Umar repeats the prohibition. The fourth hadith advises to delay prayer until the sun fully appears or disappears. Then the text mentions the view of Imam al-Shafi'i that in Makkah, prayer is permissible at all times because of the hadith of Jubayr ibn Mut'im about not preventing tawaf and prayer at any time. However, the Hanafi response is implicit: the general prohibition remains, and the exception for Makkah does not override the clear hadiths. The text then discusses the exception for Asr of that day. The hadith of Abu Hurayrah states that if one catches a rak'ah of Asr before sunset, he has caught the prayer. Since the end of Asr time is disliked but the prayer is performed due to necessity, the dislike does not invalidate it. For Fajr, however, the entire time is complete, so if sunrise occurs during prayer, it becomes invalid. The Hanafi school applies the hadith about catching a rak'ah only to Asr, not to Fajr, because Fajr's time ends at sunrise and the prayer cannot be delayed.

Key Terms
طلوع الشمس (tulu' al-shams): The time when the sun's disk begins to appear above the horizon.
غروب الشمس (ghurub al-shams): The time when the sun's disk disappears below the horizon.
ظهيرة (zahirah): The time when the sun is at its zenith, exactly midday.
مكروه تحريمي (makruh tahrimi): An act that is forbidden but not proven by a definitive dalil; it is sinful to do and must be avoided.
مكروه تنزيهي (makruh tanzihi): An act that is disliked but not sinful; it is better to avoid but valid if performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
At which of the following times is it permissible to pray an obligatory prayer that one has missed?
A) When the sun is rising
B) When the sun is at its zenith
C) After Asr prayer
D) During sunset

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits salah at three specific times due to explicit hadith, with an exception for Asr caught before sunset, and considers the dislike at other borderline times as lighter.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Ruling on Prayer During Prohibited Times (Makruh Awqat)
Ruling with proof on prayer at prohibited times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited times for prayer in the Hanafi school, explain the ruling of makruh tahrimi, and apply the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith of catching a rak'ah to distinguish between Asr and Fajr.

Core Idea
Prayer at sunrise, sunset, and zenith is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), with an exception for Asr if one catches a rak'ah before sunset.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade prayer at specific times when the sun is rising or setting, and also when it is at its zenith. These are known as the makruh awqat (disliked times). In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that prayer during these times is makruh tahrimi, the evidence from hadith, and the important exception for Asr prayer. We also explore the dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding prayer in Makkah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited times
From the hadith cited, determine the three specific times when prayer is prohibited: sunrise, sunset, and when the sun is at its zenith (noon). Note that these are based on the sun's position.
The term 'zahirah' refers to exactly noon when the sun is overhead.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its basis
In the Hanafi school, praying at these times is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), not haram. Understand that this is because the evidence (ahad hadith) is zanni al-thubut, so the prohibition is at a lower level than haram.
If the evidence were qat'i, the ruling would be haram.
3
Analyze the primary dalil
Examine the hadith: 'Do not seek to pray at sunrise or sunset, for it rises between the horns of Satan.' Identify the phrase indicating prohibition (la tataharraw) and understand that this is the basis for karahah.
The phrase 'between the horns of Satan' explains the wisdom behind the prohibition.
4
Examine the Shafi'i counter-evidence and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school cites a hadith allowing prayer around the Kaaba at any time. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is specific to tawaf prayer, not general. This shows how different schools reconcile conflicting evidence.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on the principle of takhsis (specification).
5
Apply the Hanafi ta'wil of the rak'ah hadith
The hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah before sunrise/sunset has caught the prayer' is interpreted by Hanafis as applying only to Asr, not Fajr. For Fajr, the entire time is considered complete, so if the sun rises during Fajr, the prayer is invalid. For Asr, the last part is makruh but catching a rak'ah makes it valid.
This resolves the apparent conflict between the prohibition and the rak'ah hadith.

قيامها في الظهيرة -
۶۶ نمبر ۵۷۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان تین اوقات میں نماز عصر پڑھنا مکروہ ہے (۲) اوپر کی ضروری نوٹ میں بھی مسلم کی حدیث گزری (۳) عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله الا الله قال لا تتحروا بصلوتكم طلوع الشمس ولا غروبها (فانها تطلع بين قرني الشيطان) (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلوة بعد الفجرحتى ترتفع الشمس ص ۸۲ نمبر ۸۲ ۵ر مسلم شریف، باب الاوقات التی نہی عن الصلوة فيها ص ۲۷۵ نمبر ۸۲۸ رنسائی شریف، باب نھی عن الصلوۃ بعد العصر ص ۶۶ نمبر ۵۷۱) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان تین اوقات میں نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے (۴) عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله اذا بدا حاجب الشمس فأخروا الصلوة حتى تبرزواذا غاب حاجب الشمس فأخروا الصلوه حتى تغيب (ب) ( مسلم شریف ، باب الاوقات التی نہی عن الصلوة فيها ص ۲۷۵ نمبر ۸۲۹) امام شافعی کے نزدیک بیت اللہ کے ارد گر د اوقات مکروہ میں بھی نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن جبیر بن مطعم ان النبي الله قال يا بني عبد مناف لا تمنعوا احدا طاف بهذا البيت وصلى اية ساعة شاء من ليل أو نها (ج) ( نسائى شریف ، باب اباحۃ الصلوة في الساعات کلھا بمکۃ ص ۶۸ نمبر ۵۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مکہ میں اوقات مکروہ میں بھی نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔
اس دن کی عصر غروب آفتاب کے وقت پڑھنے کی وجہ یہ ہے (۱) عن ابي هرير ان رسول الله له قال من ادرك من الصبح ركعة قبل ان تطلع الشمس فقد ادرك الصبح ومن ادرك ركعة من العصر قبل ان تغرب الشمس فقد ادرک العصر (1) ( بخاری شریف، باب من ادر ک من الفجر ركعته ص ۸۲ نمبر ۸۵۷۹ مسلم شریف ، باب من ادرک رکعتة من الصلوة فقدا درک تلک الصلوۃ ص ۲۲۱ نمبر ۲۰۸ / ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فیمن ادرك ركعة من العصر قبل ان تغرب الشمس ص ۴۵ نمبر ۶ ۱۸ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورج کے غروب ہونے سے پہلے عصر کی نماز مل گئی تو گویا کہ وہ نماز مل گئی۔ چونکہ عصر کا آخری وقت مکروہ ہے اور وہی وقت اس کی نماز کے لئے سبب بنا اس لئے سورج کے غروب ہونے کی کراہیت درمیان نماز میں آگئی پھر بھی نماز ہو جائے گی۔ اس حدیث کو حنفیہ کے نزدیک صرف عصر کی نماز پر محمول کرتے ہیں۔ اور فجر کا پور اوقت کامل ہے اس لئے اس کے درمیان میں سورج نکل گیا تو نماز فاسد ہوگی۔ گویا کہ اوقات مکروہ میں نماز پڑھنے کی ممانعت والی حدیث کو فجر کے وقت پر محمول کرتے ہیں۔
دوسرے ائمہ کے نزدیک ان اوقات میں نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے لیکن پڑھ لیا تو فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔ الظهيرة : ٹھیک دوپہر ۔
حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) وقت کفار اس کو سجدہ کرتے ہیں ( الف ) آپ نے فرمایا اپنی نماز کے لئے سورج کے طلوع ہونے اور اس کے غروب ہونے کا انتظار کرو ۔ اس لئے کہ وہ شیطان کے دو سینگوں کے درمیان طلوع ہوتا ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جب سورج کا کنارہ ظاہر ہو تو نماز کو مؤخر کرو۔ یہاں تک کہ وہ بالکل نکل جائے۔ اور جب سورج کا کنارہ ڈوبنے لگ جائے تو نماز کو مؤخر کرو یہاں تک کہ ڈوب جائے (ج) آپ نے فرمایا اے عبد مناف کے لوگو ! اس بیت اللہ کے طواف اور نماز پڑھنے سے کسی کو مت روکو رات اور دن کی جس گھڑی میں چاہیں (1) آپ نے فرمایا جس نے صبح کی ایک رکعت پالی سورج طلوع ہونے سے پہلے تو گویا کہ صبح کی نماز پالی۔ اور جس نے عصر کی ایک رکعت پالی سورج کے غروب ہونے سے پہلے تو گویا کہ عصر کی نماز پالی۔
From the hadith (no. 573) it is known that praying Asr in these three times is makruh. The necessary note above also mentioned Muslim's hadith. From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Do not seek to pray at sunrise or sunset, for it rises between the horns of Satan.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Nasa'i). From these hadith it is known that praying in these three times is makruh. From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When the edge of the sun appears, delay prayer until it fully rises; and when the edge of the sun sets, delay prayer until it fully sets.' (Muslim). According to Imam Shafi'i, it is permissible to pray around the Kaaba even in makruh times. His evidence is the hadith of Jubayr ibn Mut'im: The Prophet said: 'O Banu Abd Manaf, do not prevent anyone from circumambulating this House and praying at any hour of night or day.' (Nasa'i). This hadith shows that in Makkah it is permissible to pray even in makruh times. The reason for praying Asr at sunset: from Abu Hurayrah: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught Asr.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi). From this hadith it is known that if Asr prayer is caught before sunset, it is as if he caught the prayer. Since the last time of Asr is makruh and that time is the cause of its prayer, the karahah of sunset enters the prayer, yet the prayer is valid. The Hanafis interpret this hadith only for Asr prayer. For Fajr, the entire time is complete, so if the sun rises during it, the prayer becomes invalid. Thus the hadith prohibiting prayer in makruh times is applied to the time of Fajr. According to other Imams, praying in these times is makruh but if done, it is not invalid. Al-Zahirah: exactly noon. Footnote: (from previous page) The disbelievers prostrate to it. (a) He said: Do not wait for sunrise or sunset for your prayer, for it rises between the horns of Satan. (b) He said: When the edge of the sun appears, delay prayer until it fully appears; and when the edge of the sun begins to set, delay prayer until it sets. (c) He said: O people of Abd Manaf, do not prevent anyone from circumambulating this House and praying at any hour of night or day. (1) He said: Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise has caught Fajr; whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught Asr.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding prayer during the three prohibited times: at sunrise, sunset, and zenith (when the sun is at its meridian). The author first cites multiple hadith establishing that prayer in these times is makruh (disliked, and according to the Hanafi school, makruh tahrimi – prohibitively disliked). The hadith from Ibn Umar explicitly forbid seeking to pray at sunrise and sunset. Then the author presents the Shafi'i position: prayer in Makkah is permissible at all times, based on the hadith of Jubayr ibn Mut'im. The Hanafi school, however, holds that this is specific to tawaf prayer and does not apply generally. Next, the passage discusses the hadith about catching a rak'ah before sunrise/sunset. The Hanafi ta'wil (interpretation) is that this applies only to Asr, not Fajr. For Asr, if one catches a rak'ah before sunset, the prayer is valid even though part of it occurs in the makruh time. For Fajr, the entire time is considered complete, so if the sun rises during Fajr prayer, the prayer is invalid. This resolves the apparent conflict between the prohibition and the hadith of catching a rak'ah. The footnote explains the Arabic phrases used in the hadith.

Key Terms
الظهيرة (al-ẓahīrah): The time when the sun is at its zenith, exactly at noon.
مکروہ (makrūh): Disliked; in this context, it means prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if one begins Fajr prayer before sunrise but the sun rises during the prayer?
A) The prayer is valid because he caught a rak'ah before sunrise.
B) The prayer is invalid because the entire time of Fajr is considered complete and the sun rose during it.
C) The prayer is makruh but valid.
D) The prayer must be repeated after sunrise.

Key Takeaway
Prayer at sunrise, sunset, and zenith is makruh tahrimi, but Asr prayer caught before sunset is valid; Fajr prayer interrupted by sunrise is invalid.

Janazah and Sajdah in Prohibited Times: Exception for Cause
States the ruling and provides evidence with exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on janazah prayer and sajdah tilawah during the three prohibited times, identify the supporting evidences, and apply the exception when the cause arises within those times.

Core Idea
Janazah prayer in prohibited times is allowed if the janazah is present; the need to hasten burial overrides the prohibition.

This lesson examines the ruling on janazah prayer and sajdah tilawah during the three disliked times: sunrise, zenith, and sunset. The general rule prohibits any prayer during these times, as they are considered makruh tahrimi. However, an important exception exists when the cause—the janazah arriving or a prostration verse being recited—occurs precisely within those times. We will explore the evidence and the rationale behind this exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and general prohibition
The passage states that janazah prayer and sajdah tilawah are not performed in the prohibited times. Understand that these are considered forms of prayer, and any voluntary prayer in these times is makruh tahrimi.
The three prohibited times are: sunrise, zenith, and sunset.
2
Examine the evidence for prohibition
The author cites a hadith from Muslim about burying at sunrise, interpreted to mean not praying janazah at that time. For sajdah tilawah, an athar from Ibn Umar shows that the Companions did not prostrate after Fajr until sunrise.
The evidence is ahad (single-chain) but accepted for prohibition.
3
Analyze the exception and its cause
If the cause (janazah arriving or reciting a verse of prostration) occurs during the prohibited time itself, the ruling changes to permissibility. This is because the prohibited time becomes secondary to the cause.
The exception is based on the principle of necessity and the hadith 'Do not delay the janazah.'
4
Identify the overriding principle and supporting hadith
The principle of hastening the janazah to avoid decomposition overrides the general prohibition. The hadith 'Do not delay the janazah when it is present' (Ibn Majah) is cited as evidence.
This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text

[۲۷] (٢) اور ان اوقات مکروہ میں جنازہ پر نماز نہ پڑھے اور نہ سجدہ تلاوت کرے۔ (۱) نماز جنازہ نماز ہے اور اوقات مکروہ میں نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ اس لئے اوقات مکروہ میں نماز جنازہ بھی نہ پڑھے (۲) ضروری نوٹ میں مسلم شریف کی حدیث آئی تھی جس کا ایک ٹکڑا تھا او ان نقبر فيهن موتانا حين تطلع الشمس (الف) (مسلم شریف، باب الاوقات التي نہی عن الصلوۃ فیھا ص ۲۷۶ نمبر (۸۳) جس کا ظاہری مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہم ان اوقات میں اپنے مردوں کو دفن نہ کریں۔ لیکن مردوں کو دفن کرنے کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہیں اس لئے اس کا طلب یہی ہوگا کہ جنازہ کی نماز ان اوقات میں نہ پڑھیں ۔ اور سجدہ تلاوت میں بھی سجدہ کرنا نماز کا حصہ ہے اس لئے ان اوقات میں سجدہ تلاوت بھی نہ کرے۔ اثر میں ہے حدثنا ابو تميمة الهجيمي قال لما بعثنا الركب قال ابو داؤد يعنى المدينة قال كنت اقص بعد صلوة الصبح فاسجد فيها فنهانی ابن عمر فلم انته ثلاث مرات ثم عاد فقال اني صليت خلف رسول الله الا الله ومع ابي بكر و عمر و عثمان فلم يسجدوا حتى تطلع الشمس (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من يقرأ السجدة بعد اصبح ص ۲۰۷ نمبر ۱۴۱۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اوقات مکروہ میں سجدہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
اگر اسی اوقات مکروہ ہی میں جنازہ سامنے آیا یا اسی اوقات مکروہ ہی میں آیت سجدہ پڑھی تو چونکہ وقت مکروہ میں یہ ا سبب پیش آیا تو مکروہ اوقات ان کے سبب بنے۔ اس لئے ایسی صورت میں ان مکروہ اوقات میں نماز جنازہ پڑھ سکتا ہے اور سجدہ تلاوت بھی کر سکتا ہے۔ اصول نماز جنازہ جلدی پڑھنے کی تاکید ہے تا کہ مردہ پھول پھٹ نہ جائے اس لئے اوقات مکروہ میں جنازہ آیا تو اس وقت بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن علی بن ابی طالب ان رسول الله الا الله قال لا تؤخروا الجنازة اذا حضرت (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ما جاء في الجنازة لا تؤخروا اذا حضرت ص ۲۱۲، نمبر ۱۴۸۶)
And do not pray over a janazah nor perform sajdah tilawah. (2) And in these prohibited times, one should not pray over a janazah nor perform sajdah tilawah. (1) Janazah prayer is a prayer, and praying in prohibited times is makruh, so janazah prayer should not be performed. (2) In the necessary note, a hadith of Muslim was mentioned: '…and we bury our dead in them at sunrise' (Muslim). Its apparent meaning is that we do not bury our dead at these times. But burying the dead has no meaning; therefore it implies that we do not pray janazah at these times. And sajdah tilawah is a part of prayer, so it should not be performed at these times. There is an athar: Abu Tamimah al-Hujaymi said: When we sent the caravan – Abu Dawood said, meaning to Madinah – he said: I would give a sermon after Fajr prayer and prostrate in it, and Ibn Umar forbade me three times, then said: I prayed behind the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and they did not prostrate until the sun rose. (Abu Dawood). This proves that prostration is not permitted in prohibited times. If a janazah arrives or a verse of prostration is recited during these very prohibited times, then because the cause occurs in the prohibited time, the prohibited time becomes its cause. Thus in such a situation one may pray the janazah and perform sajdah tilawah. The principle is that janazah prayer should be hastened so that the deceased does not swell, so if a janazah comes during prohibited times, it can be performed then. The evidence is the hadith of Ali: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Do not delay the janazah when it is present.' (Ibn Majah).
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding janazah prayer and sajdah tilawah during the prohibited times. The author first states the general rule: these acts are not performed in the three prohibited times because they are forms of prayer, and prayer in those times is makruh. He then supports this with a hadith from Muslim that mentions burying the dead at sunrise, which is interpreted to mean not praying janazah at that time. For sajdah tilawah, an athar from Ibn Umar shows that the Companions did not prostrate after Fajr until sunrise. However, an important exception is made: if the cause (janazah arriving or reciting a verse of sajdah) occurs precisely during the prohibited time, then due to the urgent need, it becomes permissible. For janazah, the principle of hastening the funeral to avoid decomposition overrides the general prohibition. This is supported by the hadith 'Do not delay the janazah'.

Key Terms
جنازہ (janāzah): Funeral prayer; the body of the deceased and the prayer said over it.
سجدہ تلاوت (sajdah tilāwah): Prostration of recitation; performed upon reciting a verse of prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is not permissible under any circumstances.
B) It is permissible because the cause (arrival of janazah) occurs during the prohibited time.
C) It is permissible only if the deceased is a relative.
D) It is permissible only if the janazah is for a child.

Key Takeaway
Janazah prayer and sajdah tilawah are generally prohibited in disliked times, but if the cause (janazah or recitation) occurs within those times, they become permissible due to necessity.

Prohibition of Nafl Prayer After Fajr and Asr
States the ruling and provides brief reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafl prayer after Fajr and Asr, identify the prohibited time periods, and explain the reasoning and evidence.

Core Idea
No voluntary prayer is allowed after Fajr until sunrise or after Asr until sunset.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the prohibition of voluntary (nafl) prayers immediately after the Fajr and Asr obligatory prayers. The text provides both the ruling and a brief reasoning, supported by a Prophetic hadith. Understanding this ruling helps us navigate the recommended times for supererogatory worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that performing nafl prayer after the Fajr prayer until sunrise, and after the Asr prayer until sunset, is 'makruh' (disliked). Determine whether this is prohibitively or mildly disliked.
Hanafi scholars generally consider it makruh tahrimi due to the explicit prohibition.
2
Specify the prohibited time intervals
Note the exact boundaries: after the fard of Fajr until sunrise, and after the fard of Asr until sunset. These are the times when no voluntary prayer should be initiated.
The prohibition applies to any nafl, including sunnah prayers intended as nafl.
3
Understand the reasoning provided
The text explains that occupying oneself with the fard prayer is more virtuous; engaging in nafl immediately afterwards is like preferring a lesser act. Grasp the principle of prioritizing obligatory over voluntary acts.
This reasoning (talil) is used to support the ruling, though the primary evidence is the hadith.
4
Note the hadith evidence
The passage cites a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet forbade prayer after Fajr. Recognize that this is the primary textual evidence (dalil) for the prohibition.
Although the hadith is cut off in the text, its full version is well-known and supports the ruling.
5
Recognize the Hanafi position as mufta bihi
Understand that this ruling is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, with no significant internal disagreement. It is also accepted by other schools with minor differences.
The cross-madhhab status is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon), though details may vary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۷۷] (۳) مکروہ ہے کہ نفل پڑھے فجر کی نماز کے بعد یہاں تک کہ سورج طلوع ہو جائے اور عصر کی نماز کے بعد یہاں تک کہ سورج غروب ہو جائے۔
فجر کے فرض کے بعد طلوع آفتاب تک کوئی نفل نہ پڑھے اسی طرح عصر کے فرض کے بعد غروب آفتاب تک کوئی نفل نہ پڑھے۔ (۱) گویا کہ یہ فرض نماز ہی میں مشغول ہے اس کی فضیلت زیادہ ہوئی۔ اب نفل میں مشغول ہو نا گویا کہ کم درجہ میں مشغول ہونا ہے اس لئے نفل نماز نہ پڑھے (۲) حدیث میں بھی نفل پڑھنے سے منع فرمایا ہے عن ابن عباس ان النبی الله نهي عن الصلوة بعد الصبح
It is makruh to pray nafl after Fajr prayer until the sun rises, and after Asr prayer until the sun sets. Do not pray any nafl after the fard of Fajr until sunrise, and similarly do not pray any nafl after the fard of Asr until sunset. (1) It is as if one is occupied with the fard prayer; its virtue is greater. Occupying oneself with nafl now is like occupying with a lower rank, so one should not pray nafl. (2) The hadith also forbids praying nafl: from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet forbade prayer after Fajr...
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the prohibition of nafl (supererogatory) prayer in two specific periods: after the Fajr prayer until sunrise, and after the Asr prayer until sunset. The author explains the reasoning: the fard prayer (Fajr or Asr) itself has great virtue, and engaging in nafl immediately after would be like preferring a lesser act over a greater one. Additionally, a hadith from Ibn Abbas is cited in which the Prophet explicitly forbade prayer after the Fajr prayer (the text is cut off but it continues with the prohibition). This ruling applies to any non-obligatory prayer, including the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah (which are performed before the fard) and any other nafl.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory, voluntary prayer beyond the obligatory ones.
مکروہ (makrūh): Disliked; in this context, it means prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) to pray any voluntary prayer after the fard of Fajr until sunrise and after the fard of Asr until sunset.

Missed Prayers After Fajr and Asr: Hanafi Exception
Ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on qada in prohibited times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing qada prayers in prohibited times and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position by evaluating the proofs.

Core Idea
Missed obligatory prayers are allowed after Fajr and Asr; regular voluntary prayers are not.

This passage addresses a common question: can one pray after Fajr and Asr? While voluntary (nafl) prayers are generally prohibited in those times, the Hanafi school makes an exception for missed obligatory (fard/wajib) acts, including sajdah tilawah and janazah. The ruling is based on the Prophet's own practice of making up missed prayers, and it contrasts with the Shafi'i view that even regular sunnah prayers are permitted.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the specific acts allowed: any missed fard or wajib prayer, sajdah tilawah, and janazah. Note that regular nafl is excluded.
The word 'fawa'it' refers to missed obligatory/wajib acts.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that even regular sunnah prayers (like the two rak'ahs after Zuhr) may be prayed after Asr, based on Aisha's reports.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Ummah.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Examine the hadith of Aisha: the Prophet never left two rak'ahs after Asr. This seems to show consistent practice.
The Shafi'i interpret this as a regular practice, not qada.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the Prophet's action as qada of a missed sunnah (from Zuhr), not as establishing a new voluntary act. The general prohibition of nafl remains.
The Hanafi rely on the hadith of Umm Salamah where the Prophet explicitly said he was making up for missed Zuhr sunnah.

ولا بأس بان يصلى في هذين الوقتين الفوائت
[۲۷۸] (۴) اور کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے کہ دونوں وقتوں میں فائتہ پڑھے اور سجدہ تلاوت کرے اور جنازہ کی نماز پڑھے۔ (۱) فائنہ نماز جو واجب ہے وہ نفل سے افضل ہے اس لئے فرض نماز میں تقدیری طور پر مشغول رہنا یہ کم درجہ ہے اور حقیقی طور پر مشغول رہنا یہ اعلی درجہ ہے۔ اس لئے واجب میں حقیقی طور پر مشغول ہونا زیادہ بہتر ہوگا اور پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اسی طرح نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہے اس لئے ان کو بھی فجر کے فرض کے بعد اور عصر کے فرض کے بعد ادا کر سکتے ہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ام سلمة صلى النبي بعد العصر ركعتين وقال شغلني ناس من عبد القيس عن الركعتين بعد الظهر (ب) (بخاری شریف، باب ما یصلی بعد العصر من الفوائت ص ۸۳ نمبر ۹۰ ۵ ، مسلم شریف ، باب الاوقات التی نہی عن الصلوۃ فیھا ص ۲۷۷ نمبر ۸۳۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ فائنہ نماز عصر اور فجر کے بعد پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ ظہر کی جوسنت رہ گئی تھی وہ قضا کے طور پر آپ نے پڑھی تھی۔ نانه امام شافعی کے نزدیک عصر کے فرض کے بعد سنت بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عائشة قالت ركعتان لم يكن رسول الله لا يدعهما سرا ولا علانية ركعتان قبل الصبح وركعتان بعد العصر (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب ما یصلی بعد العصر من الفوائت ونحوها ص ۸۳ نمبر ۵۹۲ر مسلم شریف، باب الاوقات التی نہی عن الصلوۃ فیھا ص ۲۷۷ نمبر ۱۹۳۵/۸۳۵) اسی باب کی حدیث میں حضرت عائشہ سے یہ بھی مروی ہے ما کان النبی الا الله يأتيني في يوم بعد العصر الاصلی رکعتین (د) ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۵۹۳ر مسلم شریف نمبر ۸۳۵ ماقبل کا باب ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ آپ عصر کے بعد مسلسل یہ دور کعتیں پڑھا کرتے تھے۔
And there is no harm in performing missed prayers in these two times. (4) There is no harm: one may pray missed prayers in both times, perform the prostration of recitation, and offer the funeral prayer. (1) Because an obligatory prayer is superior to a voluntary one; therefore, engaging in the obligatory prayer in a hypothetical manner (i.e., having missed it) is of a lower degree, while engaging in it actually is of a higher degree. Thus, being actually occupied with the obligatory is better, and one may pray it. Similarly, the funeral prayer and prostration of recitation are obligatory, so they can be performed after the Fajr obligatory prayer and after the Asr obligatory prayer. (2) There is a hadith from Umm Salamah: 'The Prophet prayed two rak'ahs after Asr and said: Some people from Abdul Qais kept me busy from the two rak'ahs after Zuhr.' (Bukhari, Muslim). This hadith indicates that missed prayers can be performed after Asr and Fajr, because the Prophet performed the missed sunnah of Zuhr as qada. But according to Imam Shafi'i, one may even pray voluntary sunnah after Asr. His evidence is the hadith from Aisha: 'The Prophet never left two rak'ahs, in secret or openly: two rak'ahs before Fajr and two rak'ahs after Asr.' (Bukhari, Muslim). Also from Aisha: 'The Prophet never came to me after Asr except he prayed two rak'ahs.' This indicates that he continually prayed these two rak'ahs after Asr.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. The author begins by stating the ruling: it is permissible (la ba'sa) to pray missed (fawa'it) prayers—i.e., obligatory (fard) or wajib prayers that were not performed at their proper times—in the two prohibited times: after Fajr until sunrise, and after Asr until sunset. The commentary explains that this includes any wajib act, such as completing a missed obligatory prayer (fard), performing the prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah), or praying the funeral prayer (janazah). The reasoning is that obligatory acts are superior to voluntary (nafl) ones; thus, occupying oneself with them, even if only in a compensatory sense (taqdiri), is better than purely voluntary acts. The proof is the hadith of Umm Salamah, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed two rak'ahs after Asr and explained that he was performing the missed sunnah of Zuhr. This shows that qada of missed acts is allowed. Then the author presents the Shafi'i position: they argue from Aisha's hadith that even regular voluntary sunnah prayers (like the two rak'ahs often performed after Zuhr) can be prayed after Asr, because the Prophet never abandoned them. The Hanafi response is implicit: the Prophet's action was for qada of a missed sunnah, not for a regular voluntary prayer in that time. Thus, the Hanafi ruling remains that only missed obligatory/wajib prayers are allowed, not new voluntary prayers.

Key Terms
فائتہ (fā'itah): A missed obligatory prayer (fard or wajib) that must be made up (qada).
نفل (nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory prayer. Here distinguished from obligatory/wajib acts.
سجدہ تلاوت (sajdah tilāwah): Prostration of recitation; wajib upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following may be performed after Asr?
A) Regular voluntary (nafl) prayers
B) Missed obligatory (fard) prayers and sajdah tilawah
C) Only funeral prayer, not qada of fard
D) Any sunnah prayer

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, missed obligatory prayers, sajdah tilawah, and janazah are permitted after Fajr and Asr, but regular voluntary prayers are not.

Extra Voluntary Prayers After Fajr Are Makruh
Ruling on extra voluntary prayers after Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing extra voluntary prayers after Fajr, cite the prophetic evidence, and apply it to a real-life scenario.

Core Idea
Extra voluntary prayers after true dawn are makruh; only the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr are allowed.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text addresses a specific time-based ruling: what voluntary prayers are permitted after the onset of Fajr? The answer is clear — only the two sunnah rak'ahs that precede the obligatory prayer. Any additional nafl is disliked (makruh). The proof comes from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ himself. Let's examine the ruling, its evidence, and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling is. The act is ‘praying extra voluntary prayers after true dawn (subh sadiq) beyond the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr’. The ruling is that it is makruh (disliked). In the Hanafi school, this is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked).
Makruh tanzihi means avoiding it is rewarded, but doing it is not sinful.
2
Locate the Dalil (Evidence)
The text cites two hadiths: (1) The practice of the Prophet ﷺ as reported by Hafsah (رضي الله عنها) that he only prayed two light rak'ahs at dawn. (2) The explicit statement of Ibn Umar (رضي الله عنه) that ‘there is no prayer after Fajr except two rak'ahs.’ Both are ahad hadiths (zanni al-thubut).
The hadith from Hafsah is in Muslim; the one from Ibn Umar is in Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (How the Evidence Proves the Ruling)
The Prophet's consistent action (fi'l) of only praying two rak'ahs indicates that additional prayers are not part of his sunnah. The explicit statement provides a general prohibition with an exception for the two rak'ahs. Together, they establish that anything beyond the two sunnah is not allowed — hence disliked.
In Hanafi usul, a general prohibition (nahy) indicates karahah (dislike) unless there is evidence for tahrim (prohibition). Here, the prohibition is understood as makruh tanzihi.
4
Note the Scope and Applicable Time
The ruling applies from the moment of true dawn (subh sadiq) until sunrise. The same ruling applies after Asr prayer until sunset. Within the Fajr time, only the two sunnah and the two fard rak'ahs are to be prayed. Any extra nafl — whether before or after the fard — is makruh.
Some mistakenly think the two sunnah can be prayed after the fard; they must be prayed before.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ویكره ان يتنفل بعد طلوع الفجر باكثر من ركعتي الفجر۔ حتى تشرق الشمس و بعد العصر حتى تغرب
[۲۷۹] (۵) مکروح ہے کہ نفل پڑھے فجر کے طلوع ہونے کے بعد فجر کی دوسنتوں سے زیادہ۔
صبح صادق کے بعد فجر کی دوسنتیں پڑھے اور دو فرض پڑھے۔ اس سے زیادہ سنت پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے عن حفصة قالت كان رسول الله الله الله اذا طلع الفجر لا يصلى الا ركعتين خفيفتين (ه)(مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب رکھتی سیہ الفجر ص ۲۵۰ نمبر ۷۲۳) اور ترندی میں ہے عن ابن عمر ان رسول الله الله قال لا صلوة بعد حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے صبح کے بعد نماز سے روکا یہاں تک کہ سورج طلوع ہو جائے اور عصر کے بعد یہاں تک کہ غروب ہو جائے
And it is disliked to perform voluntary prayer after the break of dawn with more than the two rak'ahs of Fajr, until the sun rises, and after Asr until sunset. (5) It is disliked to pray voluntary prayers after the break of dawn beyond the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr. After true dawn (subh sadiq), one should pray the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr and the two obligatory rak'ahs. Prayer more than that is makruh. Hadith: Hafsah said: 'When dawn broke, the Messenger of Allah would not pray except two light rak'ahs.' (Muslim) And in Tirmidhi from Ibn Umar: 'There is no prayer after Fajr except two rak'ahs.' Footnote (a): He forbade prayer after morning until the sun rises, and after Asr until it sets.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof. It states the ruling: it is makruh (disliked) to perform voluntary (nafl) prayers after true dawn (subh sadiq) beyond the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr. This includes the period from Fajr until sunrise, and similarly after Asr until sunset. The Hanafi school clarifies that the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr are the only voluntary prayer allowed at that time; any additional nafl—whether before or after the Fajr obligatory prayer—is makruh. The proof is from the hadith of Hafsah (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) only prayed two light rak'ahs at dawn, these being the sunnah of Fajr. Another hadith from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) in Tirmidhi explicitly states: 'There is no prayer after Fajr except two rak'ahs.' The footnote (a) reinforces the general prohibition. The rationale is that the time is reserved for the obligatory prayer and its emphasized sunnah; extra worship may cause delay or detract from the fard.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makrūh): Disliked; an act whose avoidance is rewarded but which is not sinful. Here, it is makruh tanzihi (not tahrimi).
صبح صادق (subḥ ṣādiq): True dawn; the time when the horizontal whiteness spreads across the horizon, marking the beginning of Fajr prayer time.
سنن (sunan (pl. sunnah)): Emphasized voluntary prayers; here the two rak'ahs before Fajr are sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on praying four rak'ahs of voluntary prayer after the Fajr obligatory prayer?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Disliked (makruh tanzihi)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended (mustahabb)

Key Takeaway
Extra voluntary prayers after proper Fajr time are only makruh tanzihi, not haram; the evidence restricts it to the two sunnah rak'ahs.

The Hanafi Ruling on Voluntary Prayers Before Maghrib
Ruling and dispute on voluntary prayers before Maghrib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on voluntary prayers before Maghrib, explain the evidence, and contrast it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Praying voluntary before Maghrib is not sunnah; it is better to hasten the fard.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on performing voluntary (nafl) prayers after the adhan of Maghrib and before the obligatory prayer. While there are reports of the Prophet praying two rak'ahs at that time, the Hanafi school counsels against it to avoid delaying the fard. We will explore the evidence and the differing view of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and Hanafi ruling
State what the passage rules regarding praying two rak'ahs before Maghrib. The Hanafi position: it is better not to pray, but if prayed, it is not sinful.
The act is voluntary (nafl) prayer before fard Maghrib.
2
Examine the Hanafi proofs
Look at the hadith of Ibn Umar (no practice in Prophet's time) and the hadith of Buraidah (exception for Maghrib). Also the hadith of Jibril emphasizing haste.
These indicate the practice was not sunnah and that delaying is discouraged.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Consider the hadith of Abdullah al-Muzani where the Prophet said 'Pray two rak'ahs before Maghrib' but then added 'for whosoever wishes'.
Shafi'i takes 'pray' as a recommendation; Hanafi focuses on the qualification.
4
Understand the Hanafi reconciliation
The Prophet's addition 'for whosoever wishes' shows optionality, not sunnah. The practice was inconsistent, and the overriding principle is to hasten the fard.
Hence, it is nafl, not sunnah mu'akkadah.
5
State the practical consequence
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi says praying these rak'ahs is makruh tanzihi if it delays fard; Shafi'i says it is sunnah and recommended.
The difference affects daily practice: Hanafi scholars advise skipping it; Shafi'i encourage it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولایتتنفل قبل المغرب
[۲۸۰] (۶) مغرب کے فرض سے پہلے نفل نہ پڑھے۔
مغرب کی اذان کے بعد فرض سے پہلے دو رکعت نفل پڑھنا ثابت ہے لیکن حنفیہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نہ پڑھے تو اچھا ہے۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ فرض پڑھنے میں تاخیر ہوگی اور حدیث جبرئیل میں گزرا کہ دونوں دنوں میں مغرب کی نماز جلدی پڑھی۔ اس لئے مغرب کا فرض جلدی پڑھنا چاہئے (۲) سئل ابن عمر عن الركعتين قبل المغرب فقال ما رأيت احدا على عهد رسول الله يصليهما (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الصلوة قبل المغرب ص ۱۸۹ نمبر ۱۲۸۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور کے زمانے میں مغرب کے فرض سے پہلے دو رکعت سنتوں کا خاص رواج نہیں تھا (۳) حدثنا عبد الله بن بريدة عن ابيه قال قال رسول الله ان عند كل اذانين ركعتين ما خلا صلوة المغرب (ج) (دار قطنی ، باب الحث علی الرکوع بین الاذانین ج اول ص ۲۷۲ نمبر ۱۰۲۸) اسے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مغرب کے فرض سے پہلے سنت نہیں ہے۔
فائده امام شافعی کے نزدیک مغرب کے فرض سے پہلے دو رکعت سنت ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبد الله المزني قال قال رسول الله صلوا قبل المغرب ركعتين ثم قال صلوا قبل المغرب ركعتين لمن شاء خشية ان يتخذها الناس سنة (و) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوة قبل المغرب ص ۱۸۹ نمبر ۱۲۸۱ / بخاری شریف، باب الصلوة قبل المغرب ص ۱۵۷ نمبر ۱۱۸۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مغرب کے فرض سے پہلے سنت ہے۔ اس حدیث کی بنا پر حنفیہ کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی سنت پڑھ لے تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ طریقہ حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ سنت نہیں ہے نفل ہے۔
And he should not perform voluntary prayer before Maghrib. (6) He should not pray voluntary prayer before the obligatory Maghrib prayer. After the adhan of Maghrib, before the fard, performing two rak'ahs of nafl is reported, but the Hanafis say it is better not to pray. The reason is that it would delay the fard, and in the hadith of Jibril, it is mentioned that on both days Maghrib was prayed early. Therefore, the fard of Maghrib should be prayed quickly. (2) Ibn Umar was asked about the two rak'ahs before Maghrib; he said: 'I have not seen anyone in the time of the Messenger of Allah praying them.' (Abu Dawud). This shows that there was no common practice of two sunnah rak'ahs before Maghrib. (3) Abdullah ibn Buraidah narrated from his father that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Between every two adhans (i.e., adhan and iqamah) there are two rak'ahs, except for the Maghrib prayer.' (Dar Qutni). This also indicates that there is no sunnah before Maghrib. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i, the two rak'ahs before Maghrib are sunnah. His evidence is the hadith of Abdullah al-Muzani: 'Pray two rak'ahs before Maghrib, then he said: Pray two rak'ahs before Maghrib for whosoever wishes, fearing that people would take it as a sunnah.' (Abu Dawud, Bukhari). Based on this hadith, the Hanafis hold that if someone prays it, it is not makruh. The manner of the hadith also indicates that it is not sunnah but nafl.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an inter-madhhab dispute. The ruling: 'He should not perform voluntary prayer before Maghrib.' The Hanafi position is that it is better not to pray any voluntary (nafl) prayer after the adhan of Maghrib and before the obligatory prayer. Though there are reports of the Prophet (peace be upon him) praying two rak'ahs before Maghrib, the Hanafi school discourages this because the Prophet Jibril (peace be upon him) hastened the Maghrib prayer; delaying the fard for nafl is not preferred. Evidence from Ibn Umar indicates that this practice was not common in the Prophet's time. The hadith of Buraidah explicitly excludes Maghrib from the general recommendation of two rak'ahs between adhan and iqamah. However, Imam al-Shafi'i considers it a sunnah based on the Prophet's instruction to pray two rak'ahs before Maghrib, though the Prophet qualified it with 'for whosoever wishes' to prevent it from being taken as an obligatory sunnah. The Hanafi reconciliation: the act is not sunnah mu'akkadah, but merely permissible (nafl). Therefore, if someone prays it, it is not makruh, but it is better to omit it to hasten the fard. This is a example of istihsan (preferring the stronger evidence and the spirit of hastening the fard).

Key Terms
مغرب (maghrib): Sunset; the fourth daily prayer, performed immediately after sunset.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary prayer; here distinguished from sunnah mu'akkadah. Nafl is less emphasized than sunnah.
سنت (sunnah): The regular practice of the Prophet. Here, the dispute is whether the two rak'ahs before Maghrib are sunnah (emphasized) or merely nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the two rak'ahs before Maghrib?
A) It is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah)
B) It is forbidden (haram)
C) It is better to omit them, but if prayed, it is not makruh
D) It is obligatory (wajib)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school discourages voluntary prayer before Maghrib to avoid delaying the fard, but if performed, it is not sinful.

The Twelve Emphasized Sunnah Rak'ahs
Defines nawafil and cites hadith for twelve sunnah rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of nawafil as used in the Hanafi school, enumerate the twelve sunnah mu'akkadah rak'ahs, and explain why they are classified as such based on the Prophet's consistent practice.

Core Idea
The twelve rak'ahs that the Prophet consistently prayed daily are sunnah mu'akkadah, establishing their emphasized status.

This lesson opens the chapter on nawafil by clarifying a key terminological point: in Hanafi fiqh, 'nawafil' broadly includes both sunnah (emphasized voluntary prayers) and nafl (general supererogatory prayers). The author then provides the foundational hadith evidence from Aisha (رضي الله عنها) describing the Prophet's daily supererogatory prayer routine, which totals twelve rak'ahs. Understanding this definition and the supporting proof is essential before studying the detailed rulings of these prayers.

Guided Path
1
Define 'nawafil' in context
The passage states that nawafil means any prayer other than fard, and in this chapter it includes both sunnah and nafl. Note this broad definition to avoid later confusion.
Hanafis sometimes differentiate 'sunnah' (emphasized) from 'nafl' (non-emphasized), but here they are grouped.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
Identify the hadith of Aisha (رضي الله عنها) as the proof. It describes the Prophet's daily supererogatory prayers: before and after each obligatory prayer, plus two before Fajr.
The hadith is reported in Muslim, Abu Dawood, and Tirmidhi.
3
Enumerate the twelve rak'ahs
List them: 4 before Zuhr, 2 after Zuhr, 2 after Maghrib, 2 after Isha, 2 before Fajr. Total = 12.
Some transmissions include 2 after Jumu'ah, but those are not in this hadith.
4
Classify the ruling
Because the Prophet consistently performed these prayers and rarely omitted them, they are classified as sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). In Hanafi fiqh, omitting them is makruh tanzih.
The dalil's zanni thubut and dalala support the sunnah status, not wajib.

باب النوافل
ضروری نوٹ النوافل سے مراد فرض کے علاوہ نماز ہے۔ یہاں نوافل میں سنت اور نوافل دونوں شامل ہیں۔ دلیل یہ حدیث ہے سألت" عائشة عن صلوة رسول الله علي الله عن تطوعه ؟ فقالت كان يصلي في بيتي قبل الظهر اربعا ثم يخرج فيصلي بالناس ثم يدخل فيصلى ركعتين وكان يصلى بالناس المغرب ثم يدخل فیصلي ركعتين ويصلي بالناس العشاء و يدخل بیتی فیصلى ركعتين ... وكان اذا طلع الفجر صلی رکعتین (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب جواز النافلة قائما وقاعداص۲۵۲ نمبر ۷۳۰ ابوداؤد شریف، ابواب التطوع وركعات النبی ص ۱۸۵ نمبر ۱۲۵ ارترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی من صلى في يوم وليلة مثنتى عشرة ركعة من السنتة ماله من الفضل ص ۹۴ نمبر ۴۱۴ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ فرض نماز سے پہلے اور فرض نماز کے بعد پورے دن اور رات میں سنت مؤکدہ ہیں اور وہ بارہ رکعتیں ہیں۔ ان کی تاکید آئی ہے۔
Chapter of Nawafil. Necessary Note: By nawafil is meant prayer other than fard. Here, nawafil include both sunnah and nafl. The evidence is the hadith: 'I asked Aisha about the voluntary prayer of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ). She said: He used to pray in my house four rak'ahs before Zuhr, then go out and lead the people in prayer, then enter and pray two rak'ahs. He would lead the people in Maghrib, then enter and pray two rak'ahs. He would lead the people in Isha, then enter my house and pray two rak'ahs... And when dawn broke, he would pray two rak'ahs.' (Muslim, Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi). From this hadith, it is understood that before and after the obligatory prayers throughout the day and night, there are emphasized sunnahs, and they are twelve rak'ahs. Their emphasis is established.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a definition and introductory note for the chapter on nawafil. The author clarifies that the term 'nawafil' in this context refers to any prayer that is not obligatory (fard). It includes both sunnah (emphasized voluntary prayers) and nafl (general supererogatory prayers). The evidence for the specific sunnah prayers that the Prophet (ﷺ) consistently performed is the famous hadith of Aisha (رضي الله عنها), which describes the Prophet's daily routine of supererogatory prayers. The hadith enumerates: four rak'ahs before Zuhr, two after Zuhr, two after Maghrib, two after Isha, and two before Fajr, totaling twelve rak'ahs. The note emphasizes that these are sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnahs) because of the Prophet's continual practice. This sets the stage for the detailed rulings that follow in the chapter.

Key Terms
نوافل (nawafil): Non-obligatory prayers, including both sunnah and nafl.
سنت مؤکدہ (sunnah mu'akkadah): Emphasized sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and rarely omitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the note, what is the total number of emphasized sunnah rak'ahs mentioned in the hadith of Aisha?
A) 10
B) 12
C) 14
D) 8

Key Takeaway
The twelve rak'ahs that the Prophet (ﷺ) consistently performed each day are sunnah mu'akkadah, and they form the basis of the Hanafi ruling on emphasized supererogatory prayers.

The Emphasized Sunnah of Fajr
Establishes the two rak'ahs before Fajr as an emphasized sunnah based on the Prophet's diligence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of the two rak'ahs before Fajr as sunnah mu'akkadah and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The Prophet's greatest consistency in nawafil was the two rak'ahs of Fajr, making them an emphasized sunnah.

The Fajr prayer is preceded by two rak'ahs that the Prophet (ﷺ) never neglected. This lesson examines the textual proof that raises this sunnah above ordinary nafl, establishing it as a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized) that every Muslim should strive to maintain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the sunnah in prayer is to pray two rak'ahs after dawn. Determine the legal category: sunnah mu'akkadah, not just nafl.
The Arabic term 'السنة في الصلوة' refers to the established practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Aisha (رضي الله عنها) is cited. Identify it as a hadith from Bukhari and Muslim, and note that it is a direct evidence for the ruling.
The hadith is ṣaḥīḥ (authentic) and is used by all schools.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase 'اشد تعاهدا' (more diligent) indicates the Prophet's extraordinary care for this prayer over other nawafil. This is the proof of emphasis.
The comparative 'اشد' (more) shows a higher degree of consistency.
4
Derive the sunnah category
Because the Prophet was most diligent, this sunnah is classified as mu'akkadah (emphasized). In Hanafi fiqh, omitting it without excuse is makruh tanzih.
Emphasized sunnahs are those the Prophet rarely left.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۱] (۱) السنة في الصلوة ان يصلى ركعتين بعد طلوع الفجر
حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة قالت لم يكن النبى الله على شيء من النوافل اشد تعاهدا منه على ركعتي الفجر (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب تعاهد رکھتی الفجر ص ۱۵۶ نمبر ۱۱۶۹ار مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب رکھتی سنته الفجر ص۲۵۰ نمبر ۱۶۸۶/۷۲۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سنت فجر سنت مؤکدہ ہے۔ کیونکہ آپ اس کی بہت تاکید فرماتے تھے۔
[281] (1) The sunnah regarding prayer is to pray two rak'ahs after the rising of dawn. There is a hadith from Aisha (رضي الله عنها) who said: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) was not more diligent in any of the nawafil than he was regarding the two rak'ahs of Fajr.' (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith, it is understood that the sunnah of Fajr is a strongly emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), because the Prophet (ﷺ) stressed it greatly.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the two rak'ahs before the Fajr obligatory prayer. The matn states that the sunnah in prayer is to pray two rak'ahs after the true dawn (i.e., before the fard of Fajr). The commentary presents a hadith from Aisha (رضي الله عنها) that the Prophet (ﷺ) was more diligent in maintaining the two rak'ahs of Fajr than any other supererogatory prayer. This indicates that this sunnah is the most emphasized among the nawafil, making it a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). The ruling is clear: these two rak'ahs are a confirmed sunnah, and the Prophet's practice shows that they should not be neglected.

Key Terms
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of emphasized sunnah prayed after the true dawn and before the Fajr fard.
مؤکدہ (mu'akkadah): Emphasized; a sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and urged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is the longest prayer.
B) The Prophet was most diligent in it.
C) It is obligatory.
D) It can only be prayed at home.

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs before Fajr are sunnah mu'akkadah based on the Prophet's exceptional diligence.
