Sunnah Before and After Zuhr: Four and Two Rak'ahs
Establishes the four rak'ahs before Zuhr and two after as sunnah mu'akkadah based on the Prophet's practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of sunnah rak'ahs before and after Zuhr according to the Hanafi school and identify the hadith evidence proving their sunnah mu'akkadah status.

Core Idea
The Prophet never abandoned four rak'ahs before Zuhr, making them an emphasized sunnah.

Many Muslims know that there are sunnah prayers associated with Zuhr, but confusion can arise regarding the exact number before Zuhr. Some narrations mention two, while others mention four. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position based on the most authentic reports, showing that the complete sunnah mu'akkadah before Zuhr is four rak'ahs and after Zuhr is two rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the ruling in the matn
The matn states 'and four before Zuhr and two after' – this is the concise ruling for the sunnah prayers associated with Zuhr.
The matn does not mention the full context; the commentary provides the proof.
2
Examine the first hadith evidence
The hadith from Aisha reports that the Prophet 'never left four before Zuhr and two before Fajr.' The phrase 'never left' indicates constancy, making it a sunnah mu'akkadah.
This hadith is from Bukhari (no. 1182).
3
Examine the second hadith evidence
Ibn Umar reports memorizing ten rak'ahs from the Prophet, which includes two before Zuhr and two after Zuhr. This seems to conflict with the four before Zuhr in Aisha's hadith.
This hadith is from Bukhari (no. 1180) and Abu Dawood (no. 1269).
4
Reconcile the two hadith
The Hanafi school reconciles by taking Aisha's report as the complete sunnah mu'akkadah (four) and Ibn Umar's as the minimal or another occasion. The four rak'ahs are prayed as two pairs.
Imam Tahawi reconciles similarly.
5
State the Hanafi position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that four rak'ahs before Zuhr and two after Zuhr are sunnah mu'akkadah. This applies to every Muslim praying Zuhr.
Omitting these sunnahs is makruh tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۲] (۲) واربعا قبل الظهر...
عن عائشة ان النبي عل الله كان لا يدع اربعا قبل الظهر وركعتين قبل الغداة (بخاری شریف نمبر ۱۱۸۲) دوسری حدیث میں صلى الله ہے عن ابن عمر قال حفظت من النبى له عشر ركعات ، ركتين قبل الظهرو ركعتين بعدها وركعتين بعد المغرب في بيته و ركعتين بعد العشاء في بيته وركعتين قبل صلوة الصبح (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب رکعتین قبل الظهر ص ۱۵۷ نمبر ۱۱۸۰ر ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الا ربع قبل الظہر و بعدها ص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۲۶۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ظہر سے پہلے چار اور اس کے بعد دو
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عائشہ سے حضور سے نقل کے بارے میں پوچھا تو انہوں نے فرمایا کہ آپ میرے گھر میں ظہر سے پہلے چار رکعت پڑھتے پھر نکلتے اور لوگوں کو نماز پڑھاتے۔ پھر گھر میں داخل ہوتے تو دورکعت نماز پڑھتے ۔ اور لوگوں کو مغرب کی نماز پڑھاتے پھر داخل ہوتے اور دورکعت نماز پڑھتے ۔ اور عشا کی نماز لوگوں کو پڑھاتے اور میرے گھر میں داخل ہوتے تو دورکعت نماز پڑھتے ... جب فجر طلوع ہوتی تو دورکعت پڑھتے (ب) حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ نوافل میں سے کسی پر اتنی تاکید نہیں فرماتے جتنی فجر کی دو رکعتوں پر فرماتے (ج) آپ چار رکعت ظہر سے پہلے اور دو رکعت فجر سے پہلے نہیں چھوڑتے ۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ ابن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے حضور سے دس رکعتیں یاد کی ہیں۔ دورکعت ظہر سے پہلے ، دواس کے بعد، دو مغرب کے بعد ان کے گھر میں ، دوعشا کے بعد ان کے گھر میں اور دور کعتیں صبح کی نماز سے پہلے۔
[282] (2) And four before Zuhr... On the authority of Aisha that the Prophet (ﷺ) never left four before Zuhr and two before Fajr (Bukhari no. 1182). In another hadith, Ibn Umar said: I memorized from the Prophet (ﷺ) ten rak'ahs: two before Zuhr, two after it, two after Maghrib in his house, two after Isha in his house, and two before the morning prayer. (Bukhari, Abu Dawood). From these hadith, it is understood that (the sunnah) before Zuhr is four and after it two. Footnote: (a) Aisha was asked about the Prophet's voluntary prayers... (b) Aisha said that the Prophet was not more diligent in any nawafil than the two rak'ahs of Fajr. (c) He never left four before Zuhr and two before Fajr. In another hadith, Ibn Umar said: I memorized ten rak'ahs from the Prophet: two before Zuhr, two after, two after Maghrib in his house, two after Isha in his house, and two before the morning prayer.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling with proof for the sunnah prayers associated with Zuhr. The matn states 'and four before Zuhr...' indicating that the emphasized sunnah before Zuhr is four rak'ahs, and after Zuhr it is two rak'ahs. Two hadith are cited as evidence. The first, from Aisha (رضي الله عنها), mentions that the Prophet never omitted four rak'ahs before Zuhr and two before Fajr. The second, from Ibn Umar (رضي الله عنه), lists the ten rak'ahs he memorized from the Prophet, which include two before Zuhr, two after Zuhr, two after Maghrib, two after Isha, and two before Fajr. However, note that the first hadith mentions four before Zuhr, while the second mentions two. The commentator clarifies that the four before Zuhr are the sunnah mu'akkadah, and the two mentioned in Ibn Umar's hadith likely refer to a lighter practice or that the four include the two emphasized ones. The Hanafi position is that the sunnah before Zuhr is four rak'ahs (prayed in two pairs) and after Zuhr it is two rak'ahs. The footnote provides additional context from the hadith of Aisha, emphasizing that these were part of the Prophet's consistent practice.

Key Terms
ظهر (zuhr): The midday obligatory prayer, consisting of four rak'ahs.
سنت مؤکدہ (sunnah mu'akkadah): Emphasized sunnah that the Prophet performed consistently and rarely omitted.
اربعا (arba'a): Four, as in the number of rak'ahs before Zuhr.
ركعة (rak'ah): Unit of prayer consisting of standing, bowing, prostrating, and sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Two
B) Four
C) Six
D) None

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the sunnah mu'akkadah before Zuhr is four rak'ahs and after Zuhr is two, based on the Prophet's consistent practice as reported by Aisha.

The Regular Voluntary Prayers (Sunnan Rawatib)
Listing the sunnah prayers and their evidence from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the twelve rak'ahs of sunnah mu'akkadah and explain the evidence from hadith for each prayer time.

Core Idea
The Prophet's consistent practice establishes twelve rak'ahs as emphasized sunnah for every day.

This passage introduces the regular voluntary prayers (nawafil) that accompany the five obligatory prayers. It clarifies that 'nawafil' includes both emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) and non-emphasized nafl, and provides the primary hadith evidence from Aisha describing the Prophet's daily practice. The author then details each prayer time, explaining which rak'ahs are sunnah mu'akkadah and which are optional, based on multiple hadiths. As we go through, pay attention to how Hanafi fiqh uses the Prophet's actions (fi'l) as proof and how apparent contradictions between hadiths are harmonized.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what each prayer time's voluntary prayer is (number of rak'ahs) and whether it is sunnah mu'akkadah or ghayr mu'akkadah.
The general ruling is that the twelve rak'ahs (2 Fajr, 4 before Zuhr, 2 after Zuhr, 2 after Maghrib, 2 after Isha) are sunnah mu'akkadah. Asr and additional Isha prayers are optional.
2
Locate the dalil for each
For each prayer time, find the hadith cited as evidence. The main dalil is the hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's practice. Additional hadiths are given for specific times (e.g., Fajr sunnah emphasis, four after Zuhr).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how each hadith proves the ruling. For example, the Prophet's continuous action (fi'l) indicates sunnah mu'akkadah according to Hanafi usul.
4
Note the flexibility
Observe where the author allows alternatives (e.g., two or four before Asr, two or four after Isha). This shows how different hadiths are harmonized without conflict.
This flexibility reflects that some sunnahs are not as strongly emphasized.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify which ruling is the operative one for practice. For example, the twelve rak'ahs are the relied-upon sunnah mu'akkadah, while for Zuhr after, the practice is two sunnah then two nafl.

باب النوافل

ضروری نوٹ النوافل سے مراد فرض کے علاوہ نماز ہے۔ یہاں نوافل میں سنت اور نوافل دونوں شامل ہیں۔ دلیل یہ حدیث ہے سألت عائشة عن صلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن تطوعه ؟ فقالت كان يصلي في بيتي قبل الظهر اربعا ثم يخرج فيصلي بالناس ثم يدخل فيصلى ركعتين وكان يصلى بالناس المغرب ثم يدخل فیصلي ركعتين ويصلي بالناس العشاء و يدخل بیتی فیصلى ركعتين ... وكان اذا طلع الفجر صلی رکعتین (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب جواز النافلة قائما وقاعداص۲۵۲ نمبر ۷۳۰ ابوداؤد شریف، ابواب التطوع وركعات النبی ص ۱۸۵ نمبر ۱۲۵ ارترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی من صلى في يوم وليلة مثنتى عشرة ركعة من السنتة ماله من الفضل ص ۹۴ نمبر ۴۱۴ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ فرض نماز سے پہلے اور فرض نماز کے بعد پورے دن اور رات میں سنت مؤکدہ ہیں اور وہ بارہ رکعتیں ہیں۔ ان کی تاکید آئی ہے۔

[۲۸۱] (۱) سنت نماز میں یہ ہے کہ دور کعتیں طلوع فجر کے بعد پڑھے۔
حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة قالت لم يكن النبى صلى الله عليه على شيء من النوافل اشد تعاهدا منه على ركعتي الفجر (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب تعاهد رکھتی الفجر ص ۱۵۶ نمبر ۱۱۶۹ار مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب رکھتی سنته الفجر ص۲۵۰ نمبر ۱۶۸۶/۷۲۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سنت فجر سنت مؤکدہ ہے۔ کیونکہ آپ اس کی بہت تاکید فرماتے تھے۔

[۲۸۲] (۲) ظہر سے پہلے چار رکعتیں اور ظہر کے بعد دو رکعتیں سنت ہیں۔
عن عائشة ان النبي صلى الله عليه كان لا يدع اربعا قبل الظهر وركعتين قبل الغداة (بخاری شریف نمبر ۱۱۸۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر قال حفظت من النبى له عشر ركعات ، ركتين قبل الظهرو ركعتين بعدها وركعتين بعد المغرب في بيته و ركعتين بعد العشاء في بيته وركعتين قبل صلوة الصبح (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب رکعتین قبل الظهر ص ۱۵۷ نمبر ۱۱۸۰ر ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الا ربع قبل الظہر و بعدها ص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۲۶۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ظہر سے پہلے چار اور اس کے بعد دو رکعتیں سنت ہیں۔ اور ایک حدیث میں ظہر کے بعد بھی چار رکعت سنت کی حدیث ہے۔ قالت ام حبيبة قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه من حافظ على اربع ركعات قبل الظهر واربع بعدها حرم على النار (الف) (ابوداود شریف، باب الا ربع قبل الظهر وبعدهاص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۲۶۹ ترندی شریف، باب آخر ( باب ماجاء فی الرکعتین بعد الظبر ص ۹۸ نمبر ۴۲۷) اس حدیث کی بنا پر اور اوپر کی حدیث کی بنا پر ظہر کے بعد چار رکعتیں سنت ہیں۔ اسی لئے یہ عمل ہے کہ دورکعت سنت کی نیت سے پڑھتے ہیں۔ پھر دو رکعت نفل کی نیت سے پڑھتے ہیں۔

[۲۸۳] (۳) عصر سے پہلے چار رکعت اور چاہے تو دور کعتیں پڑھے۔
عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه رحم الله امرء صلى قبل العصر اربعا (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوۃ قبل العصر ص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۳۷۱/ ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الا ربع قبل العصر ص ۹۸ نمبر ۴۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عصر سے پہلے چار رکعت سنت ہیں۔ لیکن دوسری حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ دور کعتیں سنت ہیں۔ حدیث میں ہے عن على ان النبي صلى الله عليه كان يصلي قبل العصر ركعتين (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوۃ قبل العصرص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۳۷۲ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الا ربع قبل العصرص ۹۸ نمبر ۴۲۹) اس حدیث کی بنا پر صاحب کتاب نے فرمایا کہ عصر کی سنت دو رکعت بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے۔

[۲۸۴] (۴) مغرب کے بعد دورکعتیں ہیں۔
اس کی وجہ کئی حدیث میں اوپر گزرگئی ہے (مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلته قائماص۲۵۲نمبر ۷۳۰ )

[۲۸۵] (۵) اور عشا سے پہلے چار رکعت اور اس کے بعد چار رکعت اور چاہے تو دورکعت سنت پڑھے۔ عشا کے بعد دو رکعت کی تو کئی حدیثیں گزرگئی ہیں۔ اور عشا کے بعد چار رکعت سنت پڑھنے کی حدیث یہ ہے عن عائشة قال سألتها عن صلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه فقالت ما صلى رسول الله العشاء قط فدخل على الاصلی اربع رکعات او ست رکعات (د) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الصلوۃ بعد العشاء ص۹۲ نمبر ۱۳۰۳ رسن للبیھقی ، باب من جعل بعد العشاء اربع رکعات اوا کثرج ثانی ص ۶۷۱، نمبر ۴۵۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عشا کے بعد چار رکعت سنت ہے۔ اور ضروری نوٹ کے تحت لمبی حدیث گزری جس میں تھا کہ ويصلي بالناس العشاء و يدخل بيتي فيصلي ركعتين (ه) ( مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلة قائما و قاعد اص۲۵۲، نمبر ۷۳۰ را بو داؤد شریف ، ابواب التطوع و رکعات السنتر ص ۱۸۵، نمبر (۱۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عشا کے بعد دو رکعت سنت ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں
Chapter of Voluntary Prayers. Important note: Nawafil refers to prayers other than fard. Here, nawafil includes both sunnah and nafil. Evidence is this hadith: I asked Aisha about the voluntary prayer of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. She said: He used to pray in my house four rak'ahs before Zuhr, then go out and lead the people in prayer, then enter and pray two rak'ahs. He would lead the people in Maghrib, then enter and pray two rak'ahs. He would lead the people in Isha, and enter my house and pray two rak'ahs... And when dawn broke, he would pray two rak'ahs. (Muslim, etc.) From this hadith it is understood that before and after the obligatory prayers throughout the day and night, there are emphasized sunnahs, and they are twelve rak'ahs. Their emphasis has come. [281] (1) It is sunnah in prayer to pray two rak'ahs after dawn. A hadith: Aisha said: The Prophet did not emphasize any voluntary prayer as much as he emphasized the two rak'ahs of Fajr. (Bukhari, Muslim) From this hadith it is understood that the Fajr sunnah is an emphasized sunnah, because he emphasized it greatly. [282] (2) Four rak'ahs before Zuhr and two after Zuhr are sunnah. From Aisha: The Prophet never left four before Zuhr and two before Fajr. (Bukhari) Another hadith: Ibn Umar said: I memorized ten rak'ahs from the Prophet: two before Zuhr, two after Zuhr, two after Maghrib in his house, two after Isha in his house, and two before Fajr prayer. (Bukhari, etc.) From this hadith it is understood that four before Zuhr and two after are sunnah. Also, a hadith about four after Zuhr: Umm Habiba said: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever preserves four rak'ahs before Zuhr and four after, Allah makes him forbidden to the Fire. (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi) Based on this and the earlier hadith, four after Zuhr are sunnah. Therefore the practice is to pray two with the intention of sunnah and then two with the intention of nafil. [283] (3) Four rak'ahs before Asr, or if he wishes, two. Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah said: May Allah have mercy on a person who prays four before Asr. (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi) From this it is understood that four before Asr are sunnah. But another hadith shows two: Ali said: The Prophet used to pray two rak'ahs before Asr. (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi) Based on this, the author said that one may also pray two as the sunnah of Asr. [284] (4) Two rak'ahs after Maghrib. The evidence for this has passed in several hadith above (Muslim). [285] (5) Four rak'ahs before Isha and four after, and if he wishes, two. For two after Isha, several hadith have passed. For four after Isha, this hadith: I asked Aisha about the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. She said: The Messenger of Allah never prayed Isha and then came to me except that he prayed four or six rak'ahs. (Abu Dawood, Bayhaqi) From this it is understood that four after Isha are sunnah. And under the important note, a long hadith passed which said: He would lead the people in Isha, then enter my house and pray two rak'ahs. (Muslim, Abu Dawood) From this it is understood that two after Isha are sunnah. Therefore both are permissible.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from the commentary expands upon the chapter of voluntary prayers (nawafil) by listing the regular sunnah prayers (sunnan rawatib) associated with the five daily obligatory prayers. The author begins with a crucial note: 'nawafil' here includes both the emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) and the non-emphasized supererogatory prayers (nafl). The evidence for the twelve-rak'ah regular sunnah is the famous hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's practice in her house. Then, the passage systematically covers each prayer time. For Fajr, the two rak'ahs are strongly emphasized (sunnah mu'akkadah), based on the Prophet's particular care for them. For Zuhr, the sunnah is four before and two after, but the hadith of Umm Habiba supports four after as well, leading to the Hanafi practice of praying two as sunnah and two as nafl to combine both evidences. For Asr, there are two opinions: four or two rak'ahs; the author allows either, reflecting the flexibility in the school. For Maghrib, the two rak'ahs after are firmly established. For Isha, both two and four are reported, so the Hanafi position is to allow either, though the regular sunnah is two. The passage does not address the four before Isha as mu'akkadah, but notes its virtue. Overall, this commentary shows how Hanafi fiqh derives rulings from multiple hadith and harmonizes apparent contradictions through the practice of the early Muslims.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and sometimes praised; omission is disliked (makruh tanzih) but not sinful.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary prayer that is not emphasized; may be performed with a separate intention from sunnah.
نوافل (nawafil): General term for all non-obligatory prayers, including both sunnah and nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many rak'ahs are considered the regular emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) for Zuhr according to the passage?
A) Two before and two after
B) Four before and two after
C) Four before and four after
D) Two before and four after

Key Takeaway
The regular voluntary prayers (sunnan rawatib) consist of twelve emphasized rak'ahs spread across the five daily prayers, established by the Prophet's consistent practice.

Sunnah Prayers of Zuhr and Asr: Combining Hadith
Rulings on sunnah rak'at with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of sunnah rak'at before and after Zuhr and Asr according to the Hanafi school, and explain how the school reconciles conflicting hadith.

Core Idea
Hanafi sunnah for Zuhr and Asr combines multiple Prophetic practices, not one hadith alone.

The sunnah prayers (rawatib) are an integral part of a Muslim's daily worship, but the exact number of rak'at for Zuhr and Asr can be confusing due to varying hadith. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling from the matn and its commentary, showing how scholars reconciled the texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling from the matn
The matn states: 'Zuhr and two rak'at after it, and four before Asr, and if he wishes two rak'at.' Note the initial numbers given for each prayer.
The matn provides the minimal sunnah, but the commentary expands.
2
Examine the hadith proofs cited
Two hadith are cited: (1) Umm Habiba's hadith promising protection from Fire for four before and after Zuhr; (2) Ibn Umar's hadith recommending four before Asr, and Ali's hadith showing the Prophet prayed two before Asr. Locate these in the passage.
These are ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut), so they indicate sunnah, not obligation.
3
Trace the Hanafi method of reconciliation
For Zuhr, the commentary combines the two-rak'at matn with the four-rak'at hadith by praying two rak'at as sunnah and two as nafl. For Asr, the author allows either two or four, showing the preferred view is two.
This is a practical reconciliation: the intention distinguishes sunnah from nafl.
4
Apply the ruling to daily practice
After Zuhr fard, pray two rak'at sunnah then two rak'at nafl. Before Asr, pray either two or four rak'at sunnah, though two is preferred.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is to pray two sunnah before Asr as per the author's preference.

الظهر وركعتين بـعـدهـا [۲۸۳](۳) واربعا قبل العصر وان شاء ركعتين [۲۸۴](۴) وركعتين بعد المغرب [۲۸۵] (۵) واربعا قبل العشاء و بعدها اربعا وان شاء ركعتين. رکعتیں سنت ہیں۔ اور ایک حدیث میں ظہر کے بعد بھی چار رکعت سنت کی حدیث ہے۔ قالت ام حبيبة قال رسول الله له من حافظ على اربع ركعات قبل الظهر واربع بعدها حرم على النار (الف) (ابوداود شریف، باب الا ربع قبل الظهر وبعدهاص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۲۶۹ ترندی شریف، باب آخر ( باب ماجاء فی الرکعتین بعد الظبر ص ۹۸ نمبر ۴۲۷) اس حدیث کی بنا پر اور اوپر کی حدیث کی بنا پر ظہر کے بعد چار رکعتیں سنت ہیں۔ اسی لئے یہ عمل ہے کہ دورکعت سنت کی نیت سے پڑھتے ہیں۔ پھر دو رکعت نفل کی نیت سے پڑھتے ہیں۔ (۲۸۳) (۳) عصر سے پہلے چار رکعت اور چاہے تو دور کعتیں پڑھے۔ عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله الله رحم الله امرء صلى قبل العصر اربعا (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوۃ قبل العصر ص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۳۷۱/ ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الا ربع قبل العصر ص ۹۸ نمبر ۴۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عصر سے پہلے چار رکعت سنت ہیں۔ لیکن دوسری حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ دور کعتیں سنت ہیں۔ حدیث میں ہے عن على ان النبي الله كان يصلي قبل العصر ركعتين (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوۃ قبل العصرص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۳۷۲ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الا ربع قبل العصرص ۹۸ نمبر ۴۲۹) اس حدیث کی بنا پر صاحب کتاب نے فرمایا کہ عصر کی سنت دو رکعت بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے۔
Zuhr and two rak'at after it [283] (3) and four before Asr, and if he wishes two rak'at [284] (4) and two rak'at after Maghrib [285] (5) and four before Isha and after it four, and if he wishes two rak'at. The rak'at are sunnah. And in one hadith, there is a hadith of four rak'at sunnah after Zuhr. Umm Habiba said: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever preserves four rak'at before Zuhr and four after it, he will be forbidden to the Fire. (Abu Dawud, chapter of the four before Zuhr and after it, p. 187 no. 1269; Tirmidhi, chapter of the two after Zuhr, p. 98 no. 427). Based on this hadith and the previous hadith, four rak'at after Zuhr are sunnah. Therefore, the practice is that they pray two rak'at with the intention of sunnah, then two rak'at with the intention of nafl. (283) (3) Four rak'at before Asr, and if he wishes, two rak'at. From Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: May Allah have mercy on a person who prays four rak'at before Asr. (Abu Dawud, chapter of prayer before Asr, p. 187 no. 1371; Tirmidhi, chapter of the four before Asr, p. 98 no. 430). From this hadith it is known that four rak'at before Asr are sunnah. But from another hadith it appears that two rak'at are sunnah. There is a hadith from Ali that the Prophet used to pray two rak'at before Asr. (Abu Dawud, chapter of prayer before Asr, p. 187 no. 1372; Tirmidhi, chapter of the four before Asr, p. 98 no. 429). Based on this hadith, the author said: One may also pray two rak'at as the sunnah of Asr.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof on the sunnah prayers (rawatib) for Zuhr and Asr. The author states the matn: for Zuhr, two rak'at after it (i.e., after the fard), and for Asr, four before it, or if one wishes two. The commentary explains that the established sunnah for Zuhr after the fard is actually four rak'at, based on the hadith of Umm Habiba (RA) which promises protection from the Fire for those who preserve four before and four after. However, the common practice among Hanafis is to pray two rak'at with the intention of sunnah and then two rak'at with the intention of nafl, to reconcile different narrations. For Asr, the author cites two hadith: one from Ibn Umar (RA) recommending four rak'at, and another from Ali (RA) showing the Prophet prayed two. Hence, the author (sahib al-kitab) states that one may pray either two or four, but the preferred sunnah is two.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah muakkadah): An emphasized sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and advised, but is not obligatory.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer, voluntary, with less emphasis than sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many rak'at are the sunnah after Zuhr based on the hadith of Umm Habiba?
A) Two rak'at
B) Four rak'at
C) Six rak'at
D) Zero rak'at

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school reconciles conflicting hadith by combining intentions: four rak'at after Zuhr are prayed as two sunnah and two nafl, and before Asr either two or four are allowed, with two being preferred.

Sunnah Prayers for Maghrib and Isha
Rulings on sunnah rak'at for Maghrib and Isha with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for the sunnah rak'at associated with Maghrib and Isha prayers and identify the hadith evidence that supports each ruling.

Core Idea
Two rak'at after Maghrib are sunnah muakkadah; for Isha, two sunnah plus two nafl after, and four mandub before.

This lesson covers the recommended and confirmed sunnah prayers linked to Maghrib and Isha as taught by the Hanafi school. The author presents hadith evidence for each ruling, including a reconciliation of conflicting reports for the after-Isha prayer. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
For each prayer time (Maghrib and Isha), identify the specific act (rak'at before or after) and its legal classification (sunnah muakkadah or mandub).
The matn lists: after Maghrib two rak'at; before Isha four rak'at; after Isha four rak'at or if one wishes two.
2
Locate the Dalil for Maghrib After
Find the hadith evidence cited for the two rak'at after Maghrib. The author references a hadith from Muslim (no. 730) as passing evidence.
Multiple hadith support this ruling, making it strong.
3
Analyze the Evidence for Isha After
Examine the two hadith from Aisha: one indicating four or six rak'at (Abu Dawud, Bayhaqi) and another indicating two rak'at (Muslim). Understand the Hanafi reconciliation.
The school prays two sunnah then two nafl to honor both narrations.
4
Determine the Ruling for Isha Before
Assess the evidence for the four rak'at before Isha. The author notes no specific hadith but relies on the general hadith of 'prayer between the two adhans' (Bukhari). This makes them mandub, not sunnah muakkadah.
The absence of specific proof lowers the rank to mustahabb.
5
Summarize the Hanafi Practice
Combine the findings: after Maghrib, two sunnah; after Isha, two sunnah then two nafl; before Isha, four mandub. Note the practical implications.
This balanced approach maintains adherence to all authentic hadith.

۲۸۴] (۴) مغرب کے بعد دورکعتیں ہیں۔ اس کی وجہ کئی حدیث میں اوپر گزرگئی ہے (مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلته قائماص۲۵۲نمبر ۷۳۰ ) [۲۸۵] (۵) اور عشا سے پہلے چار رکعت اور اس کے بعد چار رکعت اور چاہے تو دورکعت سنت پڑھے۔ عشا کے بعد دو رکعت کی تو کئی حدیثیں گزرگئی ہیں۔ اور عشا کے بعد چار رکعت سنت پڑھنے کی حدیث یہ ہے عن عائشة قال سألتها عن صلوة رسول الله الا الله فقالت ما صلى رسول الله العشاء قط فدخل على الاصلى اربع رکعات او ست رکعات (د) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الصلوۃ بعد العشاء ص۹۲ نمبر ۱۳۰۳ رسن للبیھقی ، باب من جعل بعد العشاء اربع رکعات اوا کثرج ثانی ص ۶۷۱، نمبر ۴۵۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عشا کے بعد چار رکعت سنت ہے۔ اور ضروری نوٹ کے تحت لمبی حدیث گزری جس میں تھا کہ ويصلي بالناس العشاء و يدخل بيتي فيصلي ركعتين (ه) ( مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلة قائما و قاعد اص۲۵۲، نمبر ۷۳۰ را بو داؤد شریف ، ابواب التطوع و رکعات السنتر ص ۱۸۵، نمبر (۱۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عشا کے بعد دو رکعت سنت ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں حدیثوں کی بنا پر حنفیوں کا عمل یہ ہے کہ دورکعت سنت کی نیت سے پڑھتے ہیں اور اس کے بعد دو رکعت نفل کی نیت سے عشا کے بعد پڑھتے ہیں۔ چونکہ عشا کی پہلی چار رکعت پڑھنے کی دلیل حدیث مشہورہ میں نہیں ہے اس لئے عشا سے پہلے چار رکعت مندوب ہے۔ اور چونکہ منع نہیں فرمایا اور حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن مغفل قال قال النبي الله بين كل اذانين صلوة بين كل اذا نين صلوة ثم قال في الثالثة لـم شاء (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب بین کل اذانین صلوۃ ص ۷ ۸ باب الاذان نمبر ۶۲۷) اس اعتبار سے عشا کی اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان کچھ رکعتیں ہونی چاہئے۔ اسلئے عشا سے پہلے چار رکعت مندوب ہے مستحب ہے۔
[284] (4) After Maghrib, there are two rak'at. The reason for this has already passed in several hadith (Muslim, chapter of permissibility of nafl standing, p. 252 no. 730). [285] (5) And before Isha, four rak'at, and after it four rak'at, and if he wishes, two rak'at sunnah. Regarding two rak'at after Isha, several hadith have already passed. And the hadith for praying four rak'at sunnah after Isha is: from Aisha, she said: I asked her about the prayer of the Messenger of Allah, and she said: The Messenger of Allah never prayed Isha and then entered upon me except that he prayed four rak'at or six rak'at. (Abu Dawud, chapter of prayer after Isha, p. 92 no. 1303; Bayhaqi, chapter of those who made after Isha four rak'at or more, vol. 2, p. 671, no. 450). From this hadith it is known that four rak'at after Isha are sunnah. And under the necessary note, a long hadith passed which contained: And he would pray Isha with the people, then enter my house and pray two rak'at. (Muslim, chapter of permissibility of nafl standing and sitting, p. 252 no. 730; Abu Dawud, chapters of tatawwu' and sunnah rak'at, p. 185 no. 125). From this hadith it is known that two rak'at after Isha are sunnah. Therefore, based on both hadith, the Hanafi practice is that they pray two rak'at with the intention of sunnah, and after that two rak'at with the intention of nafl after Isha. Since there is no evidence in the famous hadith for praying four rak'at before Isha, four rak'at before Isha are mandub (recommended). And since it is not forbidden, and there is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Mughaffal that the Prophet said: Between every two adhans there is a prayer, between every two adhans there is a prayer, then on the third time he said: for the one who wishes. (Bukhari, chapter of between every two adhans there is a prayer, p. 7, chapter of adhan no. 627). Based on this, there should be some rak'at between the adhan and iqama of Isha. Therefore, four rak'at before Isha are mandub, mustahabb.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof on the sunnah prayers for Maghrib and Isha. The matn states: after Maghrib, two rak'at; before Isha four, after it four, or if one wishes two. The commentary first notes that the two rak'at after Maghrib are proven by numerous hadith, citing Muslim. Then for Isha, the author presents the evidence: a hadith from Aisha (RA) shows that the Prophet sometimes prayed four or six rak'at after Isha, establishing four as sunnah. Another hadith from the same source (Muslim) shows he prayed two rak'at. To reconcile, the Hanafi practice is to pray two rak'at with the intention of sunnah and then two rak'at with the intention of nafl. As for the four rak'at before Isha, the author notes they are not proven by a famous hadith specifically for Isha, but the general hadith of 'prayer between the two adhans' makes them mandub (recommended). Hence, four rak'at before Isha are mustahabb (preferred).

Key Terms
مندوب (mandub): Recommended act, also called mustahabb; less emphasized than sunnah muakkadah.
مستحب (mustahabb): Preferred, recommended; same as mandub in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, how should one pray after Isha?
A) Four rak'at sunnah only
B) Two rak'at sunnah only
C) Two rak'at sunnah then two rak'at nafl
D) One rak'at witr

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses multiple hadith to establish a balanced sunnah practice for Maghrib and Isha, distinguishing between confirmed sunnah and recommended acts.

Night Nawafil: Maximum 8 Rak'at with One Taslim
Ruling on maximum night nafl rak'at with one taslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum number of rak'at for night nawafil with one taslim and identify the proof from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
The Prophet prayed eight rak'at at night without sitting, setting the maximum for one taslim.

In this passage, the matn states the maximum rak'at for night nafl with one taslim, and the commentary brings the proof from the Prophet's practice as narrated by Aisha (RA). Understanding this ruling helps one follow the preferred form of night prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying night nawafil (voluntary prayers at night). The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) to pray up to eight rak'at with one taslim. Exceeding that is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked).
The ruling is about the number of rak'at with one taslim, not about the total night prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites the hadith of Aisha (RA) that the Prophet prayed thirteen rak'at at night, of which five were witr, and he did not sit except at the end. This implies the remaining eight were prayed in one continuous sequence with one taslim.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim (no. 737).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that the Prophet did not sit between the eight rak'at before witr. Since sitting for tashahhud ends a unit of prayer, not sitting indicates that all eight were joined with one taslim at the end.
This reasoning establishes the maximum as eight based on the Prophet's actual practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۶] (۶) فان صلى باللیل صلی ثمانی رکعات [۲۷] و نوافل النهار ان شاء صلى ركعتين بتسليمة واحدة وان شاء اربعا ويكره الزيادة على ذلك. [۲۸۶] (۶) اگر رات میں نفل پڑھے تو ایک سلام کے ساتھ آٹھ رکعتیں پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ ے اس لئے کہ حضور نے ایک سلام کے ساتھ آٹھ رکعتوں سے زیادہ نماز نہیں پڑھی ہے۔ اس لئے زیادہ سے زیادہ ایک سلام کے ساتھ آٹھ رکعت نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت كان رسول الله يصلى من الليل ثلاث عشرة ركعة يوتر من ذلك بخمس لا يجلس في شيء الا في آخرها (ب) ( مسلم شریف ، باب صلوة الميل وعد در كعاث النبي في الميل ص ۲۵۴ نمبر ۷۳۷ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تیرہ رکعتیں پڑھی اور پانچ رکعت وتر ہے اور صرف اخیر میں بیٹھے ہیں تو معلوم ہوا کہ آٹھ رکعت ایک سلام کے ساتھ رات میں پڑھی ہے۔ اس لئے ایک سلام کے ساتھ رات میں آٹھ رکعت پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ اس سے زیادہ کا ثبوت نہیں اس لئے ایک سلام کے ساتھ اس سے زیادہ پڑھنا اچھا نہیں ہے۔ نوٹ یہ سب اختلاف استحباب میں ہے۔ [۲۸۷] ( ۷ ) دن کے نفل چاہے تو ایک سلام کے ساتھ دو دو رکعتیں پڑھے اور چاہے تو چار پڑھے۔ اس سے زیادہ کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ ظہر اور فجر کی سنتوں کا ثبوت دو دورکعت کا ہے۔ اس لئے دو دو رکعت بھی نفل پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اور چار چار رکعت بھی ظہر اور عصر کی سنتیں ہیں۔ اس لئے چار رکعت بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے قالت ام حبيبة زوج النبی لال قال رسول الله من حافظ على اربع ركعات قبل الظهر واربع بعدها حرم على النار (ج) (ابوداود شریف، باب الا ربع قبل الظهر و بعد حاص۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۳۲۶۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دن کی سنت چار رکعتیں ہیں تو فل بھی اس کے مشابہ ہو کر چار رکعت ایک سلام کے ساتھ پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اس سے زیادہ ایک سلام کے ساتھ ثبوت نہیں ہے اس لئے مکر وہ ہوگا۔ لیکن کراہیت تنزیہی ہے۔
[286] (6) Then if he prays at night, he may pray eight rak'at [287] and the nawafil of the day: if he wishes, he may pray two rak'at with one taslim, and if he wishes, four, and exceeding that is makruh. [286] (6) If one prays nafl at night, he may pray eight rak'at with one taslim. This is because the Prophet never prayed more than eight rak'at with one taslim. Therefore, the maximum with one taslim is eight rak'at. There is proof in this hadith: from Aisha, she said: The Messenger of Allah used to pray thirteen rak'at at night, making witr of five among them, and he would not sit in any of them except at the end. (Muslim, chapter of night prayer and number of the Prophet's rak'at in night prayer, p. 254 no. 737). In this hadith, he prayed thirteen rak'at and five are witr, and he sat only at the end, so it is known that he prayed eight rak'at with one taslim at night. Therefore, it is permissible to pray eight rak'at with one taslim at night. There is no proof for more than that, so praying more than that with one taslim is not good. Note: All this is a difference in istihbab (preferability). [287] (7) Day nawafil: if he wishes, he may pray two rak'at with one taslim, and if he wishes, four. Exceeding that is makruh. The proof for the sunnah of Zuhr and Fajr is for two rak'at. Therefore, one may also pray two rak'at as nafl. And the sunnah of Zuhr and Asr are four rak'at, so one may also pray four rak'at. There is a hadith: Umm Habiba, the wife of the Prophet, said: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever preserves four rak'at before Zuhr and four after it, he will be forbidden to the Fire. (Abu Dawud, chapter of the four before Zuhr and after it, p. 187 no. 1269). From this hadith it is known that the sunnah of the day is four rak'at, so nafl can also be prayed as four rak'at with one taslim in analogy. There is no proof for more than that with one taslim, so it will be makruh. But it is makruh tanzihi.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof on the maximum number of rak'at for night and day nawafil with one taslim. The matn states: if one prays at night, he may pray eight rak'at; for day nawafil, one may pray two or four with one taslim, and exceeding that is makruh. The commentary explains: the Prophet's night prayer was thirteen rak'at total, with five witr, so eight were prayed in one taslim (the remaining eight before witr). Therefore, the maximum for night nafl with one taslim is eight. For day, the sunnah prayers (like Zuhr and Asr) are established as two or four, so nafl can follow the same pattern. The hadith of Umm Habiba (RA) shows four rak'at for sunnah, so nafl can be four. Exceeding four in one taslim is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). The note clarifies that the differences are in istihbab (preferability), not in permissibility.

Key Terms
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): Lightly disliked; avoiding it is better but not sinful.
استحباب (istihbab): Preferability; the state of being mustahabb, recommended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Two rak'at
B) Four rak'at
C) Eight rak'at
D) Thirteen rak'at

Key Takeaway
The maximum for night nafl with one taslim is eight rak'at, based on the Prophet's practice.

Day Nawafil: Maximum 4 Rak'at with One Taslim
Ruling on maximum day nafl rak'at with one taslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on day nawafil with one taslim and identify the proof from the hadith of Umm Habiba and analogy with sunnah prayers.

Core Idea
Day nafl should not exceed four rak'at with one taslim, analogous to the established sunnah prayers.

This passage continues with the ruling for day nawafil, specifying that one may pray two or four rak'at with one taslim, but exceeding four is makruh tanzihi. The proof is drawn from the hadith of Umm Habiba (RA) regarding the sunnah before Zuhr, and analogy with other sunnah prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying day nawafil (voluntary prayers during the day). The ruling is that one may pray two or four rak'at with one taslim; exceeding four is makruh tanzihi.
The ruling applies to any voluntary prayer performed during daylight hours.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites two proofs: (1) The established sunnah prayers are often two or four rak'at (e.g., Fajr sunnah is two, Zuhr sunnah is four). (2) The hadith of Umm Habiba (RA) that the Prophet said whoever preserves four rak'at before Zuhr and four after will be forbidden to the Fire.
The hadith is from Sunan Abu Dawud (no. 1269).
3
Understand the analogy
Since the sunnah prayers are legislated as two or four, and nawafil are similar voluntary acts, the same pattern is followed. There is no proof that the Prophet prayed more than four nafl in one taslim during the day, so exceeding four is not recommended.
This is an example of qiyas (analogical reasoning) from the sunnah to the nafl.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[۲۸۶] (۶) اگر رات میں نفل پڑھے تو ایک سلام کے ساتھ آٹھ رکعتیں پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ ے اس لئے کہ حضور نے ایک سلام کے ساتھ آٹھ رکعتوں سے زیادہ نماز نہیں پڑھی ہے۔ اس لئے زیادہ سے زیادہ ایک سلام کے ساتھ آٹھ رکعت نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت كان رسول الله يصلى من الليل ثلاث عشرة ركعة يوتر من ذلك بخمس لا يجلس في شيء الا في آخرها (ب) ( مسلم شریف ، باب صلوة الميل وعد در كعاث النبي في الميل ص ۲۵۴ نمبر ۷۳۷ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تیرہ رکعتیں پڑھی اور پانچ رکعت وتر ہے اور صرف اخیر میں بیٹھے ہیں تو معلوم ہوا کہ آٹھ رکعت ایک سلام کے ساتھ رات میں پڑھی ہے۔ اس لئے ایک سلام کے ساتھ رات میں آٹھ رکعت پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ اس سے زیادہ کا ثبوت نہیں اس لئے ایک سلام کے ساتھ اس سے زیادہ پڑھنا اچھا نہیں ہے۔ نوٹ یہ سب اختلاف استحباب میں ہے۔ [۲۸۷] ( ۷ ) دن کے نفل چاہے تو ایک سلام کے ساتھ دو دو رکعتیں پڑھے اور چاہے تو چار پڑھے۔ اس سے زیادہ کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ ظہر اور فجر کی سنتوں کا ثبوت دو دورکعت کا ہے۔ اس لئے دو دو رکعت بھی نفل پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اور چار چار رکعت بھی ظہر اور عصر کی سنتیں ہیں۔ اس لئے چار رکعت بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے قالت ام حبيبة زوج النبی لال قال رسول الله من حافظ على اربع ركعات قبل الظهر واربع بعدها حرم على النار (ج) (ابوداود شریف، باب الا ربع قبل الظهر و بعد حاص۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۳۲۶۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دن کی سنت چار رکعتیں ہیں تو فل بھی اس کے مشابہ ہو کر چار رکعت ایک سلام کے ساتھ پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اس سے زیادہ ایک سلام کے ساتھ ثبوت نہیں ہے اس لئے مکر وہ ہوگا۔ لیکن کراہیت تنزیہی ہے۔

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof on the maximum number of rak'at for night and day nawafil with one taslim. The matn states: if one prays at night, he may pray eight rak'at; for day nawafil, one may pray two or four with one taslim, and exceeding that is makruh. The commentary explains: the Prophet's night prayer was thirteen rak'at total, with five witr, so eight were prayed in one taslim (the remaining eight before witr). Therefore, the maximum for night nafl with one taslim is eight. For day, the sunnah prayers (like Zuhr and Asr) are established as two or four, so nafl can follow the same pattern. The hadith of Umm Habiba (RA) shows four rak'at for sunnah, so nafl can be four. Exceeding four in one taslim is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). The note clarifies that the differences are in istihbab (preferability), not in permissibility.

Key Terms
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): Lightly disliked; avoiding it is better but not sinful.
استحباب (istihbab): Preferability; the state of being mustahabb, recommended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the maximum number of rak'at for day nawafil with one taslim?
A) Two rak'at
B) Four rak'at
C) Eight rak'at
D) No limit

Key Takeaway
The maximum for day nafl with one taslim is four rak'at, established by analogy with sunnah prayers and the hadith of Umm Habiba.

Day Voluntary Prayers: Permissible Rak'ah Counts
Ruling on day voluntary prayers: permissible sets of two or four rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of rak'ahs for daytime voluntary prayers and explain the evidence and the rationale for the dislike of exceeding four.

Core Idea
For day nawafil, two or four rak'ahs per taslim are permissible; more is makruh tanzihi.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on voluntary prayers during the day (nawafil al-nahar). While some assume only two rak'ahs are allowed, the Hanafi school permits both two and four rak'ahs with one taslim, based on analogy with the sunnah prayers. The passage also explains why exceeding four is makruh tanzihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is voluntary prayers during the daytime (nawafil al-nahar). The ruling is that it is permissible to pray either two or four rak'ahs with one taslim.
The matn states this explicitly.
2
Locate the evidence
The commentary cites a hadith from Umm Habiba: 'Whoever preserves four rak'ahs before Zuhr and four after, Allah will make him forbidden to the Fire.' This hadith establishes four rak'ahs as a legitimate model.
The hadith is from Abu Dawood, no. 13269.
3
Trace the analogy
The sunnah prayers of Zuhr and Fajr are two rak'ahs, and Zuhr and Asr are four. By analogy, voluntary prayers can follow either pattern.
Thus, one may pray two or four.
4
Understand the dislike
Exceeding four rak'ahs with one taslim is not supported by evidence, so it is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked), not haram.
The prayer remains valid but is less meritorious.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school restricts all voluntary prayers to two rak'ahs per taslim, citing the general hadith 'prayer is two by two.' Hanafis apply that hadith specifically to night prayers.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

[287] (7) The voluntary prayers of the day: if he wishes, he may pray two rak'ahs with one taslim, and if he wishes, four; exceeding that is makruh. Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for day voluntary prayers (nawafil al-nahar). The matn states that one may pray either two or four rak'ahs with a single taslim; exceeding four is makruh. The Urdu commentary explains that for the sunnah prayers of Zuhr and Fajr, the proof is for two rak'ahs, so one may pray two. For the sunnah of Zuhr and Asr, the proof is for four, so one may pray four. A hadith from Umm Habiba encourages four before and after Zuhr. By analogy, other optional prayers can also be four. Since there is no evidence for more than four with one taslim during the day, exceeding it is considered makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked), not haram. The underlying principle is that the number of rak'ahs per taslim in voluntary prayers should follow the established sunnah patterns.

Key Terms
نوافل النهار (nawafil al-nahar): Voluntary prayers performed during the daytime, excluding the fixed sunnah prayers associated with the obligatory prayers.
مكروه تنزيهي (makruh tanzihi): A disliked act that is not prohibited; doing it is not sinful but contrary to the better practice.

Night Voluntary Prayers: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Rak'ahs per Taslim
Ruling on night voluntary prayers with intra-Hanafi dispute and inter-madhhab comparison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the maximum number of rak'ahs per taslim in night voluntary prayers, identify the proofs for each, and explain why the difference is one of preference (istihbab) rather than validity.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits up to eight rak'ahs with one taslim at night; Sahibayn restrict to two — both are valid, the dispute is over istihbab.

This lesson explores the Hanafi school's internal divergence on the number of rak'ahs for night voluntary prayers (nawafil al-layl). While the merit of night prayer is undisputed, Imam Abu Hanifa and his two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differed on whether one may combine up to eight rak'ahs with a single taslim or must limit to two. Understanding this ikhtilaf illuminates how Hanafis reconcile apparent hadith contradictions and prioritize evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the point of ikhtilaf
Read the source passage to determine the basic ruling on night voluntary prayers and identify the exact issue being disputed. The dispute is about the number of rak'ahs that can be performed with one taslim in night nawafil.
The ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).
2
Extract Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa's position: up to eight rak'ahs with one taslim is permissible; exceeding that is makruh tanzihi. His proof is the hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's night prayer of 13 rak'ahs (including witr) with a single sitting at the end, implying eight rak'ahs with one taslim.
The hadith from Sahih Muslim is cited in the commentary.
3
Extract the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
The Sahibayn hold that no more than two rak'ahs per taslim should be prayed at night. Their proof is the hadith 'Salat al-layl mathna mathna' recorded by al-Tirmidhi and others.
They also accept that daytime voluntary prayers may be four with one taslim because of separate evidence.
4
Understand the nature of the ikhtilaf
The text explicitly states that this difference is over 'istihbab' (preference), not over permissibility or prohibition. Both positions are valid; it is a matter of which is more meritorious.
Neither position makes the other invalid; a Hanafi may follow either view.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both night and day voluntary prayers must be two rak'ahs per taslim, relying on the version 'Salat al-layl wa al-nahar mathna mathna' and practices of the Prophet. Hanafis restrict the 'mathna mathna' command to the night, allowing exceptions for the day.
This shows how differences in usul (principles of interpretation) lead to different fiqh rulings.

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on night voluntary prayers (nawafil al-layl). The matn first states the basic ruling: if one prays at night, he may pray eight rak'ahs (with one taslim). The sharh then details an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa permits up to eight rak'ahs with one taslim, considering it makruh tanzihi to exceed that. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict it to two rak'ahs per taslim, arguing from the hadith 'Salat al-layl mathna mathna' (night prayer is two by two). The commentary notes that this disagreement is about preference (istihbab), not impermissibility. It also contrasts the Shafi'i position, which applies the two-by-two rule to both night and day. The Hanafi view relies on practice and specific reports (like the hadith of Aisha about the Prophet praying eight rak'ahs), while the Sahibayn prioritize the general command. The mufta bihi position is not explicitly stated, but the author's emphasis on Abu Hanifa's view suggests it is relied upon.

Key Terms
نوافل الليل (nawafil al-layl): Voluntary (supererogatory) prayers performed during the night, distinct from the obligatory and sunnah prayers.
تسليمة (taslima): The act of concluding the prayer by turning the head and saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah'. In this context, it marks the end of a unit of rak'ahs.
مثنى مثنى (mathna mathna): Two by two, i.e., every two rak'ahs constitute a complete prayer with its own taslim.

Salah — Prayer

Recitation in Obligatory Prayers
Ruling on recitation in fard prayers: wajib in first two rak'ahs, optional in last two

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on recitation in the first two and last two rak'ahs of fard prayers, and identify the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib.

Core Idea
Recitation is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer; optional in the last two.

This lesson covers a fundamental Hanafi ruling on recitation (qira'ah) in fard prayers. Understanding this distinction between the first and last rak'ahs is key to correct prayer performance and knowing when compensation is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
The act is recitation (qira'ah) during the standing portion of fard prayer. The Hanafi ruling: it is wajib in the first two rak'ahs and not wajib in the last two.
Wajib means omission requires sajdah al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Recognize the ikhtiyar
In the last two rak'ahs, the worshipper has a choice (ikhtiyar): recite al-Fatihah or remain silent (e.g., make dhikr). The preferred sunnah is to recite.
This contrasts with the first two rak'ahs where recitation is obligatory.
3
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools like the Shafi'i consider recitation fard in every rak'ah. The Hanafi distinction is based on the strength of evidence (zanni vs qat'i).
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Shafi'i, omitting in any rak'ah invalidates prayer; in Hanafi, only omission in first two requires compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في القرآة
[۲۹۰](١٠) والقراءة 
قرآت واجب ہے فرض کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں اور اس کو اختیار ہے دوسری دو رکعتوں میں۔ اگر چاہے تو سورۂ فاتحہ پڑھے اور اگر
Section on Recitation [290] (10) And recitation. Recitation is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of the fard (prayer), and he has a choice in the last two rak'ahs: if he wishes, he may recite Surah al-Fatihah, and if... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage begins the section on recitation (qira'ah) in prayer. It states a basic Hanafi ruling: recitation of the Quran, including Surah al-Fatihah, is wajib (obligatory) in the first two rak'ahs of every fard prayer. This means that if one omits it deliberately, the prayer is still valid but requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw or repetition depending on school). In the last two rak'ahs, the worshipper has a choice: he may recite al-Fatihah or remain silent (tashahhud or dhikr). The text cuts off but the full ruling typically includes that recitation in the last two rak'ahs is sunnah, not wajib. The Hanafi position differs from other schools that consider recitation in every rak'ah as wajib or fard. The distinction between fard and wajib is key: fard is proven by qat'i evidence, wajib by zanni evidence. Here recitation in the first two rak'ahs is wajib (not fard) because the evidence is from ahad hadith (al-Fatihah is required but not explicitly in the Quran).

Key Terms
قراءة (qira'ah): Recitation of the Quran during the standing portion of prayer. In Hanafi fiqh, it includes at least one verse but typically al-Fatihah and a surah.
اختیار (ikhtiyar): A choice; the worshipper may choose to recite or remain silent in the last two rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In all four rak'ahs.
B) Only in the first two rak'ahs.
C) Only in the last two rak'ahs.
D) In the first and last rak'ah only.

Key Takeaway
Recitation is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer; in the last two, it is optional (ikhtiyar).

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Recitation in Fard Prayer: First Two vs Last Two Rak'ahs
States Hanafi ruling on recitation in fard prayer and responds to Shafi'i objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that recitation in the last two rak'ahs of fard prayer is sunnah (not fard/wajib) and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith of Abu Qatada and companion practice.

Core Idea
In the last two rak'ahs of fard prayer, recitation is sunnah, not fard or wajib.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding recitation in the last two rak'ahs of fard prayer. While both schools agree that recitation in the first two rak'ahs is required, they differ on the last two. The Hanafi school permits the worshipper to recite Fatiha, remain silent, or recite tasbih, based on the principle that the last two rak'ahs are subordinate to the first. We will walk through the Hanafi proofs, consider the Shafi'i objection, and understand the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: recitation (at least one verse) is fard in the first two rak'ahs, and reciting Fatiha plus a surah is wajib. In the last two, recitation is sunnah (not fard/wajib); the worshipper may recite Fatiha, remain silent, or recite tasbih.
The first two rak'ahs are the foundation (asl), the last two are subordinate (tabi).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that reciting Surat al-Fatiha is wajib (or fard according to some) in every rak'ah of fard prayer, including the last two.
Shafi'is argue each rak'ah is an independent unit of prayer.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school cites the hadith of Abu Qatada (the Prophet recited Fatiha in the last two) and the general hadith 'La salata illa bi-Fatiha al-Kitab' (no prayer without Fatiha).
They interpret the Prophet's consistent practice as wajib.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis interpret the same hadith as showing sunnah, not wajib, because the Prophet's act can be recommended. The hadith 'La salata...' means a prayer lacking Fatiha is incomplete, but does not specify each rak'ah. Companion practice (Sa'd, Ali) supports omission.
The principle of subordination (tab'iyyah) weakens the analogy to independent rak'ahs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In Hanafi fiqh, omitting Fatiha in the last two does not invalidate the prayer (though makruh if done habitually). In Shafi'i fiqh, omission invalidates the rak'ah and the prayer.
This practical difference affects every four-rak'ah fard prayer.

(۲) حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن ابی قتادة عن ابيه ان النبي علا الا الله كان يقرأ في الظهر في الاوليين بام الكتاب و سورتين وفي الركعتين الاخريين بام الكتاب ويسمعنا الآية ويطول في الركعة الأولى ما لا يطيل في الركعة الثانية وهكذا في العصر (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب قرآنی الاخر بین بفاتحۃ الکتاب ص ۱۰۷ نمبر ۷۷۶ مسلم شریف، باب القراءة في الظهر والعصر ص ۱۸۵ نمبر ۴۵۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوسری رکعتوں میں صرف سورہ فاتحہ پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ لیکن یہ ہمارے یہاں بطور سنت. کے ہے وجوب کے نہیں (۳) جابر بن سمرة قال قال : عمر لسعد لقد شكوك في كل شيء حتى الصلوة قال اما انا فامد في الاوليين واحذف في الاخريين ولا آلو ما اقتديت به من صلوة رسول الله الا الله قال صدقت ذلک الظن بک او طنی بک (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب يطول فی الاولیین و یحذف في الاخر بین ص ۱۰۶ نمبر ۷۷ مسلم شریف ، باب القراءة في التظيم والعصر ص ۱۸۶ نمبر (۴۵۳) احذف فی الاخرین کے دو ترجمے کر سکتے ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ بالکل قرآت نہیں کرتا ہوں ۔ یہ ترجمہ حنفیہ کے مطابق ہوگا کہ دوسری دورکعتوں میں قرآت نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسرا ترجمہ یہ ہے کہ مختصر قرآت کرتا ہوں یعنی سورہ فاتحہ پڑھتا ہوں۔ اس ترجمہ سے سورہ فاتحہ کا ثبوت ہوگا جو حنفیہ کے نزدیک فرض کی دوسری دور کعتوں میں سنت ہے (۴) عن عبد الله بن ابی رافع قال كان يعني عليا يقرأ في الاوليين من الظهر والعصر بام القرآن وسورة ولا يقرأ فى الاخريين (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب كيف القراءة في الصلوة ج ثانی ص ۱۰۰، نمبر ۶ ۲۶۵ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۴۶ امن کان یقول مسح في الاخر بين ولا يقر أ، ج اول ص ۱۳۲۷، نمبر ۳۷۴۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوسری دور کعتوں میں قرآت کوئی ضروری نہیں ہے۔
امام شافعی کے نزدیک دوسری دور کعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا ضروری ہے۔ (۱) ان کے نزدیک ہر رکعت مستقل نماز ہے۔ اور نماز بغیر قرآت کے نہیں ہوتی اس لئے دوسری دورکعتوں بھی سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا ضروری
حاشیه : (الف) آپ ظہر کی پہلی دورکعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ اور دو سورتیں پڑھتے اور دوسری دور کھتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ پڑھتے۔ اور کبھی کبھی ہمیں آیت سناتے ۔ اور جتنی لمبی پہلی رکعت میں کرتے اتنی لمبی دوسری رکعت میں نہیں کرتے۔ اور ایسا ہی عصر میں کرتے (ب) حضرت عمر نے حضرت سعد سے فرمایا آپ کی ہر چیز میں شکایت کی
ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ نماز میں بھی۔ حضرت سعد نے فرمایا بہر حال میں تو پہلی دو رکعتوں میں لمبی کرتا ہوں اور دوسری رکعتوں میں مختصر کرتا ہوں۔ اور حضور کی نماز کی جس طرح اقتدا کی ہے اس میں کمی نہیں کرتا ہوں۔ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا آپ نے سچ کہا۔ میرا آپ کے ساتھ یہی گمان تھا (ج) حضرت علی ظہر اور عصر کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ اور سورۃ پڑھتے تھے۔ اور دوسری دورکعتوں میں کچھ نہیں پڑھتے تھے۔
Book of Prayer. Recitation is obligatory in the first two rak'ahs, and he has a choice in the last two: if he wishes he recites al-Fatiha, and if he wishes he remains silent, or if he wishes he recites tasbih. As for the obligatory prayer that is four rak'ahs, like Dhuhr, Asr, and Isha, or three rak'ahs like Maghrib, recitation in their first two rak'ahs is fard. If he does not recite even one long verse, the prayer becomes invalid. Reciting Surat al-Fatiha and joining a surah are both wajib. The proofs have passed. (1) In principle, in the fard prayer, the first two rak'ahs are the foundation, and the second two are subordinate to them. Therefore recitation in the first two rak'ahs is fard. (2) In the hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to recite in Dhuhr in the first two rak'ahs Umm al-Kitab and two surahs, and in the last two rak'ahs Umm al-Kitab, and he would make us hear the verse, and he would lengthen the first rak'ah more than the second, and similarly in Asr.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Qira'ah fi al-Akhirayn bi-Fatiha al-Kitab, p. 107 no. 776; Muslim, Bab al-Qira'ah fi al-Dhuhr wa al-Asr, p. 185 no. 451) From this hadith it is understood that he used to recite only Surat al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs. But in our school this is as sunnah, not wajib. (3) Jabir ibn Samurah said: 'Umar said to Sa'd: They have complained about you in everything, even prayer. Sa'd said: As for me, I lengthen in the first two and shorten in the last two, and I do not fall short of what I followed of the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. Umar said: That is what we thought of you.' (Bukhari, Bab Yutawwil fi al-Awwalayn wa Yahdhif fi al-Akhirayn, p. 106 no. 77; Muslim, Bab al-Qira'ah fi al-Dhuhr wa al-Asr, p. 186 no. 453) 'Yahdhif fi al-akhirayn' can be translated in two ways. One: I do not recite at all. This translation agrees with the Hanafis that there is no recitation in the last two rak'ahs. The other translation: I recite briefly, i.e., I recite Surat al-Fatiha. This translation proves the recitation of Surat al-Fatiha, which according to the Hanafis is sunnah in the last two rak'ahs of fard. (4) From Abdullah ibn Abi Rafi': He said: 'Ali used to recite in the first two of Dhuhr and Asr Umm al-Quran and a surah, and he did not recite in the last two.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Kayfa al-Qira'ah fi al-Salat, vol. 2 p. 100 no. 6265; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 46: Man Kana Yaqulu Yusahhil fi al-Akhirayn wa la Yaqra', vol. 1 p. 1327 no. 3742) From this effect it is understood that recitation in the last two rak'ahs is not necessary. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, reciting Surat al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs is necessary. (1) In his view, every rak'ah is an independent prayer, and prayer is not valid without recitation, so reciting Surat al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs is necessary. (2) The hadith of Bukhari previously mentioned, in which the Prophet used to recite Surat al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs, indicates that reciting Surat al-Fatiha is wajib. (3) The hadith 'La salata illa bi-Fatiha al-Kitab' (Bukhari no. 756, Muslim no. 394) also makes reciting Fatiha necessary.
Footnotes: (a) He used to recite in Dhuhr in the first two rak'ahs Surat al-Fatiha and two surahs, and in the last two rak'ahs Surat al-Fatiha, and occasionally he would make us hear the verse, and he would lengthen the first rak'ah more than the second, and similarly in Asr. (b) Umar said to Sa'd: They have complained about you in everything, even prayer. Sa'd said: In any case, I lengthen in the first two rak'ahs and shorten in the last two, and I do not fall short of what I followed of the Prophet's prayer. Umar said: You have spoken the truth; that is what I thought of you. (c) Ali used to recite in the first two of Dhuhr and Asr Surat al-Fatiha and a surah, and in the last two rak'ahs he recited nothing.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding recitation in the last two rak'ahs of fard prayer. The Hanafi position is presented first: recitation (at least one verse) is fard in the first two rak'ahs, and reciting Surat al-Fatiha and an additional surah is wajib there. In the last two rak'ahs, the worshipper has a choice: he may recite al-Fatiha, remain silent, or recite tasbih. This is because the first two rak'ahs are the foundation, and the last two are subordinate. The author then provides four proofs: (1) a hadith from Abu Qatada showing the Prophet recited only al-Fatiha in the last two, which Hanafis interpret as sunnah, not wajib; (2) the story of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, where 'yahdhif' is interpreted as either no recitation or brief recitation—both support the Hanafi flexibility; (3) the practice of Ali who did not recite in the last two; (4) the hadith 'La salata illa bi-Fatiha al-Kitab' is understood by Hanafis to apply only when one recites, not as an absolute requirement for every rak'ah. Then the Shafi'i position is stated: they consider every rak'ah independent, requiring Fatiha, and cite the same hadith as proof of wajib. The Hanafi response is implicit: the Prophet's practice of reciting Fatiha in the last two does not prove obligation, as it can be sunnah; the hadith 'La salata...' is interpreted to mean no prayer is complete without Fatiha, but it does not specify which rak'ah. The passage ends with the Shafi'i arguments, but the Hanafi position is already established from the earlier proofs.

Key Terms
فاتحة الكتاب (Fatihah al-Kitab): The opening chapter of the Quran, also called Umm al-Kitab.
سورة (Surah): A chapter of the Quran; here meaning an additional surah after Fatiha.
الاوليان (al-awwalān): The first two rak'ahs of a prayer.
الاخريان (al-ākharān): The last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer.
فرض (farḍ): A legal obligation proven by a decisive evidence; omission invalidates the act.
واجب (wājib): A legal obligation proven by speculative evidence; omission does not invalidate but requires compensation.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed; omission is not sinful but is discouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting Surat al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer?
A) Fard (obligatory, omission invalidates prayer)
B) Wajib (obligatory, omission requires sajdah sahw)
C) Sunnah (recommended, one may also remain silent or recite tasbih)
D) Haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, recitation in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer is fard (Fatiha + surah wajib), while in the last two it is sunnah, permissible to omit.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Recitation Wajib in All Rak'ahs of Nafl and Witr
Explains that recitation is obligatory in every rak'ah of optional and witr prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on recitation in nafl and witr prayers and explain the evidence from hadith that supports this Hanafi position.

Core Idea
In nafl and witr, every rak'ah requires recitation because each pair is an independent prayer.

In this passage, the author establishes that recitation of Fatiha and a surah is wajib (obligatory) in every rak'ah of both nafl (voluntary) and witr prayers. The reasoning is rooted in the structure of nafl prayer, where each two rak'ahs form an independent unit (shaf'), and each unit demands its own recitation. The proof comes from two key hadith: the general principle that prayer is 'two by two' and the specific practice of the Prophet in witr. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate this position and support it with evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled? The act is recitation (qira'ah) in prayers. The ruling is that it is wajib in every rak'ah of nafl and witr.
Note that 'wajib' in Hanafi terminology means obligatory, but not at the level of fard; omission requires compensation (sajdah sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer if done unintentionally.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'Salat al-layl wa al-nahar mathna mathna' (prayer of night and day is two by two). This is a general principle that applies to all non-obligatory prayers.
This hadith is found in Abu Dawud and other collections; it is a 'zanni' transmission but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'mathna mathna' means that each pair (shaf') of rak'ahs constitutes an independent prayer. Therefore, each shaf' requires its own recitation, meaning recitation is wajib in both rak'ahs of every pair.
This reasoning inherently applies to nafl prayer. For witr, which is partly nafl, the same rule applies.
4
Note the specific evidence for witr
The hadith of Aisha describes the Prophet reciting specific surahs in all three rak'ahs of witr, including the third. This explicitly demonstrates that recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of witr.
This hadith is used as direct proof, and then an analogy (qiyas awla) extends to nafl: if recitation is wajib in the third rak'ah of witr, it is even more so in all rak'ahs of regular nafl.

Source Text

[۲۹۱] (۱۱) والقراءة واجبة في جميع ركعات النفل و في جميع الوتر
نقل کی ہر دورکعت ایک شفعہ ہے اور شفعہ مستقل نماز ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ چار رکعت کی نیت باندھی تو دورکعت ہی لازم ہوگی ۔ چار رکعت لازم نہیں ہوگی۔ ہر دور کعت الگ الگ شفعہ ہے اس کا اشارہ حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر عن النبي الله قال صلوة الليل والنهار مثنی مثنی (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی صلوۃ النھار ص ۱۹۰ نمبر ۱۲۹۵) اس لئے ہر شفعہ میں قرآت کرنالازم ہے۔ اور ہر شفعہ کی ہر رکعت میں قرآت کرنا ضروری ہے (۲) وتر بھی من وجہ نفل ہے اس لئے اس کی تیسری رکعت میں قرآت کرے گا۔ احتیاط کا بھی تقاضا یہی ہے(۳) وتر کی تیسری رکعت میں قرآت کرنے کا ثبوت حدیث میں ہے سألت عائشة باي شيء كان يوتر رسول الله؟ قالت كان يقرأ في الاولى بسبح اسم ربک الاعلى و في الثانية بقل يا أيها الكافرون وفى الثالثة بقل هوا الله احد والمعوذتين (الف) ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء ما يقرآنی الوترص ۱۰۶ نمبر ۴۶۳ را بو داؤد شریف، باب ما یقرآنی الوترص ۲۰۸ نمبر ۱۴۲۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وتر کی تیسری رکعت میں قل ھو اللہ احد پڑھی۔ جس سے ثابت ہوتا ہے وتر کی تیسری رکعت میں سورۃ ملانا واجب ہے۔ اور جب وتر کی تیسری رکعت میں قرآت کی جائے گی تو نفل کی تیسری رکعت میں بدرجہ اولی قرآت کی جائے گی۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عائشہ سے میں نے پوچھا کہ حضور کن کن سورتوں سے وتر پڑھتے تھے۔ حضرت عائشہ نے فرمایا پہلی رکعت میں سے اسم اور دوسری رکعت میں قل یاں کھا الکافرون اور تیسری رکعت میں قل ھو اللہ احد اور قل اعوذ برب الناس اور قل اعوذ برب الفلق پڑھا کرتے تھے
[291] (11) And recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs of nafl and in all of witr. Explanation: Every two rak'ahs of nafl are one shaf' (pair), and each shaf' is an independent prayer. This is the reason that if one intends four rak'ahs, only two rak'ahs become obligatory; four rak'ahs do not become obligatory. Each pair of rak'ahs is a separate shaf'. An indication of this is in the hadith from Ibn Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'The prayer of the night and day is two by two.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Salat al-Nahar, p. 190 no. 1295) Therefore, recitation is necessary in every shaf', and recitation in every rak'ah of every shaf' is necessary. (2) Witr is also in some aspects nafl, so in its third rak'ah he will recite. Caution also demands this. (3) Proof of recitation in the third rak'ah of witr is in the hadith: 'I asked Aisha: With what surahs did the Messenger of Allah perform witr? She said: He used to recite in the first rak'ah 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la', in the second 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun', and in the third 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad' and al-Mu'awwidhatayn.' (Tirmidhi, Bab Ma Ja'a ma Yaqra'u fi al-Witr, p. 106 no. 463; Abu Dawud, Bab Ma Yaqra'u fi al-Witr, p. 208 no. 1423) This hadith shows that he recited 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad' in the third rak'ah of witr, which proves that joining a surah in the third rak'ah of witr is wajib. And since recitation is done in the third rak'ah of witr, then in the third rak'ah of nafl it is done with higher priority.
Footnote (a): I asked Aisha: With which surahs did the Prophet perform witr? She said: In the first rak'ah he recited 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la', in the second 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun', and in the third 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad' and 'Qul a'udhu bi-rabbi al-nas' and 'Qul a'udhu bi-rabbi al-falaq'.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof stating that recitation (at least Fatiha and a surah) is wajib in every rak'ah of nafl (optional) and witr prayers. The author explains the reasoning: each pair of rak'ahs (shaf') in nafl is an independent prayer. This is supported by the hadith 'Salat al-layl wa al-nahar mathna mathna' (prayer of night and day is two-by-two). Therefore, since each shaf' is independent, recitation is required in every rak'ah of that shaf'. For witr, it is considered partly nafl, so the same rule applies. Additionally, a specific hadith from Aisha describes the Prophet's recitation in witr, showing he recited surahs in all three rak'ahs, including the third. This proves that recitation (particularly joining a surah after Fatiha) is wajib in every rak'ah of witr. The author then concludes that if it is wajib in witr, it is even more so in regular nafl (by analogy of first priority). Thus, the Hanafi position is clear: in all rak'ahs of nafl and witr, recitation is wajib, and omitting it would require compensation (sajdah sahw) or invalidate the prayer if done intentionally without valid reason.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary or supererogatory prayer, also called tatawwu'.
وتر (witr): An odd-numbered prayer (usually three rak'ahs) performed after Isha, considered wajib according to Hanafis.
شفعة (shaf'ah): A pair of rak'ahs; the basic unit of nafl prayer.
مثنى (mathnā): Two by two; referring to the manner of performing nafl prayer in pairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafis, what is the ruling on recitation in the third rak'ah of witr?
A) Recitation is not required; one may remain silent
B) Recitation is sunnah but not wajib
C) Recitation is wajib (at least Fatiha and a surah)
D) Recitation is fard and omitting it invalidates witr

Key Takeaway
Recitation of Fatiha and a surah is wajib in every rak'ah of nafl and witr, supported by the hadith 'mathna mathna' and the Prophet's practice in witr.

Qada of Invalidated Nafl Prayer
Ruling with proof that qada of nafl is wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada of invalidated nafl prayer and explain the proof from Quranic verses and the analogy to vows.

Core Idea
Starting a nafl prayer makes it like a vow; breaking it requires qada.

In this passage, the author presents a key Hanafi principle: a voluntary (nafl) prayer, once initiated with the takbir al-tahrimah, becomes binding like a vow (nazr). Therefore, if one invalidates it, he must make it up (qada). This ruling is supported by two Quranic verses. Let's examine the reasoning and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is 'starting a nafl prayer and then invalidating it'. The ruling is that one must make it up (qada). The legal category is wajib.
The ruling applies only after the takbir al-tahrimah has been said.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two Quranic verses: (1) Surah al-Hajj 22:29, commanding the fulfillment of vows, and (2) Surah Muhammad 47:33, prohibiting the nullification of good deeds.
The first verse is the main proof; the second reinforces the idea that once a good deed is started, it should not be nullified.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do these verses support the ruling? The first verse commands fulfilling vows; a started nafl prayer is analogized to a vow. The second verse prohibits nullifying deeds; breaking the prayer is considered nullification, so one must compensate by doing the prayer again (qada).
The analogy to a vow (nazr) is crucial: just as a person who vows to pray an extra prayer must fulfill it, a person who starts a nafl prayer has effectively 'vowed' to complete it.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may not require qada for nafl because they view it as purely voluntary. The Hanafi position is based on the notion that commencement creates a binding commitment.
The difference arises from how each school interprets the intention and the effect of the opening takbir.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if someone starts a two-rak'ah nafl prayer and then speaks deliberately, they must later pray two rak'ahs as qada. If they started four rak'ahs, only two rak'ahs are wajib because the binding is per shaf' (unit of two rak'ahs).
The qada prayer is also nafl, but it is wajib to perform it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۲] (۱۲) ومن دخل في صلوة النفل ثم افسدها قضاها
ر اگر کسی نے نفل کی نیت باندھی اور تحریمہ کے بعد اس کو توڑ دیا تو دورکعت کی قضا لازم ہوگی۔ نفل جب تک شروع نہ کرے وہ نفل ہے، تبرع ہے۔ لیکن شروع کرنے کے بعد وہ ایک قسم کی عملا نذر کی طرح ہو جاتی ہے اور نذر کو پوری کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اس لئے نفل شروع کرنے کے بعد توڑ دے تو اس کو قضا کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ نذر پوری کرنے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ثم ليقضوا تفثهم وليوفوا نذورهم (ب) (آیت ۲۹ سورۃ الحج ۲۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ نذر پوری کرنا چاہئے ۔ دوسری آیت میں ہے کہ عمل کو باطل نہیں کرنا چاہئے اس لئے نفل کی جب نیت باندھ لی تو وہ ایک عمل بن گیا۔ اس لئے اس کو باطل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور تو ڑ دیا تو اس کی قضا لازم ہوگی ۔ آیت میں ہے یا ایھا الذين آمنوا اطيعوا الله واطيعوا الرسول ولا تبطلوا اعمالكم (ج) (آیت ۳۳
حاشیہ : (ب) پھر بال وغیرہ کی گندگی ختم کرنا چاہئے اور اپنی نذر کو پوری کرنا چاہئے (ج) اے ایمان والو! اللہ کی اطاعت کرو اور رسول کی اطاعت کرو اور اپنے اعمال کو باطل نہ کرو۔
[292] (12) And whoever enters into nafl prayer and then invalidates it, he must make it up. Explanation: If someone intends nafl and after the takbir al-tahrimah breaks it, then making up two rak'ahs becomes necessary. Nafl, as long as he has not started it, is nafl, a voluntary act. But after starting, it becomes practically a kind of vow, and fulfilling a vow is necessary. Therefore, if he breaks it after starting, making it up becomes wajib. The proof for fulfilling a vow is this verse: 'Then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows' (Surah al-Hajj 22:29). From this verse it is understood that one should fulfill a vow. The second verse states that one should not nullify righteous deeds. Therefore, when one has intended nafl, it becomes a deed; so it should not be nullified. And if he breaks it, making it up becomes necessary. The verse is: 'O you who have believed, obey Allah and obey the Messenger and do not invalidate your deeds' (Surah Muhammad 47:33).
Footnotes: (b) Then one should remove dirt (like hair) and fulfill one's vows. (c) O believers! Obey Allah and obey the Messenger, and do not nullify your deeds.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage gives the Hanafi ruling that if one starts a nafl prayer (by making the opening takbir) and then deliberately invalidates it (e.g., by talking, eating, or breaking wudu), it becomes wajib to make it up (qada) by performing two rak'ahs of nafl again. The reasoning is that once a nafl prayer is begun, it becomes like a vow (nazr) that one has taken upon oneself; and fulfilling a vow is wajib. The author cites two Quranic verses: first, 'Then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows' (al-Hajj 22:29), which generally commands fulfilling vows; second, 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (Muhammad 47:33), which prohibits canceling a good deed once started. Thus, the initial voluntary act becomes binding upon commencement. The ruling specifically says that if one breaks the prayer after takbir al-tahrimah, he must make up two rak'ahs (the standard minimum for nafl). This is because the nafl prayer is considered as a two-rak'ah unit (shaf'). Therefore, if one intended four rak'ahs and breaks it, only two rak'ahs become qada, not four, since the binding is per shaf'. The Hanafi position is that qada of nafl is wajib, not fard, due to the evidence being zanni.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary prayer that becomes binding upon commencement.
قضاء (qaḍā'): Making up a missed or invalidated prayer after its prescribed time.
نذر (nazr): A vow to perform an act of worship; fulfilling it is wajib.
تحریمہ (taḥrīmah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer and makes it binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafis, if someone starts a two-rak'ah nafl prayer with takbir and then deliberately speaks, what must they do?
A) Nothing, because nafl is voluntary
B) Repeat just that rak'ah
C) Make up two rak'ahs of nafl (qada)
D) Give charity as expiation

Key Takeaway
Once a nafl prayer is started with takbir al-tahrimah, it becomes wajib to complete; if invalidated, qada is wajib.
