Breaking a Nafl Prayer Requires Qada
Ruling that a nafl prayer once begun becomes a vow and must be completed or made up

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on breaking a nafl prayer after commencement, explain why qada is wajib using the analogy to nadhr, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument from Quran 9:91.

Core Idea
Once you begin a nafl prayer, it becomes a binding vow — breaking it obligates its make-up.

You may think a voluntary prayer can be abandoned at any time, but the Hanafi school teaches otherwise. This lesson explores why commencing a nafl prayer transforms it into a binding commitment, requiring qada if invalidated, and how the Shafi'i school disagrees. Understanding this dispute reveals deeper principles about the legal effect of intention (niyyah) and the obligation to fulfill one's acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: if one enters a nafl prayer and spoils it, qada of two rak'ahs is wajib.
The minimum nafl unit is two rak'ahs.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that no qada is required; the nafl remains voluntary even after commencement.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf between the schools.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i rely on Quran 9:91: 'There is no blame upon the doers of good.'
They interpret this to mean voluntary acts are not binding.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school cites Quran 22:29 (fulfill vows) and 47:33 (do not invalidate deeds), arguing that commencing the prayer creates a binding obligation like a vow.
The specific command to fulfill vows overrides the general verse.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis require make-up; Shafi'is do not.
This affects how a mufti advises a person who breaks a nafl prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲) ومن دخل في صلوة النفل ثم افسدها قضاها . اگر کسی نے نفل کی نیت باندھی اور تحریمہ کے بعد اس کو توڑ دیا تو دورکعت کی قضا لازم ہوگی۔ نفل جب تک شروع نہ کرے وہ نفل ہے، تبرع ہے۔ لیکن شروع کرنے کے بعد وہ ایک قسم کی عملا نذر کی طرح ہو جاتی ہے اور نذر کو پوری کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اس لئے نفل شروع کرنے کے بعد توڑ دے تو اس کو قضا کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ نذر پوری کرنے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ثم ليقضوا تفثهم وليوفوا نذورهم (ب) (آیت ۲۹ سورۃ الحج ۲۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ نذر پوری کرنا چاہئے ۔ دوسری آیت میں ہے کہ عمل کو باطل نہیں کرنا چاہئے اس لئے نفل کی جب نیت باندھ لی تو وہ ایک عمل بن گیا۔ اس لئے اس کو باطل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور تو ڑ دیا تو اس کی قضا لازم ہوگی ۔ آیت میں ہے یا ایھا الذين آمنوا اطيعوا الله واطيعوا الرسول ولا تبطلوا اعمالكم (ج) (آیت ۳۳ سورہ محمد ۴۷) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ اعمال کو باطل نہیں کرنا چاہئے اور باطل کر دیا تو اس کی قضا کرے۔ امام شافعی کے یہاں نفل شروع کرنے کے بعد توڑ دے تب بھی وہ نفل ہی رہتی ہے۔ اس کی قضا کرنا واجب نہیں۔ ان کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے مـا عـلـى المحسنين من سبيل والله غفور رحيم (الف) ( آیت ۹۱ سوره تو به ۹) اس آیت میں ہے کہ احسان کرنے والے اور نفل کام کرنے والے پر کوئی راستہ نہیں ہے۔ یعنی واجب نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے نفل نماز شروع کرنے کے بعد توڑ دے تو قضا واجب نہیں ہے۔
(12) And whoever enters into a nafl prayer and then spoils it, he must make it up (qada). If someone intends nafl and after the takbir tahrimah breaks it, the qada of two rak'ahs becomes obligatory. As long as one does not begin the nafl, it is nafl, a voluntary act. But after beginning, it practically becomes a kind of vow (nadhr), and fulfilling a vow is necessary. Therefore, if one breaks it after starting, making it up is wajib. The evidence for fulfilling a vow is this verse: 'Then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows.' (Surah Al-Hajj 22:29). This verse shows that a vow must be fulfilled. Another verse says do not nullify your deeds: 'O you who have believed, obey Allah and obey the Messenger and do not invalidate your deeds.' (Surah Muhammad 47:33). This verse shows that deeds should not be invalidated, and if invalidated, one must make up for it. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, if one breaks a nafl after starting, it remains nafl; making it up is not wajib. His evidence is the verse: 'There is no blame upon the doers of good.' (Surah At-Tawbah 9:91). This verse indicates that the virtuous who do nafl acts are not held accountable, so breaking it does not require qada.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author presents the Hanafi ruling that if one commences a nafl prayer and then invalidates it, he must make it up (qada). The reasoning is that beginning a nafl prayer transforms it into a binding commitment akin to a vow (nadhr), and vows are obligatory to fulfill as per Quranic verses. Additionally, the verse prohibiting the invalidation of deeds supports this. The passage contrasts with the Shafi'i position, which holds that nafl remains voluntary even after commencement, and breaking it does not necessitate qada, based on the verse exempting those who do good. The Hanafi school prioritizes the analogy to nadhr and the imperative to fulfill vows.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow; an act that becomes obligatory because one has pledged it to Allah.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or invalidated prayer; performing it after its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the evidence for qada of a broken nafl prayer?
A) Quran 9:91
B) Quran 22:29 and 47:33
C) Hadith about intention
D) Consensus

Key Takeaway
Commencing a nafl prayer transforms it into a binding commitment; if invalidated, it must be made up (qada).
